1401 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Lowman v. Stafford


Civ. No. 10699


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


226 Cal. App. 2d 31; 37 Cal. Rptr. 681; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1249



March 25, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 20, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Irving H. Perluss, Judge.

Action by one employee against a coemployee for personal injuries sustained in a collision of two company trucks.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to complaint was sustained with leave to amend and plaintiff failed to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured employee appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which dismissed his negligence cause of action against defendant co-employee for personal injuries sustained in a collision of two company trucks.


OVERVIEW: The injured employee brought an action against his co-employee and employer after being injured in a truck accident caused by the co-employee. Because the accident involved employees of the same company, the trial court dismissed the complaint as within the exclusive remedies of workers' compensation with leave for the injured employee to amend his complaint to show an exception. The injured employee did not amend his complaint, but contended that Cal. Lab. Code § 3601(a) was unconstitutional because it limited his right of action against the co-employee to injuries caused by intoxicated, willful, or reckless conduct. The court affirmed the dismissal and the validity of § 3601(a). The court determined that under Cal. Const. art. XX, § 21, the legislature had the power to enact comprehensive workers' compensation legislation. Because Cal. Lab. Code § 3601(a) did not abolish the injured employee's common law cause of action, but only restricted it to certain circumstances, and because workers' compensation bestowed other benefits on the injured employee, the court conclude that § 3601(a) did not exceed the legislature's plenary power.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that workers' compensation legislation restricting the injured employee's cause of action against the co-employee to intoxicated, willful, or reckless conduct was not unconstitutional and affirmed the dismissal of the injured employee's complaint against the co-employee.

 

1402 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Great Lakes Properties, Inc. v. Rolling Hills Estates


Civ. No. 27257


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


225 Cal. App. 2d 525; 37 Cal. Rptr. 448; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1400



March 12, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 8, 1964, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 6, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Bayard Rhone, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to prevent annexation of territory by defendants and to test the validity of a county boundary commission's refusal to accept for filing a proposal for incorporation of a new city.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that a boundary commission properly refused to accept for filing the landowners' two proposals for the incorporation of a new city under Cal. Gov't Code § 35002 and that the filings did not prohibit defendant city from proceeding with its proposed annexation of the same land.


OVERVIEW: In a dispute over the use of certain land, the landowners sought to incorporate a new city, while the city sought to annex the land. In the landowners' proceeding in mandamus to prevent the annexation and to challenge the boundary commission's refusal to accept the landowners' proposals for incorporation, the trial court found in favor of the city. The court held that Cal. Gov't Code § 35002, which provided that after a city located in a county of 4,000,000 or more people filed a petition for annexation of a territory, no other proposal for the annexation or incorporation of that territory could have been filed did not violate Cal. Const. art. IV, § 25, cl. 28, 33. The court reasoned that while Los Angeles County was the only county in the state large enough for the requirement to apply, there was a rational reason to impose additional procedural restraints for annexation in a county of that size. The court noted that the statute did not single one county out specifically. The court then held that under Cal. Gov't Code § 35002, the landowners' filing of two petitions to incorporate were of no effect because they were filed within 45 days of the city's annexation proposal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the landowners' writ of mandate.

 

1403 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Zurica


Crim. No. 8922


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


225 Cal. App. 2d 25; 37 Cal. Rptr. 118; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1339



February 19, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 10, 1964, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 15, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Adolph Alexander, Judge.

Prosecution for robbery and for kidnaping for the purpose of robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three defendants appealed their convictions by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for robbery and for kidnapping for the purpose of robbery. The charges arose from defendants robbing two cocktail bars.


OVERVIEW: Defendants went into the bars and made the customers lie down while defendants robbed the bar. One defendant was later arrested with a gun, which he denied was his. The court affirmed defendants' convictions, finding that there was ample evidence to support the verdict. Any inconsistencies in the identifications of defendants as the perpetrators by the prosecution witnesses or uncertainties of witnesses in giving their testimony were matters solely in the first instance for the jury. Here, the jury might reasonably have found that under the stress of events different victims at one of the bars perceived and retained different impressions of the participants in the crimes and of their roles, but the jury nevertheless could still have concluded that all three defendants were involved. In addition, the trial court properly omitted instructions on circumstantial evidence. It was unnecessary because the conviction of each defendant did not depend upon inferences drawn from a pattern of circumstances but rather upon the credibility to be given the testimony of eyewitnesses directly implicating each defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1404 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Mack v. State Board of Education


Civ. No. 20828


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


224 Cal. App. 2d 370; 36 Cal. Rptr. 677; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1479



January 28, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 25, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Byron Arnold, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the State Board of Education to restore plaintiffs' teaching credentials or show cause why it should not do so.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner teachers sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which dissolved their writ of mandate and denied their petition for a preemptory writ of mandate under Cal. Gov't Code § 11523 and Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1094.5 following the revocation of their teaching credentials by respondent California Board of Education. The teachers allegedly swore falsely in a loyalty oath.


OVERVIEW: Two teachers had their credentials revoked by the California Board of Education under the Levering Act, Cal. Gov't Code §§ 3100-3109, for having allegedly lied in their loyalty oath. The teachers, who at one time were members of the Communist Party, had asserted under oath that they were not members of any organization that had conspired to overthrow the United States Government. The lower court dissolved an alternative writ of mandate that it had issued to the teachers and denied their request for a preemptory writ of mandate pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 11523 and Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1094.5. The court found that the teachers were entitled to reconsideration because it found that the board had improperly taken judicial notice under Cal. Gov't Code § 11515 that the Communist Party actively sought to overthrow the government. In reaching this decision, the court noted that evidence should be required before the power of judicial notice was employed in any situation where a fact was in doubt.


OUTCOME: The court found that the husband and wife were entitled to reconsideration.

 

1405 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Osteopathic Physicians & Surgeons v. California Medical Asso.


Civ. No. 26954


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


224 Cal. App. 2d 378; 36 Cal. Rptr. 641; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1480



January 28, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 24, 1963, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 25, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Robert H. Patton, Judge.

Action to determine the validity of a merger agreement entered into by a state medical association and a state osteopathic association.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Motion to dismiss appeal as to certain causes of action denied. Judgment on pleadings for defendants as to first cause of action and dismissing other causes of action after demurrers thereto were sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an adverse judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in their suit opposing the unification of two professional associations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought suit to challenge the construction and validity of a unification and merger agreement entered into between a state medical association and a state osteopathic association. The trial court issued a declaratory judgment deeming the merger agreement legal and valid. Plaintiffs appealed, contending that defendants conspired to restrain trade and the competitive practice of medicine by eliminating the practice of those identified as osteopathic physicians and surgeons. In affirming, the appellate court concluded that the complaint failed to allege interference with any practice of any plaintiff. Under the agreement at issue, doctors of osteopathy could continue their practice under the use of the designation "doctor of osteopathy"; none were required to give up such designation nor the practice of osteopathy.


OUTCOME: Judgment in favor of defendants was affirmed, as plaintiffs' complaint failed to allege that the merger agreement had interfered with any practice of any plaintiff. Plaintiffs thus failed to demonstrate a restraint of trade and the competitive practice of medicine.

 

1406 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sunseri v. Board of Medical Examiners


Civ. No. 21111


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


224 Cal. App. 2d 309; 36 Cal. Rptr. 553; 1964 Cal. App. LEXIS 1472



January 24, 1964 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 18, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco and from an order denying a motion to amend a petition for a writ of mandate. Byron Arnold, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Board of Medical Examiners to set aside findings of unprofessional conduct made against plaintiff and to reconsider its order revoking plaintiff's license to practice medicine, stayed by a five-year period of probation.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed with directions; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment denying writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandate and challenged the trial court's order denying his motion to amend his petition for the writ. The doctor wished to compel respondent Board of Medical Examiners to set aside its findings of unprofessional conduct as defined by Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2399.5 and to reconsider its order.


OVERVIEW: The board found the doctor guilty of six counts of prescribing dangerous drugs without either a prior examination or medical indication thereof under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2399.5. On appeal, the doctor's principal contention was that the findings of the board were not supported by the evidence and hence its order and decision were invalid. Notwithstanding the limited scope of review, the court concluded that no substantial evidence supported the board's order and decision as to five counts and, as to those counts, the order was reversed. There was no direct evidence of the doctor's participation in the events charged in the first five counts. The court determined that the board's findings and order as to four counts rested on hearsay evidence only and one count was without any support in the evidence. The court held that there was substantial evidence to support the board's findings and order on the sixth court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment against the doctor. The court directed the trial court to issue its writ of mandamus. The doctor's purported appeal from the order denying his motion to amend his petition for the writ of mandate was dismissed.

 

1407 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hinkley


Crim. No. 1618


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


223 Cal. App. 2d 471; 36 Cal. Rptr. 5; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1557



December 17, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County denying motion to vacate judgment and dismiss the complaint. William P. Mahedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied a motion to vacate the conviction and to dismiss the complaint against him. Defendant was convicted for receiving stolen property under Cal. Penal Code § 496.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not timely file for a new trial or appeal the sentence of probation. However, he later challenged the conviction after the state supreme court ruled that the giving of an instruction based on the statutory presumption of § 496 was improper because the section of the statute stating that anyone receiving stolen property from a minor was presumed to know that the property was stolen was unconstitutional. Defendant contended that he could not have earlier raised the issue because the new law was not in effect. On appeal, the court disagreed. First, the statute was unconstitutional as to "receiving" stolen property, but defendant bought the property. Further, there was direct evidence that defendant knew the property was stolen. Because the time to challenge had passed, defendant's only relief was through coram nobis. Such a writ was extraordinary and was not available where defendant was challenging an irregular jury instruction. Even though defendant did not characterize his motion as one for coram nobis relief, that was the only remedy. Under any other theory, there was no jurisdiction to entertain the motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's motion.

 

1408 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Beachem


Crim. No. 1620


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


223 Cal. App. 2d 383; 35 Cal. Rptr. 673; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1543



December 16, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. James C. Toothaker, Judge.

Prosecution for assault with a deadly weapon on a peace officer.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted defendant under Cal. Penal Code § 245(b) of assault with a deadly weapon on a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated in a county jail, defendant refused to return to his cell. When two peace officers took steps to put him back in the cell, defendant, who had a razor blade in one hand and a broomstick handle in the other, resisted. One of the officers was cut from the razor blade, and defendant was prosecuted for assault with a deadly weapon on a peace officer under § 245(b). On the day of trial, defendant relieved his attorney and insisted on self-representation, and the trial judge spoke with defendant about the advisability of having an attorney and the procedures in handling a trial. Defendant admitted to prior felony convictions. On appeal from defendant's conviction, the court held that: (1) the trial judge did not abuse his discretion by accepting defendant's waiver of counsel because defendant was given considerable opportunity to have counsel, he had an attorney who represented him at all stages of the case up to the day of trial, and he was not unfamiliar with legal proceedings; and (2) § 245(b), which imposed a special punishment for an assault upon a peace officer, did not violate due process because it was not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1409 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Epstein v. California Horse Racing Board


Civ. No. 26988


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


222 Cal. App. 2d 831; 35 Cal. Rptr. 642; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1737



December 4, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 19, 1964. Traynor, J., and Peters, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Kenneth N. Chantry, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the California Horse Racing Board to set aside its decision and order determining that respondent should not be granted permission to engage in parimutuel wagering and should not be permitted access to racing enclosures within its jurisdiction.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting writ reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Horse Racing Board (board) sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent citizen a peremptory writ of mandate commanding the board to set aside its decision and order which determined that the citizen should not be granted permission to engage in pari-mutuel wagering and should not be permitted access to racing enclosures within its jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The citizen was refused admission to a park on the ground that he was among the classes prohibited from entering racing enclosures and participating in pari-mutuel betting under Cal. Penal Code § 337a. The citizen sought a hearing and four days prior, the citizen's motion to dismiss the information and stop the probation concerning his conviction was granted. The court held that it was clear that in the absence of a statute, there existed no constitutional right of access to racetracks or other places of public amusement. Even if a reviewing court reasonably could have reached a different conclusion, as the trial court apparently did, the decision of the board could be reversed only if it constituted a clear abuse of discretion. When all evidence contrary to that received in support of the board's findings was disregarded and all legitimate and reasonable inferences indulged in their support, there was no clear abuse of discretion. The court reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which had granted the citizen a peremptory writ of mandate commanding the board to grant the citizen access to racing enclosures.

 

1410 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Dave's Market, Inc. v. Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control


Civ. No. 21097


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


222 Cal. App. 2d 671; 35 Cal. Rptr. 348; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1711



November 27, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 22, 1964. McComb, J., and Peters, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Byron Arnold, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control to set aside its decision revoking plaintiff's general off-sale retail liquor license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied the licensee a peremptory writ of mandate. The licensee sought judicial review of an administrative decision of respondent Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, which ordered the revocation of the licensee's general off-sale retail liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control charged the licensee with selling alcoholic beverages at prices below the applicable fair trade prices. The court rejected the licensee's contention that the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act's fair trade provisions were unconstitutional, finding that the fair trade provisions were a valid and constitutional exercise of the police power. The admission of the duly filed fair trade contracts invoked three statutory presumptions under Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1963, subds. 15, 19, 33 that the subject alcoholic beverages were in fair and open competition. The court found that a vague offer of proof through the testimony of an importer, rectifier, and wholesaler of distilled spirits that off-brand distilled beverages were not in fair and open competition with other advertised brands was properly rejected because it did not disprove fair and open competition or negate the constitutionality of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act's fair trade provisions. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, finding that the penalty of revocation was not a clear abuse of discretion based on the licensee's deliberate and repeated course of unlawful conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1411 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bernhardt


Crim. No. 8335


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


222 Cal. App. 2d 567; 35 Cal. Rptr. 401; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1701



November 22, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 7, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying a new trial. Arthur Crum, Judge.

Prosecution against doctors of chiropractic for conspiracy to practice medicine without license, and for manslaughter.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; appeals from orders dismissed. Judgments of conviction reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, chiropractic doctors, were charged with conspiracy to violate Cal. Bus. & Prof. § 2141 and with the crime of manslaughter, Cal. Penal Code § 192. The doctors appealed from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found each doctor guilty of the crimes charged and denied the doctors' motions for new trials.


OVERVIEW: The doctors, were found guilty of conspiracy to violate Cal. Bus. & Prof. § 2141 and of the crime of manslaughter, Cal. Penal Code § 192. On appeal, the doctors asserted that the jury was erroneously instructed as to the applicable law. The court stated that the concept conveyed by the instruction given in the present case was that nothing more than ordinary negligence constituted criminal negligence sufficient to sustain a conviction under the charge of involuntary manslaughter. The court held that this concept was erroneous. Further, the court stated that for conviction of manslaughter, the state had to do more than establish mere coincidence between an act and the fact of death. It had to establish the "causal connection" between the violation and the loss of life. The court held that the trial court's failure to instruct upon the element of proximate causation constituted error. The trial court should have given such an instruction on its own motion. The court reversed the judgment of conviction as to each count with respect to each doctor.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal of each doctor from the order denying his or her motion for a new trial. However, with respect to each doctor, the court reversed the judgment of conviction as to each count.

 

1412 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Metro Realty v. County of El Dorado


Civ. No. 10632


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


222 Cal. App. 2d 508; 35 Cal. Rptr. 480; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1695



November 21, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of El Dorado County. Ralph McGee, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Actions challenging as unreasonable an order by a county board of supervisors rejecting plaintiff's tentative subdivision map and urging invalidity of two zoning ordinances.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner challenged the judgments from the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California) that found in favor of defendant county subsequent to an order by a county board of supervisors rejecting plaintiff's tentative subdivision map and upheld the validity of two zoning ordinances.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowner appealed from judgments in favor of defendant county in two actions consolidated for trial, under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 11525, challenging as unreasonable an order by the county rejecting landowner's tentative subdivision map; and the second, an action urging invalidity of two zoning ordinances. The landowner charged the ordinances were unconstitutional and invalid because they were enacted without notice to the landowner. The court affirmed the first judgment because it found the action of the board of supervisors in rejecting the map was proper even if its assigned reason, conflict with the zoning ordinance, was open to challenge. The court did not pass upon the first ordinance because its status was moot. The court noted that adoption of El Dorado County, Cal., Ordinance 482, followed a chronology of steps looking toward the formulation of a countywide water development and conservation plan. Adoption of an ordinance of limited duration and application did not exceed the county's police powers. The court held that the interim zoning ordinance was neither arbitrary nor oppressive, nor was it invalid, for want of notice given before its adoption.


OUTCOME: The judgments in favor of the county were affirmed.

 

1413 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Iscoff v. Police Com. of Francisco


Civ. No. 21108


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


222 Cal. App. 2d 395; 35 Cal. Rptr. 189; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1680



November 19, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Byron Arnold, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a city police commission and the city's board of permit appeals to approve plaintiff's application for a transfer of his pawnbroker's license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pawnbroker challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandamus compelling respondents, police commission, board of permit appeals (board), and members, to approve his application for a transfer of his pawnbroker's license.


OVERVIEW: The pawnbroker applied for a transfer of his license to a different street. The police chief denied the application, and the board upheld the decision. The pawnbroker appealed the trial court's denial of his petition for a writ of mandate directing the police commission and board and their members to approve the application. The court affirmed. The court held that the charter's overall standards guiding the police chief and board in issuing permits to pawnbroker businesses, which affected the health, crime, policing, and welfare of the city, did not offend constitutional requirements that discretionary power be restricted by specific standards. The court held that the pawnbroker erroneously argued that the denial of his application was invalid under San Francisco, Cal., Municipal Code § 1279, which was repealed by implication after the adoption of the new charter. The court held that the board gave the pawnbroker due process and exercised its sound discretion in denying the permit after considering substantial evidence, including opinions, that the proposed business would have caused a police problem and downgrading of the neighborhood.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the pawnbroker's petition for mandamus relief to direct the police commission, board, and members to approve the transfer of his license to a different street.

 

1414 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hicks


Crim. No. 4249


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


222 Cal. App. 2d 265; 35 Cal. Rptr. 149; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1657



November 14, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 7, 1964. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Gerald S. Levin, Judge.

Prosecution for unlawfully offering to sell and furnish a narcotic to a person and delivering a substance other than such narcotic.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which convicted him of offering unlawfully to sell and furnish a narcotic to a person and delivering a substance other than such narcotic in violation of Cal. Health and Safety Code § 11503.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial of offering unlawfully to sell and furnish a narcotic to a person and delivering a substance other than such narcotic in violation of § 11503. On appeal, he contended that § 11503 was unconstitutional as being vague, uncertain and arbitrary. The court affirmed his conviction. The court held that there was nothing unintelligible or ambiguous in the language of the act. Its language was quite clear. It stated that every person who offered to sell a narcotic and delivered a non-narcotic substance was guilty of a crime. This was true, whether at the time of the offer the offeror actually intended to deliver a narcotic or intended only to deliver a non-narcotic. The court stated that it was the delivery of a non-narcotic that completed the crime. Anyone reading the statute should have had no difficulty in understanding what it meant. In the statute there was a reasonably adequate disclosure of the legislative intent regarding the evil to be combated in language giving fair notice of practice to be avoided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of offering unlawfully to sell and furnish a narcotic to a person and delivering a substance other than such narcotic.

 

1415 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Elliott


Crim. No. 3469


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


221 Cal. App. 2d 575; 34 Cal. Rptr. 560; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2187



October 28, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Placer County. Leland J. Propp, Judge.

Prosecution for escape from a state forestry camp.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant escaped from a state forestry camp. Prior to his escape, defendant was disciplined for violating a prison rule. In that proceeding defendant was adjudged guilty and punished by a fine, loss of privileges, and solitary confinement. The Superior Court of Placer County (California) rejected defendant's double jeopardy defense and convicted him of escape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction, that his plea of double jeopardy should not have been stricken, and that he was erroneously and unconstitutionally convicted under Cal. Penal Code § 4531 because his status at the camp was similar to that of a parolee. The court affirmed. First, the court held that it was superfluous to say that the testimony supported the judgment. Second, defendant's disciplinary action for violating a prison rule was legally insufficient to support a plea of double jeopardy in defense of a charge of escape. Punishment by the prison authorities for a violation of its rules or for the enforcement of necessary discipline did not place defendant in jeopardy within the constitutional sense and it constituted no defense whatever to a charge of the character for which defendant was tried. Third, § 4531 provided specifically that escape from a prison forestry camp was a felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for escape.

 

1416 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Martin


Crim. No. 9354


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


221 Cal. App. 2d 14; 34 Cal. Rptr. 299; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2101



October 8, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of violating Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code § 52.51, wearing a mask or personal disguise in public with out a permit. Petitioner filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus, contenting that § 52.51 was void because the field had been preempted by state legislation.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that § 52.51 prohibited the wearing of a mask or other disguise in public without a permit, while Cal. Penal Code §§ 185, 650a, forbade the same act whether committed on public property or otherwise. Petitioner contended that the ordinance attempted to validate the wearing of a mask or disguise by one who had secured a municipal permit to do so, while the Penal Code contained no licensing provision and prohibited the act regardless of any local permit. The court found that a clear conflict existed between the ordinance and the Penal Code, which arose directly from the language of the enactments. The court said that the purpose of the legislature to occupy the entire field was plainly apparent. Accordingly, the court concluded that the ordinance provision was void.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of habeas corpus discharging petitioner from custody.

 

1417 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Zapata


Crim. No. 3447


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


220 Cal. App. 2d 903; 34 Cal. Rptr. 171; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2327



October 7, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 31, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 4, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Stanley W. Reckers, Judge.

Prosecution for illegal possession of heroin.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted defendant of illegal possession of heroin in a case brought by the State of California.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that Cal. Health and Safety Code § 11500 was unconstitutionally applied because of his addiction to narcotics and his possession of heroin was a product of his addiction or compulsive craving. Inherent in this contention was a distinction between an addict's possession in satisfaction of his compulsive craving and possession for other purposes. The court held that by imprisoning defendant for possession, the state was penalizing his act, not his craving. There was no evidence that he was under the influence of narcotics at the time of his arrest, that he was unconscious, or that he was not fully aware of his surroundings and his actions. Even on the assumption that the condition of a compulsive addict might under some circumstances render the person incapable of crime, there was no evidence of such a condition here. The court found no illegality in defendant's arrest or in the officers' actions, which culminated in the exposure of contraband. Further, the probation report amply supported the trial judge's decision that defendant was not a fit subject for a rehabilitation facility and there was no reason to disturb that decision. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of defendant's conviction of illegal possession of heroin.

 

1418 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Widener


Crim. No. 8453


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


220 Cal. App. 2d 826; 34 Cal. Rptr. 130; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2318



October 2, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment (order granting probation) of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. John A. Shidler, Judge.

Prosecution for illegal possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment (order granting probation after conviction) affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) convicted defendant of illegal possession of marijuana. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant testified at trial that he found a bottle of amphetamine tablets and two partially burned marijuana cigarettes in the closet of his bedroom following a Halloween party at his home. Defendant contended that he brought the drugs with him in his automobile so as to remove them from his house and dispose of them. Defendant did not object to the introduction of the marijuana cigarettes in evidence and did not contend that the police did not have probable cause to interrogate defendant, arrest him, or make the search his vehicle, which produced the marijuana cigarettes. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction. The court rejected defendant's contention, finding substantial evidence to support the jury's guilty verdict. The court also rejected defendant's claim that trial counsel was ineffective. The court found that defendant was given a vigorous defense. Finally, the court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530. The court found that the statute unambiguously forbade conscious and voluntary possession of narcotics.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for illegal possession of marijuana.

 

1419 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Buese


Crim. No. 3479


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


220 Cal. App. 2d 802; 34 Cal. Rptr. 102; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2314



October 1, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 27, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Siskiyou County dismissing an information. J. Everett Barr, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Siskiyou County (California) dismissed an information charging defendant with bringing a drug into the county jail without authority to do so, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 4573.5. The People appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant brought pills into the county jail concealed under her armpit. The pills were tablets that contained phenobarbital and methamphetamine. They were classified as a hypnotic and could not be obtained without a prescription. The trial court dismissed the information charging defendant on the ground that the statute was so vague that one had to guess at its meaning. The court reversed the dismissal, holding that the trial judge erred in finding the statute unconstitutional. Defendant could not attack a statute on grounds that were not applicable to her. The court could not consider the question of constitutionality with reference to hypothetical situations. The substance carried by defendant was a hypnotic drug. The court determined that it was within the types of drugs that the legislature intended to be included in the prohibition of the statute. The legislature was not required to specify each category of drugs within the statute. The court further found that, if the People were required to show that the drug was brought into the jail without authorization for purposes of the motion to set aside the information, only slight proof satisfied the requirement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the information.

 

1420 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Randazzo


Crim. No. 9259


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


220 Cal. App. 2d 768; 34 Cal. Rptr. 65; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2309



September 30, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 28, 1963, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 27, 1963. Peters, J., and Tobriner, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County and from an order granting a new trial. Newell Barrett, Judge.

Prosecution for theft.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of dismissal reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the decision of the Appellate Department of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that affirmed the grant of a new trial and subsequent dismissal on Fourth Amendment grounds of theft charges against defendant. The appellate court certified the case to resolve the issue of whether constitutional protections against unreasonable search and seizure applied to unreasonable searches by private persons.


OVERVIEW: A store detective looked under a dressing room partition to watch defendant in the next enclosure, observed her roll up a blouse, and put it in her purse. The detective had no particular reason to suspect defendant and had made many similar arrests. The trial court granted a new trial on the ground that the evidence was illegally obtained and later dismissed the charges due to suppression of the evidence. The court held that the evidence was admissible. The court adhered to the rule that evidence obtained in an unreasonable search and seizure by a private citizen and subsequently delivered to prosecuting authorities was admissible. The court noted that the evidence would not be admissible if acquired by government officers in the same manner. The court also emphasized that the Fourth Amendment restricted only governmental agencies and that the Fourteenth Amendment prohibited only "state action," and the court declined to extend the protections afforded by either constitutional provision to private acts. The retailer did not violate any law when it undertook to protect its legitimate business against thievery, and its interests necessarily outweighed a shoplifter's asserted rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed the theft charges against defendant and the order that granted defendant a new trial.

 

1421 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


McIvor v. Savage


Civ. No. 7125


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


220 Cal. App. 2d 128; 33 Cal. Rptr. 740; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2235



September 12, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Robert P. Kneeland, Judge.

Action for personal injuries sustained in an automobile accident.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Summary judgment for defendants reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee brought an action against appellee coemployees for personal injuries she sustained as a passenger in an accident involving their vehicles in the employer's parking lot. The Superior Court of Orange County (California) granted the coemployees' motions for summary judgment because the injuries were compensable under the Workmen's Compensation Act, Cal. Lab. Code § 3201 et seq., and the employee sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed, holding that Cal. Lab. Code § 3601 did not foreclose the action by the employee against the coemployees for injuries sustained by the employee as a result of the negligent conduct of the coemployees merely because the injuries sustained were compensable under the Workmen's Compensation Act. The court held that the fact that such injury arose out of and in the course of employment did not establish per se that the coemployees who inflicted that injury were acting within the scope of their employment. The phrase "scope of his employment" as used in Cal. Lab. Code § 3601 to describe the nature of the act of the coemployee whose conduct caused such injury was not synonymous with the phrase "arising out of and in the course of the employment" as used in Cal. Lab. Code § 3600 to describe a compensable injury. Because the coemployees had not alleged uncontradicted facts establishing as a matter of law that they were acting within the scope of their employment in driving their automobiles off of the employer's parking lot at the time of the accident, a triable issue of fact existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment for the coemployees.

 

1422 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Don Wilson Builders v. Superior Court of Los Angeles County


Civ. No. 27491


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


220 Cal. App. 2d 77; 33 Cal. Rptr. 621; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2230



September 11, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 7, 1963, and Petitioners' Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 6, 1963. McComb, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Los Angeles County from proceeding further in an action to enjoin alleged discrimination in housing in violation of the Unruh Civil Rights Act.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ discharged and peremptory writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, builders, owners, subdividers, sellers, and promoters of a housing tract, brought this proceeding in prohibition to restrain respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) from proceeding further in an action brought by the Attorney General. The action sought to enjoin petitioners from discriminating in housing based upon race in violation of the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code §§ 51-52.


OVERVIEW: The Attorney General brought suit against petitioners, builders, owners, subdividers, sellers, and promoters of a housing tract, seeking to enjoin them from violating the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code §§ 51-52, by selling houses in a manner that unlawfully denied the full and equal accommodations, advantages, facilities, privileges, and services of their business establishment on the grounds of race or color. The complaint alleged that petitioners refused to sell or offer to sell any of the houses to African-Americans. After respondent district court granted the preliminary injunction sought by the Attorney General, petitioners filed this action seeking a writ of prohibition. The issue was whether the Attorney General, on behalf of the State of California, had authority to maintain a civil action to restrain petitioners' business activities. The court held that the Attorney General had broad common law authority to do so in the absence of legislative restriction, analogizing to California Supreme Court cases holding that the Attorney General could enforce statutes enacted to safeguard the public such as the Unfair Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 17000-17101.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for a writ of prohibition sought by petitioners, builders, owners, subdividers, sellers, and promoters of a housing tract. The court also discharged the alternative writ of prohibition. In view of other California Supreme Court cases involving situations substantially analogous to the present case, the court sustained the contention of the Attorney General relative to maintaining the action against petitioners.

Sinclair v. Baker


Civ. No. 26840


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


219 Cal. App. 2d 817; 33 Cal. Rptr. 522; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2442



September 6, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 3, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 23, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying motions for a new trial, to vacate judgment, to retax costs, and to vacate order denying retaxation of costs. Kenneth N. Chantry and Philbrick McCoy, Judges.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the State Personnel Board to set aside its decision denying plaintiff's appeal of his performance report rating, to establish fair working standards, and to grant plaintiff a pay raise.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order denying motion to vacate judgment affirmed; orders denying motions to retax costs and to vacate order denying retaxation of costs, modified and affirmed; appeal from order denying a new trial dismissed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denied petitioner employee's petition for a writ of mandate requesting reversal of respondent state personnel board's denial of the employee's appeal of his annual performance report and his related motions. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee received an annual performance report of "short of standard" in his special investigator position for the state. He appealed the report to the director of his department and to the state personnel board (board), which appointed a hearing officer to hear the case. The hearing officer's denial of the employee's appeal was adopted by the board without its consideration of the evidence or arguments. The employee then filed a petition for a writ of mandate in the trial court requesting reversal of the board's decision. The petition was denied and the employee appealed from the denial of his petition, his motion for a new trial, his motion to vacate judgment, and his motion to vacate the order denying retaxation of the board's bill of costs. The court dismissed the appeal from the denial of the motion for a new trial because it was a non-appealable order. The court modified the denial of the motion to retax costs, finding that the employee should only have been charged $ 7.50 instead of $ 12.50 for filing fees. Otherwise, the court affirmed all judgments, finding that they were supported by substantial evidence and that the employee was not denied procedural due process.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the employee's appeal from the order denying his motion for a new trial, reduced the orders on the motions to vacate costs from $ 12.50 for clerk's fees to $ 7.50, and affirmed the judgment against the employee and the denial of his motion to vacate the judgment.

People v. Perez


Crim. No. 4258


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


219 Cal. App. 2d 760; 33 Cal. Rptr. 398; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2434



September 5, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 23, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco dismissing an indictment. Francis McCarty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which dismissed an indictment in which defendant was charged with unlawful possession of heroin and marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and searched when he entered an apartment in which the police were arresting everyone. The police found three marijuana cigarettes on defendant, a bottle of narcotics under the driver's seat of his vehicle that was parked across the street, and heroin and drug paraphernalia in a locker that was located at a bus terminal. The trial court granted the dismissal on the ground that the only evidence had been seized illegally. The People argued that defendant was lawfully arrested for visiting a place where defendant knew that narcotics were being smoked or used in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11556. On appeal, the court found that the warrantless search of the locker, which was distant from the place of arrest and contemporaneous with defendant's arrest, was not a search incident to defendant's arrest. Additionally, defendant did not visit a place where narcotics were being used because narcotics were not being used when he arrived at the apartment. Section 11556 referred to actions taking place inside the apartment, not to a standing condition of the apartment. Thus, the arrest was unlawful, and the subsequent searches were also unlawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

McMahan's Furniture Co. v. Pacific Grove


Civ. No. 20627


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


219 Cal. App. 2d 732; 33 Cal. Rptr. 476; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2430



September 4, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Monterey County. Elmer Machado, Judge pro tem. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to enjoin enforcement of portions of an ordinance prohibiting the erection and maintenance of signs.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting injunction, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed an order of the Superior Court of Monterey County (California), which permanently enjoined enforcement of portions of an ordinance prohibiting the erection and maintenance of certain signs used by plaintiff merchants.


OVERVIEW: The merchants filed an action against the city to enjoin the enforcement of portions of an ordinance that prohibited the erection and maintenance of signs used by the merchants at their places of business. The trial court granted the merchants a permanent injunction, and on appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the trial court erred in determining that the ordinance was arbitrary, unreasonable, and discriminatory in classifying as permissible signs which did not project more than 14 and 24 inches, and prohibiting signs of greater overhang. The court found that the city acted in a field clearly within its police power, and fixed projection limits that it deemed reasonable. The court held that the merchants failed to prove their burden of showing that the classification was unreasonable, in light of the presumption favoring the city's determination, the lack of evidence of engineering or planning experts, and in their reliance upon the lay opinions of other owners of signs violating the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that granted the merchants a permanent injunction enjoining the city from enforcing the ordinance, in favor of the city.

Luckenbach S.S. Co. v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 10519


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


219 Cal. App. 2d 710; 33 Cal. Rptr. 544; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2428



September 3, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 23, 1963. Traynor J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Fred R. Pierce, Judge.

Action to recover corporate income tax paid to the state under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff foreign taxpayer sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), in favor of defendant franchise tax board, in the foreign taxpayer's suit to recover corporate income tax paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The foreign taxpayer sought review of a judgment in favor of the franchise tax board in a suit to recover corporate income taxes paid under protest. The foreign taxpayer contended that the franchise tax board's application of its apportionment formula to determine taxes attributable to the foreign taxpayer's in-state activity was erroneous. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that the franchise tax board's apportionment formula did not impermissibly derive from extraterritorial sources. The court noted that there was nothing unconstitutional about the fact that an apportionment formula necessarily took into account income which was earned outside it borders. The court explained that in order for an apportionment formula to be valid, it was required to be based upon one or a combination of logically relevant factors. The court found that the franchise tax board's port day formula reasonably proportioned the forum state's contributed values by acknowledging the productive value supplied to the entire voyage of a vessel. The court explained that such a formula was consistent with due process and not violative of the Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the franchise tax board in the foreign taxpayer's suit for recovery of corporate income taxes paid.

 

1427 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Pacific Employers Ins. Co. v. Industrial Acci. Com.


Civ. No. 10634


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


219 Cal. App. 2d 634; 33 Cal. Rptr. 442; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2418



August 29, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioners' Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 23, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING to review an order of the Industrial Accident Commission awarding compensation for a disability caused by an occupational disease.



DISPOSITION: Award affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurer sought review of an order of respondent Industrial Accident Commission (commission), which awarded compensation to an employee for a disability caused by an occupational disease.


OVERVIEW: The employee was awarded compensation for his silicosis occupational injury. The insurer argued that the award required it to bear the burden of the entire compensation payable to the employee, even though the insured was only the last of series of employers. On appeal, the court affirmed the award. The court held that Cal. Lab. Code § 5500.5's provision providing that any selected employer or employers contributing to the disability of the silicosis victim must bear the burden of the entire award with only the limited right of reimbursement retained and without recourse to public funds to effect complete reimbursement, was a valid exercise of police power. The court reasoned that the legislature foresaw the possibility of insolvency of an employer liable for contribution and had forestalled frustration of contribution on by requiring self-insured employers to deposit a bond or securities in an amount fixed by the Director of Industrial Relations. Thus, the court concluded that the problem of reimbursement was narrowed and left inaccessible only insolvent insurers and employers beyond the jurisdiction of the commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the compensation award to the employee.

Doyle v. Board of Barber Examiners


Civ. No. 10569


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


219 Cal. App. 2d 504; 33 Cal. Rptr. 349; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2400



August 21, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Stanley W. Reckers, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Board of Barber Examiners to annul the suspension of plaintiff's certificates as a registered barber and as operator of a barbershop.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner barber sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) that denied the barber a writ of mandate to annul his suspension by respondent, California Board of Barber Examiners, based on the barber having hired more than two apprentices in his shop in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6550.


OVERVIEW: The barber claimed that § 6550 was a violation of due process by restricting him from hiring more than two apprentices in his shop and § 6550 should have been construed to allow one apprentice per registered barber in the shop. The board claimed that § 6550 imposes a ceiling of one apprentice per barbershop-owner, regardless of the number of registered journeymen employed in the shop. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the barber a writ of mandate to prevent the board from suspending him and held that § 6550 was clear and it did not allow three apprentices in the barber's shop and § 6550 was a proper function of the police power of the state to regulate the public health interest in maintaining controls over barber shops. The court further held that the public health interest in regulating the barber shops and the licensing of barbers had a rational basis and § 6550 did not violate the due process clauses of the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the barber a writ of mandate to set aside the board's decision to suspend the barber.

Stoumen v. Munro


Civ. No. 20310


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


219 Cal. App. 2d 302; 33 Cal. Rptr. 305; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2375



August 14, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 11, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 9, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County. Richard M. Sims, Jr., Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control to set aside its decision revoking an on-sale general liquor license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar owner sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which denied the bar owner's writ of mandamus to compel respondent Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control (ABC) to set aside its decision revoking the bar owner's on-sale general liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The ABC charged the bar owner with violations on two counts: Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 25601 for keeping a disorderly house (Count I) and § 24200(e), a resort for sexual perverts (Count II). A hearing officer determined that the allegations were true and recommended revocation of his liquor license, which the ABC director adopted. The ABC Appeals Board affirmed the decision. The bar owner sought a writ of mandamus from the superior court to set aside the ABC's decision. The superior court affirmed the decision as to Count I and reversed as to Count II because § 24200(e) was previously declared unconstitutional. The bar owner appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed, ruling that there was substantial evidence to support the ABC's findings that the allegations were true based upon the testimony of several undercover agents and that the pleadings adequately presented the charges to allow the bar owner to be able to prepare a defense. The court concluded that the alleged settlement agreement that the bar owner claimed to have entered into with the ABC had no effect because it was not executed by the ABC acting through its director, who had no knowledge of the alleged agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the bar owner's writ of mandamus to compel ABC to set aside its decision to revoke the bar owner's liquor license.

 

1430 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Yribarne v. County of San Bernardino


Civ. No. 7095


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


218 Cal. App. 2d 369; 32 Cal. Rptr. 847; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1788



July 17, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 6, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 11, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Thomas Coakley, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to restrain a county and its board of supervisors from calling an election or acting further in response to a petition for the organization of a municipal water district; wherein interveners applied for an order determining constitutionality of the Municipal Water District Act of 1911 as amended.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed with directions. Judgment declaring act constitutional affirmed with directions for dissolution of preliminary injunction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claiming that the Municipal Water District Act of 1911 (MWDA), Cal. Water Code Ann. § 20-1 et seq., was unconstitutional, appellant taxpayer sued respondent county and its officials (county) to prevent an election sought by intervenor citizens to authorize organization of a municipal water district. Although it granted a preliminary injunction, the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California) then upheld the law. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer argued that the MWDA was unconstitutional because it permitted his property to be included in the new district without first finding that it benefited him and because it involved an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power. After granting a preliminary injunction, the trial court upheld the MWDA. On appeal, the court affirmed and ordered the injunction dissolved. It held that an earlier ruling by the California Supreme Court that the MWDA was constitutional was binding on the court and that even if there were doubts as to constitutionality, the passage of time as well as the fact that 48 municipal water districts had been organized in the interim required affirmance of the judgment of constitutionality. The court found that (1) the legislature was fully empowered by general law to establish such a district, which was quasi-municipal in nature, for the purpose of supplying general municipal needs; (2) the nature of the powers granted to those districts was a political question to be determined by the state; and (3) the constitution did not limit the legislature's power in determining what property would be included within municipal territory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court holding the MWDA constitutional and ordered the trial court to dissolve the preliminary injunction.

Cohon v. Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control


Civ. No. 20485


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


218 Cal. App. 2d 332; 32 Cal. Rptr. 723; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1783



July 16, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Edward F. O'Day, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control to set aside its decision suspending an off-sale retail liquor license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensees challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) denying the licensees a peremptory writ of mandate in a proceeding for judicial review of an administrative decision of appellee, the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control (California). The decision ordered the suspension of an off-sale retail liquor license issued by the Department.


OVERVIEW: The Department had filed an accusation against the licensees charging them with selling from their licensed premises cases of distilled spirits under certain labels at sales prices below the applicable fair trade price. A hearing officer found against the licensees and the Department adopted the officer's decision. The licensees contended that the purported fair trade contracts relied upon did not comply with the provisions of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24750 and did not constitute valid contracts, open competition was nonexistent under the law as administered by the Department, and the evidence was insufficient to support a finding of fair and open competition. The court held that: (1) Cal. Const. art. XX, § 22, granted to the Department the power to deny, suspend, or revoke alcoholic beverage licenses for good cause where the granting or continuance of such license would have been contrary to public welfare or morals; (2) Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24200(a) provided the Department similar power; (3) the Department's decision was support by substantial evidence in the record; and (4) the Department's statutory interpretations deserved great respect and were not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment rendered by the trial court.

North Sacramento v. Citizens Utilities Co.


Civ. No. 10532


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


218 Cal. App. 2d 178; 32 Cal. Rptr. 308; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1764



July 11, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 2, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 4, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County declaring the City of North Sacramento to be the owner of a water system and granting possession thereof to such city. James H. Oakley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city instituted a condemnation proceeding, under Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 1401, et seq., to acquire the water system supplying its citizens. Appellant utility company challenged an order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which declared the city to be the owner of a water system and granting possession thereof to the city.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the issue presented was whether the trial court erred in issuing its order and in putting the city into possession without exacting, as a condition precedent thereto, payment of interest on the compensation from the date of the interlocutory judgment to the date when possession was taken. The court held that it was the legislative intent that, where the public agency elects to condemn the property of a public utility under Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 1401, et seq., increases or decreases in the original award covering the period after the filing of the petition and until the condemnor takes possession shall be made exclusively by the commission under Cal. Pub. Util. Code § 1417-1419; that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1255b, providing for interest-less-benefits during this period, was inapplicable; and that California Const. art. XX, § 22 had no application to special proceedings under statutes enacted pursuant to Cal. Const. art. XII, § 23a.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order declaring the city to be the owner of a water system, granting possession thereof to the city, and denying the utility company interest on the compensation.

Case v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 26839


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


218 Cal. App. 2d 36; 32 Cal. Rptr. 271; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1747



July 8, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 4, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Robert H. Patton, Judge.

Action to have part of a municipal zoning ordinance and the granting of a conditional use thereunder declared unconstitutional and void.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Declaratory judgment for defendants on the pleadings, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted the motions of respondents, city and landowners, for a declaratory judgment on the pleadings and declared the validity and constitutionality of an approval of a conditional use. Appellants first challenged the zoning administrator's decision to approve the use before the city planning commission and then before the city council.


OVERVIEW: Following the city's conditional use request procedure, the landowners applied for permission to construct a "deluxe apartment house complex group dwelling type of housing project." A public hearing was held after which the city zoning administrator conditionally approved the application and appellants began their series of challenges to his decision. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the lower court. The court first considered the question of whether the municipal code provisions which permitted the establishment of a housing project in an R1 zone were constitutional and held that they were. Next, the court ruled that the allegations of the amended complaint with reference to the conduct of public hearings did not preclude the court from granting respondents' motions for declaratory judgment under the circumstances. The court ruled that the lower court's procedure in overruling the demurrers and then granting declaratory relief on the pleadings was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court which upheld the city zoning administrator's approval of a conditional use permit requested by the landowners.

 

1434 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Rocklite Products v. Municipal Court for Los Angeles Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 26795


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


217 Cal. App. 2d 638; 32 Cal. Rptr. 183; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1951



June 27, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 23, 1963, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 20, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Harold P. Huls, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District of Los Angeles County from taking further proceedings in a criminal prosecution.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, company and related individuals, brought an action in prohibition to restrain appellee municipal court from taking further proceedings in a criminal prosecution against them. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denied the writ and the company and individuals sought review of the decision.


OVERVIEW: The company and individuals were named as defendants in an action brought by the attorney general in the municipal court. The attorney general alleged violations of the Cartwright Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 16700 et seq. The company and individuals sought to restrain the municipal court from taking any further proceedings. They contended that the Act was unconstitutional, the municipal court lacked jurisdiction over the criminal prosecution, and the complaint failed to state a criminal offense as required. The court rejected all of these arguments and affirmed the decision that denied the issuance of a writ to prevent the prosecution of the company and the individuals. The court noted that an amendment to the Act had been repealed as unconstitutional. However, it did not render the entire Act unconstitutional because the amendment was separate from the rest of the Act such that its unconstitutional vagueness invalidated only the amendment. The municipal court had proper jurisdiction over the proceeding as per Cal. Penal Code § 1462. The complaint properly stated a criminal offense and did not need to set forth the punishment for the alleged crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the writ sought to prevent the further prosecution of the company and individuals.

* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action seeking declaratory relief with respect to the validity of a municipal zoning ordinance and an injunction restraining enforcement of the ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Judgment declaring the ordinance invalid and enjoining the enforcement thereof modified by striking the injunction portion and otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and officers, sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which found in favor of respondent real estate developers that a certain municipal zoning ordinance was unconstitutional and granted the developers' request permanently enjoining appellants from rezoning a certain area.


OVERVIEW: The developers purchased a 142 acre tract of land that was zoned R-1 for single-family dwellings. Subsequently, the developers sought rezoning and the land was rezoned. Shortly thereafter, the city entered into a contract with the state, by the terms of which the state obligated itself to assist the city in the preparation of a comprehensive general plan for physical development. A plan was constructed, a hearing was held before city council, and the ordinance was passed. The developers protested at every stage. The developers filed an action against appellants seeking to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional and seeking a permanent injunction prohibiting the city from rezoning the land. The trial court found in favor of the developers. On appeal, the court modified the trial court's judgment by disallowing the permanent injunction against the rezoning of the property. The court then affirmed the trial court's judgment, as modified, in favor of the developers, finding that there was substantial evidence to support the trial court's finding that the planning commission did not submit findings or summaries of hearings to the city council as required by Cal. Gov. Code § 65653.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment by disallowing the permanent injunction against the rezoning of the property. The court then affirmed the trial court's judgment, as modified, in favor of the developers in their action to declare a certain municipal zoning ordinance unconstitutional.

Los Angeles v. California Towel & Linen Supply Co.
