Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


217 Cal. App. 2d 410; 31 Cal. Rptr. 832; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1921



June 20, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Robert H. Patton, Judge.

Action by a city to collect delinquent municipal license taxes from a linen supply company.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment on pleadings in favor of plaintiff, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant company appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), which held in favor of plaintiff city in an action to collect delinquent municipal license taxes from the company.


OVERVIEW: The city brought an action against the company to collect delinquent municipal license taxes. The trial court held in favor of the city, and the company appealed, arguing that it did engage in business within the city. The court ruled that the company not only failed to exhaust administrative remedies available to them but it knowingly neglected to make more than an insignificant use of the orderly procedure provided for securing a correct tax assessment. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the city, concluding that where a defendant attempted to defend an action for collection of taxes upon the ground that its activities did not bring it within the purview of the tax law under which the assessment was made the rule of exhaustion of administrative remedies applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the city was affirmed.

 

1437 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Subsequent Injuries Fund v. Industrial Acci. Com.


Civ. No. 20975


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


217 Cal. App. 2d 322; 31 Cal. Rptr. 508; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1914



June 19, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING to review an order of the Industrial Accident Commission insofar as it denies to petitioner credit for social security disability payments being made to the applicant.



DISPOSITION: Order annulled; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner California Subsequent Injuries Fund sought review of an order of respondent California Industrial Accident Commission insofar as it denied the Fund a credit for social security disability payments being received by respondent injured employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured in an industrial accident, which accelerated an existing diabetic retinitis to produce blindness in his right eye. Prior to the injury, he had already suffered the complete loss of vision in his left eye. He filed for benefits from the Fund. At his hearing evidence was presented that he received federal social security disability benefits for his preexisting condition and the subsequent injury. The employee was found to be 100 percent disabled. His employer's carrier was responsible for a part of the award, and the remainder of it was issued against the Fund. The Fund received a credit under Cal. Lab. Code § 4753 for the employee's social security disability payments. The employee filed for reconsideration and the Commission vacated the Fund's credit. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that social security disability payments were not within any of the exceptions in § 4753, so the employee was not entitled to a double recovery for the same disabilities. The court held that since the social security disability payments were in part accountable to the preexisting liability for which the Fund was liable the credit had to be allowed.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the Commission's order and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1438 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Silver v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 26690


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


217 Cal. App. 2d 134; 31 Cal. Rptr. 545; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 1883



June 12, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 7, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Leon T. David, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief seeking nullification as unconstitutional of a rubbish collection ordinance and to have a contract awarded for the sale of metals collected set aside.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal with prejudice after general demurrer to third amended and supplemental complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent city's motion for demurrer in the taxpayer's action for declaratory relief seeking to nullify as unconstitutional the city's ordinance relating to rubbish collection and to set aside a contract awarded for the sale of metals collected.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer initiated an action against the city alleging that its rubbish collection ordinance was invalid, unconstitutional, and incited damage suits against the city for unconstitutional discrimination against hotels and motels. The trial court granted the city's motion for demurrer. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that under its police powers the city had full power to adopt the rubbish collection ordinance under Cal. Const. art. XI, § 6, 8, 11 and Los Angeles City Charter, § 2(4), (6), (9), (11)b and § 3(14). The court determined that the allegations that the ordinance was invalid because it was intended for the financial benefit of a private corporation and was intended solely as a revue measure were without legal effect because the motivation of the city in passing the ordinance was irrelevant to the inquiry concerning its reasonableness. The court also held that the taxpayer did not have standing to assert unconstitutional discrimination against hotels and motels because he was not within the allegedly discriminated against class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of demurrer in favor of the city, holding that the rubbish ordinance was a valid and constitutional exercise of the city's police powers.

 

1439 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Carmichael v. Carmichael


Civ. No. 10482


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


216 Cal. App. 2d 674; 31 Cal. Rptr. 514; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2070



May 28, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 26, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 24, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Yuba County. J. F. Good, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for divorce.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Interlocutory judgment granting wife a divorce and disposing of community property modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband sought review of an interlocutory divorce decree that was entered in favor of respondent wife, in her divorce action, by the Superior Court of Yuba County (California).


OVERVIEW: The husband argued that the trial court erred in granting his wife a divorce because it failed to give full faith and credit to the prior ex-parte Nevada divorce that he had obtained against his wife. He also contended that the trial court abused its discretion in its award of the community property to the respective parties and that his wife was awarded a disproportionate share of the property. In affirming the decree and the division of the property, the court held that a divorce decree was not entitled to full faith and credit where neither party had a domicile in the divorce state, and the attacking party was not served within the jurisdiction and did not appear in the action. The court found that the husband never had a domicile in Nevada when he filed for divorce in that state, and that his wife did not participate in that action. The court stated that the unequal division of property was warranted because where a divorce was granted on the ground of extreme cruelty, the nonoffending party was entitled to be awarded more than one-half of the community property. The wife was granted a divorce on the ground of extreme cruelty.


OUTCOME: The interlocutory decree that granted the wife a divorce and disposed of the community property was modified and affirmed.

 

1440 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kuhn


Crim. No. 1869


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


216 Cal. App. 2d 695; 31 Cal. Rptr. 253; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2072



May 28, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Byron F. Lindsley, Judge.

Prosecution for wilful failure to file a state income tax return with intent to evade the tax imposed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted defendant of wilful failure to file a state income tax return pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 19406.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his conviction for wilful failure to file a state income tax return. Defendant asserted that Cal. Rev. & Tax Code §§ 19406, 19401, defined the same offense, one which was a felony and one that was a misdemeanor. Defendant asserted that that constituted an infringement of his constitutional guarantee of equal protection of the law. The court affirmed. The court stated that under the rules of construction where the provisions of the statute were subject to two or more reasonable interpretations the interpretation that harmonized was to be adopted. The court stated that the phrase "regardless of intent to evade" indicated that intent was an immaterial factor in the misdemeanor offense therefore they did not define the same offense because wilful intent was a necessary element to offense in the felony statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for wilful failure to file a state income tax return.

 

1441 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Samarkand of Santa Barbara, Inc. v. County of Santa Barbara


Civ. No. 26740


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


216 Cal. App. 2d 341; 31 Cal. Rptr. 151; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2025



May 20, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Rehearing and Appellant's Request for a Modification of the Opinion were Denied June 14, 1963. Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 17, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County. C. Douglas Smith, Judge.

Action to recover real property taxes paid to a county.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to amended complaint was sustained with leave to amend and plaintiff declined to amend, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff business sought review from a decision of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which rendered judgment in favor of defendant county, when plaintiff requested the return of real property taxes under the welfare exemption.


OVERVIEW: The questions for the court were whether inclusion of the words "educational, scientific, or literary purposes" in the business' charter disqualified it for the welfare exemption and whether Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 268 had cured the failure of the business to file claims for exemption as required. However, the past and present uses of the business' property had been fully charitable and the problem grew out of the declaration of purposes found in the charter. The court concluded that the articles of incorporation could not be condemned on the ground of nonexempt purposes and that there was no need to amend them. The business was entitled to the welfare exemption for the years in question. The plain meaning of the statutory provisions appeared to be that, while there was no time limit upon the right to cancellation, a refund could be had only after presentation of a proper claim showing a right thereto which had to be filed within three years after payment of the sum sought to be refunded and subject to the further condition that suit must be brought within six months after such rejection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied plaintiff business the return of real property taxes under the welfare exemption.

 

1442 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Metromedia, Inc. v. Pasadena


Civ. No. 26575


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


216 Cal. App. 2d 270; 30 Cal. Rptr. 731; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2016



May 16, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 14, 1963, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 10, 1963. Schauer, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Steven S. Weisman, Judge.

Action to determine constitutionality of city ordinances regulating billboards and to enjoin their enforcement.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiffs reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and others, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which ruled in favor of plaintiff advertisers, declared that certain city ordinances regulating billboards were unconstitutional, and enjoined their enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The city passed ordinances that limited billboard usage and prohibited the construction of billboards. The advertisers filed a complaint alleging that the ordinances were unconstitutional. The trial court agreed with the advertisers and enjoined the enforcement of the ordinances. On appeal, the court reversed. The sole question presented on appeal was whether or not the trial court erred in determining that the distinction made in the ordinances between "point-of-sale" and "non-point-of-sale" signs rendered them unconstitutional as being discriminatory in classification. The court held that the ordinance merely limited the business of outdoor advertising, as it limited other businesses, to specified districts. The advertisers' signs were made pursuant to the conduct of the business of outdoor advertising itself, and did not relate to the structure housing a business like an ordinary business sign. The court held that the unique nature of outdoor advertising and the nuisances fostered by billboards and similar outdoor structures justified the separate classification of such structures for the purposes of governmental regulation and restriction.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the city and others and against the advertisers, and reversed the judgment in the action to enjoin enforcement of city billboard ordinances.

 

1443 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


American Airlines, Inc. v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 26775


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


216 Cal. App. 2d 180; 30 Cal. Rptr. 590; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2003



May 15, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 5, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 10, 1963. Schauer, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Clarence L. Kincaid, Judge.

Action for a refund of use taxes paid under protest to the state.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff common carrier appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that the carrier was not entitled to the refund of use taxes assessed by and paid to defendant state tax board. The superior court held that the use tax applied to the carrier's stored replacement engines and propellers did not violate the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution or Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 6352.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the engines and propellers were purchased for storage and use in California, that the property was stored and used in California, and that the personal property had come to rest in California prior to its installation into aircraft within the meaning of the Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §§ 6008, 6201, 6202. The court rejected the carrier's argument that the taxes imposed on its engines and propellers were outside the purposes of the use tax. The court held that the use tax was a complement to the state sales tax and had been formerly adjudicated a constitutional revenue-raising measure for the state. The court rejected the carrier's assertion that the state use tax could not apply because the engines and propellers were primarily consumed in interstate commerce. The court affirmed that it was adequate that the engines and propellers were purchased and brought into the state for the purpose of installation in aircraft located in the state. The court affirmed that imposition of the use tax was not an unconstitutional burden on interstate commerce and that the board's previous adjudications under § 6352 were consistent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the board was not required to refund the use tax assessed against the carrier.

Muller v. Reagh


Civ. No. 20902


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


215 Cal. App. 2d 831; 30 Cal. Rptr. 633; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2562



May 8, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Byron Arnold, Judge.

Action for damages for false imprisonment and for recovery of personal property or the value thereof.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which dismissed the arrestee's case after sustaining, without leave to amend, defendant individual's demurrer to the arrestee's complaint for false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The arrestee brought a charge of false imprisonment against several individuals and the city and county after he spent several days in jail upon his failure to post bail on a warrant of attachment. The arrestee's complaint and amendments encompassed 170 pages, and the individual sought a demurrer, which the trial court granted, while also denying the arrestee leave to amend. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the arrestee had failed to allege facts constituting the invalidity of the legal process that constituted a false imprisonment. The allegation that the warrant was void, illegal, unauthorized, or that the sheriff unlawfully imprisoned the arrestee were conclusions of law. Furthermore, the court found that the warrant of attachment was regular on its face, and that the endorsement of the judge's order, which did not provide for surety bonds, was the order of the judge, and was in accordance with Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1215.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the individual's demurrer based on the arrestee's failure to allege facts constituting a false imprisonment.

De Martini v. Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control


Civ. Nos. 19938, 20051


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


215 Cal. App. 2d 787; 30 Cal. Rptr. 668; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2558



May 7, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petitions for a Rehearing were Denied June 3, 1963, and the Petitions of Plaintiffs and Respondents, and Plaintiffs and Appellants for a Hearing by the Supreme Court were Denied July 3, 1963. Schauer, J., and Peters, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco and from a writ of mandate. Carl F. Allen, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control to vacate its decision suspending an off-sale general liquor license.



DISPOSITION: Appeals from writ dismissed; judgment reversed with directions. Judgment granting writ reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, suspended plaintiff licensees' off-sale general liquor licenses for selling alcohol at retail prices less than the fair trade price. Upon review, the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) ordered the issuance of peremptory writ of mandate commanding the department to vacate and set aside its decision. Both parties appealed from the judgment and the writ.


OVERVIEW: Initially, the court noted that an appeal could not have been taken from the peremptory writ of mandate, and therefore, it dismissed the appeal from the writ. As to the appeal from the judgment, the court reversed the trial court's order and instructed the trial court to enter judgment denying the petition for a writ of mandate. The court held that (1) the department's decision to suspend the license was supported by substantial evidence, (2) there was no prejudicial abuse of discretion, and (3) the department proceeded in the manner required by law. Accordingly, the court found that the findings and conclusions of the trial court to the contrary were erroneous. Specifically, the court held that the fair trade agreements in question conformed to the statutory requirements of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 23000-25762, were supported by consideration, and were valid and enforceable. Additionally, the court found substantial evidence that the alcoholic beverages covered by the agreements were in fair and open competition.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal from the writ of mandate. As to the appeal from the judgment, the court reversed the trial court's order and instructed the trial court to enter judgment denying the petition for a writ of mandate.

 

1446 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


County of Colusa v. Strain


Civ. No. 10452


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


215 Cal. App. 2d 472; 30 Cal. Rptr. 415; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2522



April 25, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 21, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 19, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Colusa County. Ben R. Ragain, Judge.

Action on agreed facts to determine respective rights of a county and a landowner under a county ordinance requiring a permit for the leveling of land having more than a certain minimum area and to determine the constitutionality of such ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for county affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Colusa County (California), which held: (1) that an ordinance requiring a permit for the leveling of land was constitutional; (2) that a county permit was required without regard to interferences with the drainage rights of neighboring owners; and (3) that upon application, an injunction would issue to restrain the landowner from land leveling without a permit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county adopted an ordinance requiring a permit for the leveling of land having an area greater than five acres. The landowner refused to comply with the ordinance. The parties sought a judicial declaration which, in advance of actual conduct, would determine whether or not that conduct would render a citizen amenable to criminal punishment under a county ordinance, which he asserted to be unconstitutional. Because of the interest, which the landowner alleged in future leveling of his property, and because the ordinance affected a substantial segment of the economy in the county, it was appropriate for the court to pass upon the ordinance. The court determined that the standards, which guided the road commissioner in granting or denying permits, were sufficiently definite. The ordinance did not violate constitutional inhibitions against unlimited delegations of authority. The court held that the exemption of small parcels was not "palpably arbitrary." Finally, if the county desired to provide property owners with advance protection against harm, the court could not say that its action was outside the broad police powers reposed in the county by Cal. Const. art. XI, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order, which held: (1) that an ordinance requiring a permit for the leveling of land was constitutional; (2) that a county permit was required without regard to interferences with the drainage rights of neighboring owners; and (3) that upon application, an injunction would issue to restrain the landowner from land leveling without a permit.

Board of Administration, State Employees' Retirement System v. Ames


Civ. No. 20913


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


215 Cal. App. 2d 215; 29 Cal. Rptr. 917; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2484



April 18, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 12, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Humboldt County. Donald H. Wilkinson, Judge.

Action by the Board of Administration, State Employees' Retirement System, to recover from defendant the actuarial equivalent of benefits for which system is liable to a state employee for injuries received in the course of his employment which were caused by defendant's negligence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Humboldt County (California), which awarded plaintiff retirement system the sum of $ 5,166.78 in an action to recover from defendant the actuarial equivalent of benefits for which plaintiff was liable to a state employee for injuries received in the course of his employment that were caused by defendant's negligence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff state retirement system brought a subrogation action against defendant driver to recover the benefits paid to a state highway patrolman for injuries received in the course of his employment. The patrolman was injured when defendant, while intoxicated, negligently drove his vehicle into the patrol car driven by the state employee. The trial court granted judgment in favor of plaintiff in the amount prayed for, the sum of $ 5,166.78, which sum represented the amount paid the patrolman before a determination was made that his injury was industrially incurred. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that plaintiff's action was not time-barred, and that defendant was not prejudiced by the fact that he was not a party to the Industrial Accident Commission proceeding. The court further held that providing plaintiff a subrogation right to proceed against defendant did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Constitution, because the classification of state employees as different from employees in private business was not arbitrary, but rather had a substantial relation to the purpose for which the legislation was designed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that it was constitutionally permissible for plaintiff state retirement system to assert its subrogation claim against defendant driver to recover the actuarial equivalent of benefits for which plaintiff was liable to a state highway patrolman for injuries received in the course of the patrolman's employment, which resulted from defendant's negligence.

 

1448 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. One 1961 Ford Falcon


Civ. No. 26607


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


215 Cal. App. 2d 149; 30 Cal. Rptr. 110; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2475



April 16, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Ben Koenig, Judge.

Proceeding for forfeiture of an automobile used in violation of the narcotics laws.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the registered co-owners of an automobile, challenged the forfeiture of their car from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) after their daughter was found in the car while in possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Police noticed the occupants of a car holding a lighted cigarette at night in a fire area closed to smoking. They investigated, smelled marijuana, and searched the two occupants. Finding marijuana, the occupants were arrested. The People prevailed in an action seeking forfeiture of the car, and the registered co-owners, the driver's parents, appealed. The court held that the search and seizure was legal because the officers were under a duty to stop to investigate smoking in a fire area. Thereafter, the odor of marijuana, coupled with the passenger's furtive movements, was sufficient to arouse the police officer's suspicion and to justify the subsequent search. It was irrelevant whether the registered owners knew that the car was used for an illegal purpose because they had given their daughter permission to use the vehicle. The forfeiture laws were not unconstitutional because they distinguished between registered owners and legal owners of vehicles as the powers and duties of the two were different.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1449 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Benson v. Superior Court of Napa County


Civ. No. 21127


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


214 Cal. App. 2d 551; 29 Cal. Rptr. 760; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2642



March 28, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of the Real Party in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 22, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in mandamus to compel the Superior Court of Napa County to admit relevant testimony on the issue of 189 claimed illegal votes in an election contest action. Charles J. McGoldrick, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner contestant filed a petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondent Superior Court of Napa County (California) to admit relevant testimony on the issue of 189 claimed illegal votes in an election contest action.


OVERVIEW: The contestant and defendant candidate both ran for public office. The contestant filed a statement with the county clerk contesting the election and demanding a recount, alleging that illegal votes were cast for the candidate. The contestant delivered a list of 189 claimed illegal votes to the constable for service upon the candidate. After the constable was unable to locate the candidate, the constable attached a copy of the list on the door of the candidate's residence on Friday, January 11, 1963. On Tuesday, January 15, the trial of the election contest commenced. Counsel for the candidate objected to the admission of testimony as to the illegal votes because Cal. Elec. Code § 20052 had not been complied with in that a list of the claimed illegal votes had not been delivered to the candidate at least three days before trial. The objection was sustained. On appeal, the court ordered that a peremptory writ issue directing the superior court to receive relevant testimony of the alleged illegal votes. The court held that the attachment of the list to the candidate's door constituted sufficient delivery of the list because § 20052 made no reference to "personal service."


OUTCOME: The court ordered that a peremptory writ issue directing the superior court to receive relevant and material testimony of the 189 votes asserted by the contestant to be illegal votes.

 

1450 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Van Zanten v. Superior Court of San Diego County


Civ. No. 7244


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


214 Cal. App. 2d 510; 29 Cal. Rptr. 625; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2638



March 27, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of San Diego County from proceeding further on a petition to commit a person for treatment as a narcotics addict. Vincent A. Whelan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner arrestee filed a petition for a writ of prohibition against respondent Superior Court of San Diego County to restrain the superior court from taking further action on a petition. The arrestee had been arrested under Cal. Penal Code § 11721 for the unlawful use of narcotics, and a petition had been filed under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 6500-6510 seeking to commit her as a person addicted to the use of narcotics or in danger thereof.


OVERVIEW: On her return from Mexico, an arrestee, who was a resident of Bellflower, California, was arrested by federal authorities for failing to register as a narcotics user. While in a county jail, a deputy saw needle marks on her arms, concluded that she was in imminent danger of becoming addicted to narcotics, and arrested her under Cal. Penal Code § 11721 for the unlawful use of narcotics. Then, she was taken to doctors in San Diego, California, where she admitted to the use of narcotics, and was released. Later, a petition was filed under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 6500-6510 in San Diego seeking to commit her as a narcotics addict, and she was brought to San Diego County. She sought a writ of prohibition to restrain the superior court from taking action on the petition. The court held that: (1) Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6502 required an order directing an examination of an alleged addict to recite that a petition had been filed stating that there "is now" in such county a person, who was mentally ill; and (2) the superior court had no authority because the arrestee was not a resident of San Diego County and she was not actually present therein when the petition was filed.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ.

Ehrlich v. McConnell


Civ. No. 26392


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


214 Cal. App. 2d 280; 29 Cal. Rptr. 283; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2605



March 21, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Rex Hardy, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Insurance Commissioner to set aside his decision suspending licenses of insurance agents and brokers for a period of six months.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), denying appellants' writ of mandate asking the court to compel respondent Commissioner of Insurance to reverse the judgment suspending appellants' insurance license.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed a writ of mandate to compel respondent Commissioner of Insurance to reinstate appellants' license to sell insurance, after respondent suspended appellants' license for misrepresentation in advertising and in financing insurance premiums in a manner constituting loans of money at usurious interest rates. The trial court entered judgment for respondent, and appellants sought review. On appeal, the court held that the finding that appellants engaged in misleading advertising was supported by substantial evidence. In so holding, the court stated that appellants sent solicitation letters to individuals that just had their license suspended and the letters misrepresented the nature of the premium charged for insurance since the purpose of the transaction was to finance insurance premiums. Further, the court held that the trial court's failure to make specific findings requested by appellants was not an error. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment for respondent.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying appellants' writ of mandate asking the court to compel respondent Commissioner of Insurance to reverse the judgment to suspend appellants' insurance license was affirmed.

 

1452 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Garey


Civ. No. 26411


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


214 Cal. App. 2d 39; 29 Cal. Rptr. 98; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2570



March 14, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 5, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 8, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County determining heirship. Newcomb Condee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner grandchild appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which deemed her ineligible to recover from her intestate deceased paternal grandmother's estate owing to the adoption of the grandchild by her stepfather.


OVERVIEW: Grandchild appealed a judgment holding that she was not an heir to her deceased paternal grandmother's estate owing to her adoption by her stepfather. The court affirmed. The grandchild's mother had divorced her natural father, who was the child of the deceased paternal grandmother and later remarried. Thereafter, the grandchild was adopted by her mother's new husband, her stepfather. When her natural father's mother died intestate, the grandchild sought to be deemed an heir. The trial judge rejected this effort, ruling that the grandchild's adoption by her stepfather extinguished her right to intestate succession from her natural father's ancestors. On appeal, the court held that this was a correct interpretation of the state Probate Code's provision dealing with adoptions. The judgment below was therefore affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment below was affirmed. Grandchild's adoption by her stepfather extinguished the paternal rights of her natural father and, thus, the grandchild's right to recover from her natural father's intestate ancestors upon their deaths was likewise extinguished.

 

1453 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Finston


Crim. No. 8266


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


214 Cal. App. 2d 54; 29 Cal. Rptr. 165; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2571



March 14, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 5, 1963, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 8, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. Donald R. Wright, Judge.

Prosecution for forgery and grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which, following a nonjury trial, convicted defendant of forgery and grand theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, while employed by an auto dealership, forged signatures of endorsement on customers' refund checks and deposited the checks into his personal bank account. Defendant also obtained checks from his employer for nonexistent referrals. On appeal, defendant contended that Cal. Penal Code § 487.1 unreasonably increased the penalties for theft crimes committed by employees and was unconstitutional. The court held, however, that employees constituted a class so reasonably identified as to justify classified legislation. The court found no error in the admission of evidence concerning similar acts for which defendant was not charged. Such evidence addressed the issues of defendant's knowledge and intent. Pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 956, an error in identifying the name of defendant's employer was not material.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

1454 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


South Coast Fisheries, Inc. v. Department of Fish & Game


Civ. No. 26173


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


213 Cal. App. 2d 325; 28 Cal. Rptr. 537; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2731



February 21, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 17, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying a new trial. George Francis, Judge.

Actions for a refund of moneys paid to the state for fish processing licenses and taxes.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed; appeal from orders dismissed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fishermen sought review of decisions from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgments in favor of respondent Department of Fish and Game in the fishermen's actions for a refund of moneys paid to the State for fish processing licenses and taxes.


OVERVIEW: The fishermen brought actions against the Department for a refund of moneys paid to the State for fish processing licenses and taxes. The trial court entered judgments in favor of the Department. On appeal, the fishermen contended that the tax in question was illegal because it was a disguised tax upon fish imported before they had lost their character as "imports" under the "original package" doctrine enunciated in case law. The court held that: (1) a privilege tax measured by gross product consumed was a valid exercise of the State's taxing power; (2) goods imported by manufacturers for use in their manufacturing processes lost their tax exempt status as "imports" when they had been committed to, and were essential to, their current operational needs; and (3) a tax upon a processing and canning business could be validly levied, and the amount thereof computed by measuring the materials that were received at the processing plants and that, because of their very nature, were immediately put to the very use for which they were imported.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1455 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Crees v. California State Board of Medical Examiners


Civ. No. 26230


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


213 Cal. App. 2d 195; 28 Cal. Rptr. 621; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2715



February 20, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 21, 1963, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 17, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Walter C. Allen, Judge.

Action to have defined and declared certain rights, immunities, and privileges claimed under the Medical Practice Act and the Chiropractic Act and to enjoin defendants from interfering with such rights.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff chiropractors appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in favor of defendants, State Board of Medical Examiners and State Board of Chiropractic Examiners (boards), in an action for a declaration of the chiropractors' rights and duties under the Medical Practice Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 2000-2490, and the Chiropractic Initiative Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 1000, 1001-1 to 1000-19.


OVERVIEW: The chiropractors brought an action seeking to have certain claimed rights defined and declared under the Medical Practice Act (MPA) and the Chiropractic Initiative Act (CIA). The trial court entered judgment for the boards. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the trial court and held that colleges of chiropractic could not expand and enlarge the rights of chiropractors under the CIA. Therefore, an inquiry into the curricula was irrelevant. The scope of the term "chiropractic" was limited to the understanding and definition of the term in 1922, when the CIA was enacted. The possession of a chiropractic license was not a defense to a violation of the MPA. Any regulation purporting to enlarge the scope of the CIA was invalid. Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 2141, which made the treatment of the sick without a valid license a misdemeanor, was not unconstitutionally vague and did not violate the chiropractors' due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court granting judgment to the boards in the chiropractors' declaratory judgment action to have their rights under the MPA and CIA defined..

 

1456 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Good


Civ. No. 20745


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


213 Cal. App. 2d 45; 28 Cal. Rptr. 378; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2693



February 15, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 4, 1963, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 9, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Marin County overruling objections and fixing additional inheritance tax. N. Charles Brusatori, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executor sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which overruled his objections to respondent controller's fixing an additional inheritance tax pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 13441.


OVERVIEW: The children as executors considered that gifts that were made to them by the deceased were made in contemplation of death and thus reported them as such in their California inheritance tax affidavit and federal estate tax return, which subjected them to the California death tax as well. I.R.C. § 2011 calculated the credit for state death taxes without any credit for gift taxes, and the controller fixed an additional tax pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 13441, which was the amount by which the credit pursuant to § 2011 exceeded the California inheritance tax. The executor objected on the ground that the application of § 13441 increased their aggregate federal and state death taxes, therefore they should have been able to pay the amount of the additional state tax to the Federal Government. The court held that the word "allowed" in § 13441 meant "allowable," therefore all the controller had done by his additional assessment was impose a tax to which the state was rightfully entitled. The court determined that although § 13441 was designed to benefit the taxpayer, they refused to adopt a construction of § 13441 that would have deprived the state of its right to a tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that overruled the executor's objections to the controller's imposition of an additional inheritance tax.

 

1457 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rozell


Crim. No. 3387


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


212 Cal. App. 2d 875; 28 Cal. Rptr. 478; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2923



February 11, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 13, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Albert H. Mundt, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft by false pretenses.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment (order granting probation following a conviction) affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) for grand theft by false pretenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant applied for and received benefits under the aid to needy children program. However, she failed to disclose that an unrelated adult male was living with her during the period she received benefits. Under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 1508, the income of this adult male should have been taken into consideration in determining defendant's eligibility for benefits. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to conclude that the adult male was living with defendant. Defendant used his surname on credit applications, and they both signed a conditional sales contract for the purchase of used car. The adult male was frequently observed in defendant's home, and articles of his clothing were found there. The adult male listed defendant's address as his residence in employment paperwork. The court upheld the constitutionality of § 1508. The statutory language was not vague, and the statute did not deprive the adult male of his property without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Alden v. Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County


Civ. No. 26875


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


212 Cal. App. 2d 764; 28 Cal. Rptr. 387; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2908



February 7, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County from conducting further proceedings in an injunction action.



DISPOSITION: Peremptory writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner water board directors sought a writ of prohibition to restrain respondent, the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County (California)(superior court), from issuing an injunction enjoining the directors from acting based on invalid election.


OVERVIEW: The directors sought a writ of prohibition to bar the superior court from granting an injunction against the directors' authority. A peremptory writ was granted by the court to resolve the issues given the public interest in the efficient workings of the water board. The court found no merit to the claims by the real parties in interest, the citizens who commenced the initial action, that the water board formation election was not lawfully conducted. The court found that because a certificate had been issued by the secretary of state as required under the Cal. Water Code § 30323, the county water district was formally incorporated and beyond attack by a private individual. The court determined that the formation election had not violated any constitutional prohibition and that there was no evidence of irregularity under the procedure required to form a county water district as prescribed under the code.


OUTCOME: The court granted the directors' petition and issued a writ of prohibition that restrained the superior court from any further action, except for dismissal, on the complaint against the directors.

 

1459 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


H. W. Rohl Co. v. County of San Diego


Civ. No. 6783


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


212 Cal. App. 2d 707; 28 Cal. Rptr. 196; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2901



February 6, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 25, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Bonsall Noon, Judge.

Action to have a county ordinance declared invalid and to enjoin its enforcement and proceeding in mandamus to review the county board of supervisors' denial of a use permit and to compel the issuance of the permit.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed. Judgment for defendants modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee quarry sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which sustained appellee county's objection to the introduction of evidence on whether a county zoning ordinance was valid and which denied the quarry's application for a writ of mandate directing the county to approve its application for a permit to operate a rock crushing and processing plant.


OVERVIEW: The quarry sought a use permit in order to operate a rock crushing and processing plant. The planning commission recommended approval of the permit, but the county's board of supervisors denied the permit after a hearing de novo. The quarry brought an action against the county on two bases: 1) that the ordinance that permitted the board to hold a hearing de novo and make its own recommendation was invalid; and 2) that the board abused its discretion in denying the permit. The trial court sustained the county's objections to taking evidence on the first issue and decided that the board had not abused its discretion when it denied the permit. The quarry sought review, and the court affirmed, as modified. The court held that that first question could not have been decided in the same action as the second. However, the court said, the trial court's order sounded as if the quarry could never have challenged the ordinance's validity. Therefore, the court modified the order to state that the validity of the ordinance could not have been challenged until after the quarry had exhausted its other remedies. As to the denial of the permit, the court found that the record supported the order.


OUTCOME: The court modified and affirmed a judgment that upheld the county's objections to evidence of whether the county's zoning ordinance was valid. The court also affirmed an order that denied the quarry's application for a writ of mandate to compel the county to approve its application for a permit to operate a rock crushing and processing plant.

 

1460 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Du Bois v. Land


Civ. No. 6910


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


212 Cal. App. 2d 563; 28 Cal. Rptr. 167; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2880



January 31, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Richard B. Ault, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the board of directors of a county water district to take steps for holding a referendum in regard to an ordinance including additional property in the district.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners within an area sought to be included in a county water district, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied the owners' request for a writ of mandamus to compel respondents, board members of the county's water district, to take steps to hold a referendum with regard to an ordinance that sought to include additional property in the district.


OVERVIEW: After the board of directors adopted an ordinance to include the additional property in the district, the owners filed a petition for referendum of the ordinance; the petition did not include signatures of registered voters who lived within the district. On appeal from the superior court's denial of mandamus relief, the owners contended that the California Water Code was to be construed as providing registered voters in an area sought to be included with a right of referendum and that unless so construed, the Code would be discriminatory and unconstitutional. The court held that the unambiguous provisions of Cal. Water Code §§ 32400, 32402, 32406, 32447, 32448 applied to the ordinance passed by the board of directors and clearly vested a right of referendum only in the voters and electors of the district itself. The voters, such as the owners, residing in the land sought to be included had no such right of referendum for the obvious reason that they were not electors of the district. The court also found that the classification in the statutes was not unconstitutional because it was reasonable; electors in the district bore the greatest burden of expense involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Housing Authority of County of Kings v. Peden


Civ. No. 200


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


212 Cal. App. 2d 276; 28 Cal. Rptr. 11; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2844



January 22, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the Superior Court of Kings County overruling demurrer without leave to answer and directing clerk to issue peremptory writ of mandate. Meredith Wingrove, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant chairman of the Housing Authority of Kings County, California, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Kings County (California), which overruled his demurrer and ordered him by a peremptory writ of mandate to execute a housing cooperation agreement between the City of Hanford and respondent Housing Authority of Kings County, so that the city could join in a countywide housing development plan.


OVERVIEW: The city chose to participate in a countywide housing development plan rather than establish a separate city housing authority. The city council adopted a resolution conforming to the requirements of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 34209 to join the countywide plan. The city was required to execute a cooperation agreement with the county housing authority, as well, but the chairman refused. The county housing authority filed a petition for a peremptory writ of mandate ordering the chairman to execute the cooperation agreement. The chairman filed a demurrer, which was overruled. The superior court issued the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that Cal. Const. art. XXXIV, § 1 gave the city the alternative of proceeding separately or as part of the countywide housing development plan. Following the city's resolution, the plan was approved in a valid countywide election. The court held that the city's voters had sufficient notice of the housing plan that was at issue because it was publicized in newspaper articles, at public meetings, at club meetings, at a booth at the county fair, by the distribution of literature, by a 250-person committee, and by an opposition committee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the superior court.
