O'Kane v. Catuira


Civ. Nos. 20548, 20549, 20550


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


212 Cal. App. 2d 131; 27 Cal. Rptr. 818; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2823; 94 A.L.R.2d 487



January 21, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 5, 1963, in each of the Consolidated Cases and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 20, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Alvin E. Weinberger, Judge.

Actions to enjoin defendants from engaging in the business of transmitting moneys from the United States to the Philippines.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, California Superintendent of Banks (superintendent), appealed from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which refused to enjoin defendants, corporation and individuals engaged in the business of transmission of moneys from the United States to the Philippines, from continuance of their business.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent filed actions against an incorporated travel agency and two individuals, who were engaged in the foreign exchange business in California and the Philippines, that sought to enjoin them from continuation of their business because of their failure to be businesses of the type approved by the statutes. Each of the defendants argued that application of Cal. Fin. Code § 1800, 1801 to them was unconstitutional. The trial court denied the superintendent's actions, and found the statutes were unconstitutional. The superintendent appealed. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the legislation did not have a reasonable or substantial reason for the discrimination against defendants' businesses as opposed to the types of businesses that were allowed licenses. Such distinctions were unreasonable and arbitrary and a violation of Cal. Const. art. I, § 21, the privileges and immunities clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that the statutes, which provided for licensure and regulation of money exchange with foreign and United States currency, were unconstitutional in their entirety.

 

1463 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. One 1960 Mercedes Benz Roadster


Civ. No. 20603


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


211 Cal. App. 2d 842; 27 Cal. Rptr. 617; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2975



January 16, 1963 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 13, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Raymond G. Callaghan, Judge.

Proceeding for forfeiture of vehicle used in the unlawful transportation of narcotics.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment decreeing forfeiture, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant car owner appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which ordered the forfeiture of defendant motor vehicle to the State because it was used to unlawfully transport narcotics.


OVERVIEW: The car owner's motor vehicle was used to unlawfully transport narcotics. This use was without his knowledge; however, he did give the driver express permission to drive the motor vehicle. On appeal, the car owner alleged that the forfeiture statute, Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 11610-11629 violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and Cal. Const. art. I, §§ 13 and 21. Specifically, he argued that there was no reasonable basis for the distinction made between registered owners and lienholders in Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 11621-11622. Affirming the judgment, the court held that the distinction made between registered owners and lienholders was not arbitrary or unreasonable and that it was reasonably and substantially related to the legitimate purposes of the legislation, which was the suppression of illegal narcotics traffic. It was reasonable to assume that registered owners had more direct control over the use of their motor vehicles than lienholders had. This assumption warranted the exemption given to lienholders under Cal. Health & Safety Code §§ 11621-11622.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1464 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Contreras


Crim. No. 7690


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


211 Cal. App. 2d 641; 27 Cal. Rptr. 619; 1963 Cal. App. LEXIS 2954



January 9, 1963 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. Herbert V. Walker, Judge.

Prosecution for possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for possession of marijuana in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530 and the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: A police officer recognized a woman he had arrested for prostitution and drug offenses with defendant. He followed them to a hotel. The officer noted from the fire escape that the window to their room was closed. He went up to the room and heard sounds that caused him to believe that they were having sex. He knocked on the door. When the woman opened it, defendant was on the bed and the window was open. He discovered a needle and syringe in an empty cigarette package just outside the window. The officer searched the room and found a marijuana cigarette in defendant's coat pocket. Defendant was convicted of possession of marijuana with a prior conviction of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11500. He filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the officer's suspicions were reasonable. He did not have sufficient evidence as he stood outside of the hotel room to make an arrest, but he did have grounds to make a further inquiry. The woman's actions supported the inference that she consented to the officer entering the room and once the officer found the narcotic kit outside the window there was probable cause to search the entire room.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1465 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Smith


Civ. No. 6857


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


211 Cal. App. 2d 473; 27 Cal. Rptr. 536; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1531



December 28, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Respondent City of Barstow for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 20, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County. Joseph T. Ciano, Judge.

Action against a police officer and the city employing him for damages for the officer's allegedly wilful and malicious shooting of plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of dismissal as to city after demurrers to counts of second amended complaint directed against city were sustained without leave to amend, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant victim challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which overruled the demurrer on the victim's first cause of action against respondent police officer, but sustained the demurrers without leave to amend as to the causes of action against respondent city, and dismissed those causes against the city.


OVERVIEW: The victim was shot in the back by the police officer after the victim was placed under arrest and then fled from the police officer. The victim's complaint alleged that the police officer willfully and maliciously shot the victim and that the city was negligent in its hiring, retention, and instruction of the police officer. After the police officer and the city answered the complaint, the victim amended his complaint twice. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the victim's second amended complaint was insufficiently pled such that the court was unable to determine if the city was not relieved of its liability because the police officer was performing a discretionary act when he shot the victim. The court found that because the victim's complaint was insufficiently pled, the superior court erred in sustaining the demurrer, as there were factual issues as to whether the city was liable or not; thus, the city should answer the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order in favor of the city that sustained the city's demurrer to the victim's cause of action without leave to amend and instructed the superior court to overrule the demurrer and allow the city to answer the victim's complaint.

 

1466 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Jorgensen v. Cranston


Civ. No. 10415


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


211 Cal. App. 2d 292; 27 Cal. Rptr. 297; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1507



December 21, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Stanley W. Reckers, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the State Controller to pay a judge's widow the allowances provided by the Judges' Retirement Law, as amended.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment granting writ, but denying interest, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state controller appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which held that plaintiff, a judge's widow, was entitled to a writ of mandate which retroactively granted her an increase in her widow's pension benefits. The widow cross-appealed the superior court's denial of interest on the judgment that was awarded to her.


OVERVIEW: The widow's husband died in 1954. The widow received all of the benefits that she was entitled to at that time, which consisted of a lump-sum payment. The law pertaining to widows of judges was thereafter amended, and Cal. Gov't Code § 75104.4 provided that the widow was entitled to one-half of the pension that her husband would have received. The controller contended that the retroactive legislation violated Cal. Const. art. IV, §§ 31, 32. The lower court granted a writ of mandate and held that the widow was entitled to the pension, but she was not entitled to interest on her pension payments. The court affirmed, holding that even though the widow had received a lump-sum payment that paid her all the pension monies that were due her at the time, the retroactive increase in her pension rights was not an unconstitutional gift because her pensionable status had continued even after she received the lump-sum distribution. Because Cal. Civ. Code § 3287 did not apply to public retirement funds, the court ruled that the widow was not entitled to interest on the additional pension funds that she was entitled to receive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which granted the widow of a writ of mandate requiring the controller to retroactively pay her increased widow's benefits and which denied the widow interest on the judgment which she received.

 

1467 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Modesto Irrigation Dist. v. Modesto


Civ. No. 150


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


210 Cal. App. 2d 652; 27 Cal. Rptr. 90; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1615



December 11, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 6, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County. Ross A. Carkeet, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action seeking declaratory relief respecting a municipal ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment holding the ordinance valid affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff irrigation district (district) appealed from a declaratory judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California), which held valid a ordinance of respondent city, regulating the location of overhead utilities. The trial court denied an injunction to permanently enjoin the city from enforcing the ordinance, which was enacted pursuant to the Subdivision Map Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 11500 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The district was engaged in the business of transmitting, distributing, and selling electric power. A city ordinance required the location of overhead utilities on lot easements rather than along city streets. The district contended that the ordinance was invalid because the state had exclusive jurisdiction over the franchise of power lines in cities. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of a declaratory judgment for the city. The ordinance was not in conflict with any state statute. It was enacted pursuant to an express delegation of authority under Calif. Water Code § 22476. The only restriction imposed by the state was that any condition imposed by a city had to be reasonable. The court construed § 22476 with reference to the Subdivision Map Act. The ordinance did not exceed the power delegated to the city. It did not prohibit the use of streets by the district and included four specific exceptions to compliance with it, as well as one exception for other good and sufficient reasons. The mere showing that the maintenance of power lines along easements was more burdensome or more expensive did not, ipso facto, make the restrictions unreasonable.


OUTCOME: In a declaratory judgment action brought by the district, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which upheld the validity of the city's ordinance regulating overhead utilities.

 

1468 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Marrone


Crim. No. 1814


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


210 Cal. App. 2d 299; 26 Cal. Rptr. 721; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1574



November 29, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County and from an order denying a new trial. Vincent A. Whelan, Judge.

Prosecution for kidnaping and for conspiracy to commit the crime of kidnaping.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted him of kidnapping and conspiracy to commit the crime of kidnapping. Defendant also challenged the trial court court's denial of his motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of kidnapping and conspiracy to commit the crime of kidnapping. The trial court denied defendant's motion for new trial. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that a jury instruction regarding the existence of an agreement between defendant and a coconspirator was erroneous where the jury instruction incorrectly stated defendant could be convicted even if the jury believed his claim that he was just simulating the kidnapping of the victim. The court reasoned that the prosecution needed to show that he intended to do an unlawful act. The court held that the error was harmless because it was obvious the jury did not believe the testimony of defendant in reference to any feigned or simulated kidnapping of the victim. The court determined no prejudicial error resulted from the trial judge's remarks pertaining to what factors the jury could consider in deciding whether defendant was telling the truth where the remarks were a fair and logical statement of the facts. The court concluded comments made by the trial judge in no way led the jury to believe defendant had the burden of proving his innocence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of kidnapping and conspiracy to commit the crime of kidnapping. The court also affirmed an order that denied defendant's motion for new trial.

 

1469 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Bank of America Nat'l Trust & Sav. Asso. v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 20120


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


209 Cal. App. 2d 780; 26 Cal. Rptr. 348; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1744



November 20, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 16, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Clarence W. Morris, Judge.

Action by a bank for the recovery of a specified sum, with interest, charged to and collected from the bank as use tax.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which entered judgment in favor of respondent state in an action by the bank to recover a specified sum, with interest, that had been charged to and collected from the bank as a use tax.


OVERVIEW: The state charged use taxes against a bank on the ground that the bank was required to collect the taxes from its depositors who had purchased personalized checks, and having failed to do so became liable for the payment of the taxes and interest thereon from its own funds. The bank contested liability for the taxes, paid the taxes and interest under protest, filed a written claim for refund, and upon rejection of the claim filed an action for recovery of the amount paid, with interest. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the state. On appeal, the court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that the bank was a retailer in accordance with Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 6203, that a retailer who failed to collect the use tax was liable to the state for the tax pursuant to § 6203-6204, that a retailer's liability was one of a debt and not of the tax itself, and that imposition of such a liability on the bank was no more of an interference with its functions as a national bank than any other legal proceeding to which it might be subjected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that the bank was obligated to collect and pay the state's use tax that was owed by the bank's depositors who had purchased personalized checks, and that having failed to do so the bank was obligated to pay the amount owed from its own funds.

 

1470 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Swann v. Burkett


Civ. No. 20464


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


209 Cal. App. 2d 685; 26 Cal. Rptr. 286; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1730



November 19, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 16, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court for the Berkeley-Albany Judicial District of Alameda County. Redmond C. Staats, Jr., Judge.

Action for damages for refusal of defendants to rent a unit of a triplex to plaintiffs because of their race.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for defendants reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, brought suit against defendant owners under the Unruh Civil Rights Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 51, based on the property owners' refusal to rent a triplex unit to them because they were black. The Appellate Department of the Alameda County Superior Court (California) reversed the trial court's granting of a nonsuit for owners and certified the question of whether a triplex rental was a business activity under the Act.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, finding that the owner was engaged in a permanent settled position in renting his triplex units for gain, and that Cal. Civ. Code §§ 51-52 applied to the situation of a triplex rental. The court found that the legislature used the words "all" and "of every kind whatsoever" in referring to business establishments covered in Cal. Civ. Code § 51, and the inclusion of these words, without any exceptions and without specification of particular kinds of enterprises, left no doubt that the term business establishments was used in the broadest sense reasonably possible. The provisions of the Hawkins Act, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 35700 et seq., which related only to discriminatory practices by an owner of a publicly assisted housing accommodation, did not act to show a legislative intent to exclude from application of the Unruh Civil Rights Act a broader definition of housing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court for the owner.

 

1471 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Paul v. Wadler


Civ. No. 20592


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


209 Cal. App. 2d 615; 26 Cal. Rptr. 341; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1724



November 16, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County denying defendants' motion for dissolution and modification of a temporary restraining order and granting plaintiff a preliminary injunction restraining defendants from selling fluid milk below the minimum established price. Robert E. Cassin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant milk seller challenged the order of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which denied its motion for dissolution and modification of a temporary restraining order and granted respondent state a preliminary injunction restraining appellant from selling fluid milk below the minimum established price.


OVERVIEW: Respondent filed a complaint alleging that appellants were engaged in the business of selling fluid milk and that appellants used various schemes so that the net amount paid by the consumer was less than the applicable retail store minimum price prescribed by law. Appellants admitted their status as retail stores subject to regulation by the respondent, as well as the course of conduct charged, but maintained that their actions were legal and the statutes unconstitutional. The court found that Cal. Agric. Code § 4361 did not prevent appellants from buying containers from their customers, but it prevented them from doing this in connection with the sale of milk so that the price paid by the customer would be less than the established minimum price. The court noted that the statute specifically provided that the credit for the return of the container must be in excess of the minimum price. The court concluded that appellants could not use the subterfuge of buying back empty containers to avoid the established minimum price provided by law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order because there was no abuse of discretion in issuing the preliminary injunction where appellant violated a statute regulating milk prices.

Banning v. Desert Outdoor Advertising, Inc.


Civ. No. 6866


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


209 Cal. App. 2d 152; 25 Cal. Rptr. 621; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1669



October 30, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 26, 1962. Schauer, J., and Peters, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County. S. Thomas Bucciarelli, Judge.

Action to enjoin maintenance of a billboard sign allegedly located in violation of a setback ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advertiser challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which enjoined the advertiser from maintaining a sign located 4 feet from an abutting roadway, pursuant to an ordinance of appellee city that established a 20-foot setback for all buildings or structures.


OVERVIEW: The city brought an action that sought to enjoin the advertiser from maintaining a sign within four feet of an abutting roadway. The advertiser asserted that the ordinance was being unconstitutionally, inequitably and unjustly enforced, in that the city's officials refused to enforce its provisions against any person other than the defendant. The trial court enjoined maintenance of the sign after it determined that the enforcement of the ordinance by the city or its officials had not been with intentional or purposeful discrimination. The advertiser asserted that other signs in the city had not been subjects of actions even though they also violated the city ordinance. The court affirmed the decision to enjoin maintenance of the sign and determined that in a proceeding arising out of the violation of a statute, the mere showing of a failure to institute similar proceeding with respect to other known violations did not require a finding that the enforcement proceeding in question was prompted by intentional or purposeful discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of the city that enjoined the advertiser from maintaining a sign located 4 feet from an abutting roadway, pursuant to a city ordinance that established a 20-foot setback for all buildings or structures.

 

1474 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Conrad v. Superior Court of Tehama County


Civ. No. 10538


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


209 Cal. App. 2d 143; 25 Cal. Rptr. 670; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1668



October 30, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 26, 1962. Peek, J., did not Participate Therein.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Tehama County from proceeding further on an information.



DISPOSITION: Order to show cause discharged and writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Tehama County (California) from further proceedings based upon an information in four counts charging petitioner with violations of California's Corporate Securities Law, familiarly known as the "Blue Sky Law," Cal. Corp. Code § 25000 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The information alleged that petitioner had violated Cal. Corp. Code §§ 26104(a), 25500, and 25152. Petitioner contended that the evidence at the preliminary hearing was insufficient to justify petitioner's being held to answer because the securities laws did not make it a crime for an individual to sell corporate securities which he owned for the benefit of the corporation and that if § 25152 were so construed, it would be unconstitutional. The court disagreed and denied the writ. The court held that the evidence at the preliminary hearing presented a clear picture that petitioner acted as a promoter soliciting and obtaining money from four individuals upon representations that they were to receive his personal shares, when, in fact, the corporate shares had not been issued and when the application before the California Corporation Commissioner for their issuance had been removed and was later abandoned. Such activity clearly constituted a criminal violation of the securities laws. In addition, § 25152 was not unconstitutional because § 25152, when read in conjunction with § 26104(a), made it clear that the actions of the petitioner constituted a public offense.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitioner's writ of prohibition holding that the evidence at the preliminary hearing was sufficient to require him to answer and that the state security laws were not unconstitutional for lack of clarity.

Paul v. Allied Dairymen, Inc.

Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


209 Cal. App. 2d 112; 25 Cal. Rptr. 595; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1663

Action to enjoin a dairy association from violating minimum producer price regulations of the Department of Agriculture concerning fluid milk and other dairy products.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state agriculture director appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Tulare County (California), which dismissed for lack of jurisdiction an action seeking to restrain defendant milk producers' association from violating state regulations setting minimum prices for dairy products.


OVERVIEW: The California Milk Stabilization Act (Act), Cal. Agr. Code, div. 6, ch. 17, regulated, in part, minimum prices for dairy products sold in California. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the action. The court held that since the sole matter before the trial court was the preliminary injunction application, the trial court did not have jurisdiction to reach the merits of the underlying action, and therefore the dismissal of the action was error.

1477 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Southern Pacific Co.


Crim. No. 44


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


208 Cal. App. 2d 745; 25 Cal. Rptr. 644; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1859



October 22, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 19, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of dismissal of the Justice Court of Madera County. Alec W. Brown, Judge.

Prosecution for wilfully and unlawfully failing to provide cattle with proper feed while such cattle were in one of defendant's cattle cars.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to the complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision by the California Superior Court, which affirmed a decision that granted defendant's motion to dismiss a charge of unlawfully failing to provide cattle with proper food and drink in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 597.


OVERVIEW: Defendant transported cattle from Utah to California. Once the rail car reached its destination, the cattle were left in the rail car without food and water. The consignee had not yet accepted delivery and defendant still had charge and custody of the cattle. The State charged defendant with unlawfully failing to provide food and water for the cattle. Defendant filed a demurrer to the charge, which the justice court sustain on the basis that the charge was preempted by the Cruelty to Animals Act, 45 U.S.C.S. §§ 71-74. The superior court affirmed that decision and the State sought review. The court affirmed, finding that whether federal law superseded state law in this instance depended on whether the cattle were still in interstate commerce. The court held that they were. The court noted that an interstate shipment was not complete until there was complete delivery to the consignee and surrender of dominion and control over the property by defendant. Because the cattle were still in the rail car and had not been delivered to the consignee, they were still in interstate commerce. The court further held that the federal act precluded the application of state law to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the State's charges against defendant, which accused defendant of failing to provide food and water to cattle.

People v. Hoerler

Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two

1479 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


County of San Mateo v. Palomar Holding Co.


Civ. No. 20275


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


208 Cal. App. 2d 194; 24 Cal. Rptr. 905; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1772



October 4, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Joseph A. Branson, Judge.

Action by a county to enjoin defendants from dividing and transferring any real property owned by them in a certain unincorporated area of the county without prior approval under certain county ordinances.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment granting an injunction, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant builders appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which, at the request of plaintiff county, enjoined the builders from subdividing and transferring real property without first obtaining the county's approval through the procedures contained in San Mateo County, Cal., Ordinance No. 977 § 2(n).


OVERVIEW: The lower court found that the builders sold lots without complying with § 2(n), which required the builders to submit their subdivision plats to the county. The builders claimed their constitutional rights were violated and that the approval of adjacent developments that they owned was tantamount to county approval for the disputed, specified properties. The lower court enjoined the builders from subdividing and transferring the specified real property without first obtaining the county's approval, and the court affirmed. The court held that the procedures contained in § 2(n) did not grant the county planning commission judicial functions and because the planning commission did not have judicial functions, there was no due process requirement for a hearing. The court also ruled that the builders had no standing to object to the application of § 2(n) because the builders were required to invoke and exhaust their administrative remedies before seeking redress in the courts. The court further held that the builders were required to submit development plans for all their properties because the planning issues for all of the builders properties were not identical.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which enjoined the builders from subdividing and transferring specified real property without first having the subdivision approved by the county.

 

1480 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Gleason v. Santa Monica


Civ. No. 25995


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


207 Cal. App. 2d 458; 24 Cal. Rptr. 656; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1930



September 6, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 2, 1962, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 31, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Allen T. Lynch, Judge.

Action to determine constitutionality of certain provisions of the California Redevelopment Law and for other relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to fifth amended complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents of city sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgment in favor of defendant city and sustained the city's demurrer to the residents' fifth amended complaint without leave to amend. The residents' action challenged the constitutionality of provisions of the California Redevelopment Law.


OVERVIEW: The residents filed a complaint for declaratory relief challenging the constitutionality of provisions of the California Redevelopment Law. Acting under these provisions, the city adopted an ordinance approving a redevelopment plan and appropriating certain public expenditures for that purpose. The complaint challenging the ordinance was filed within 60 days after the ordinance was adopted, as required by Cal. Health & Safety Code § 33746. The city filed an answer alleging that the complaint failed to state facts sufficient to constitute a cause of action. In sustaining the city's demurrer to the complaint, the superior court calculated the time within which the action should have been brought from the date that the city council voted in adopting the ordinance, as opposed to the ordinance's effective date. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the word "adoption" in § 33746 applied to the city's decision to adopt the ordinance, and not to the effective date of the ordinance. Since an action had to be brought within 60 days after the date of adoption and since the date of adoption was the date the ordinance was acted upon, the residents' action was not timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court, which dismissed the residents' complaint without leave to amend.

 

1481 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Vassar


Crim. No. 1711


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


207 Cal. App. 2d 318; 24 Cal. Rptr. 481; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1911



August 30, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 24, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County and from an order denying a new trial. Merrill Brown, Judge.

Prosecution for illegally furnishing, giving and administering heroin to a minor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which denied his motion for a new trial after he was convicted of unlawfully, furnishing, giving, and administering a narcotic other than marijuana to a minor, a violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11502.


OVERVIEW: After a minor asked defendant for a fix, defendant allegedly injected heroin in the minor's arm. Defendant was convicted of unlawfully, furnishing, giving, and administering a narcotic other than marijuana to a minor under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11502. After the trial court denied his motion for a new trial, defendant appealed. On review, the court held that § 11502 was not unconstitutionally vague where it did not define the word minor. The court further held that there was sufficient evidence to show that the minor was injected with a narcotic. The evidence submitted was that the minor requested a fix. The jury was justified in believing that defendant did furnish the minor with a narcotic and that it was heroin. The court concluded that the narcotic content of a substance could be proved by circumstantial evidence. Finally, the court held that the prosecution's use of the transcript of the minor's preliminary examination testimony was to refresh his recollection and was not an attempt to impeach the minor's trial testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1482 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Thain v. Palo Alto


Civ. No. 20025


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


207 Cal. App. 2d 173; 24 Cal. Rptr. 515; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1895



August 29, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 26, 1962, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 24, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. John D. Foley, Judge.

Action to determine validity of a municipal weed abatement ordinance, for refund of assessment levied thereunder against plaintiff's property, and for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city levied an assessment against appellant property owner under weed abatement ordinance. Santa Clara, Cal., Ordinance § 32.01. Property owner paid the assessment under protest. Subsequently, property owner initiated an action in the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) and challenged the ordinance on constitutional grounds. The trial court entered judgment in favor of city and property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court explained that the ordinance at issue provided that: no owner or other specified person occupying or having charge of any building, lot or premises shall permit weeds to remain on such premises or public sidewalks or streets, or alleys between said premises and the center line of any public street or alley. § 32.01. The court further explained that the ordinance allowed the city to assess a property owner for the costs of abatement, in the event the property owner failed to comply with the directive of the ordinance. §§ 32.09 - 32.09. The court held that the purpose of the ordinance was the promotion of the health, safety, and welfare of the inhabitants of the city and, as such, fell within the city's police powers. The court found that the provisions of the ordinance bore a reasonable and substantial relation to its object. Moreover, the court held that the notice provisions of the ordinance satisfied the requirements of due process. The court concluded that the ordinance was valid and constitutional, not only on its face, but also as applied to property owner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1483 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Lockheed Aircraft Corp. v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 25764


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


207 Cal. App. 2d 119; 24 Cal. Rptr. 316; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1888



August 24, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 17, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Kurtz Kauffman, Judge.

Action to obtain a refund of personal property taxes.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant County of Los Angeles (county) appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which held that plaintiff taxpayer was owed a refund of personal property taxes that had been paid to the county.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer manufactured airplanes, and it valued its inventory of partially completed airplanes by a standard costing method which estimated the average cost of manufacturing an airplane. The county's assessor was aware of the taxpayer's method of valuing its inventory when the assessor valued the taxpayer's airplane inventory. Because the airplanes in the inventory were constructed later in the building cycle, the standard costing accounting method attributed higher costs to the airplanes than those which were actually incurred. The taxpayer did not contest the assessor's valuation by appealing to the board of equalization. The lower court held that the taxpayer was entitled to a refund, and the court reversed. The court held that the taxpayer had not been assessed for nonexistent property. Rather, the court found that because the assessor was aware that the assessment he placed on the airplanes was not based upon actual costs, but was based upon estimated costs, the taxpayer's dispute with the county was a valuation issue. Therefore, the taxpayer was required to appeal to the board of equalization and exhaust its administrative remedies before it could challenge the assessment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment that the taxpayer was entitled to a refund of personal property taxes and entered judgment for the county.

Board of Trustees v. Owens


Civ. No. 10051


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


206 Cal. App. 2d 147; 23 Cal. Rptr. 710; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2003



July 26, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 20, 1962. Schottky, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted. Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 26, 1962. Schauer, J., and McComb, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Lassen County. A. K. Wylie, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to determine whether charges against a permanent teacher were sufficient grounds for his dismissal by the board of trustees of the school district.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiff reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Lassen County (California) entered a judgment that permitted respondent employer to terminate appellant employee's position as a permanent teacher on the grounds of "unprofessional conduct." The employee challenged the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a public school teacher, printed certain articles that aired his grievances regarding the educational system. The employer terminated the employee's position on the grounds of "unprofessional conduct." The trial court entered a judgment for the employer and the employee appealed. On review, the employee argued that he was unconstitutionally being punished for expressing his political ideas. The court reversed the trial court's order finding that the employee did not engage in "unprofessional conduct." The court found that the term "unprofessional conduct" was not precisely defined and that the proper question was whether the employee's actions disrupted or impaired the teaching process. The court found that the letters did not cause any disruption or impairment of discipline or the teaching process. The court also found that the employee had not violated any rule or policy by publicizing the letters.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that permitted the employer to terminate the employee's position as a permanent teacher on the grounds of "unprofessional conduct."

 

1485 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Wadley v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 25879


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


205 Cal. App. 2d 668; 23 Cal. Rptr. 154; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2180



July 16, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Robert H. Patton, Judge.

Action for personal injuries sustained by plaintiff when the motorcycle he was riding allegedly struck a defect in a county highway.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorcyclist appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in favor of defendant county in the motorcyclist's action for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: The motorcyclist was injured when his motorcycle struck a defect in a county highway. He contended that he filed a claim with the county nine months after the accident occurred. The county filed a general demurrer, which was sustained by the trial court without leave to amend, upon the grounds that the motorcyclist's claim was not filed within one hundred days after the date of the accident as required by Cal. Gov't Code §§ 710, 715. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that as the cause of action upon which the motorcyclist proceeded was based upon an alleged dangerous or defective condition of public property, it was governed by the provisions of the Public Liability Act of 1923 (Act), Cal. Gov't Code § 53050 et seq. The provisions of the Act had to be satisfied before the county could be held liable. Cal. Gov't Code §§ 710, 715 prescribed the manner in which and the time within which the motorcyclist's suit could have been filed against the county and required the filing of his written claim as a condition precedent to the filing of his suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the motorcyclist's complaint.

 

1486 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Calderon


Crim. No. 3274


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


205 Cal. App. 2d 566; 23 Cal. Rptr. 62; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2166



July 11, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 5, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County and from an order denying a new trial. James H. Oakley, Judge.

Prosecution for illegal possession of marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted him of illegally possessing marijuana after having had a prior conviction for a like offense in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11530. Defendant also challenged the superior court's order denying his request for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was court-martialed for the possession of marijuana prior to being arrested for the possession of marijuana cigarettes which were found in a shirt he was wearing. Defendant admitted that the cigarettes were marijuana, and an expert at trial testified that the cigarettes were marijuana although the expert did not state the nature of the chemical analysis that he performed. The superior court and not the jury ruled that the police had probable cause when they seized the marijuana. The superior court convicted defendant of illegally possessing marijuana and prior conviction of a like offense in violation of § 11530, and the court affirmed. The court held that the expert was not required to state the basis of his opinion unless he was requested to do so. Because defendant did not cross examine the expert, the expert's testimony was admissible and sufficient to convict defendant. The court ruled that because the probative nature of the evidence seized was not dependent upon whether the search was legal, it was the superior court's function, and not that of the jury, to determine whether there was probable cause for the search which discovered the marijuana.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's conviction of defendant for illegally possessing marijuana after having had a prior conviction of a like offense.

 

1487 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board


Civ. No. 10234


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


204 Cal. App. 2d 729; 22 Cal. Rptr. 634; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2304



June 18, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied July 17, 1962, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 15, 1962. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Fred R. Pierce, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board to reverse its decision setting aside a decision of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control suspending an on-sale beer licence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant California Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control appealed the denial by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) in favor of appellee California Alcoholic Beverage Control Appeals Board of a petition for a writ of mandamus. The Board had set aside a decision of the Department suspending an on-sale beer license held by two individuals.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Cal. Admin. Code tit. 4, § 70, the Department placed a bar on "off-limit" to military personnel. Agents of the Department requested the licensees to post two "off-limits" signs on their premises. The licensees refused to comply with the sign posting. The Department found that the licensees had violated § 70, but the board reversed. The Department then sought a writ of mandamus against the Board, but the trial court denied the writ. The court affirmed. The court held that the "off-limits" signs were akin to a badge of disrepute by which second-class status could, by official action be attached to a licensee who had never been determined in any proceeding to be guilty of any wrongdoing. There was nothing in the legislative scheme embodied in the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, or the powers vested in the Department by the California Constitution, which sanctioned the classification of licensees as the Department attempted to do in the cases under review. The means used to enforce the objective were clearly improper because they penalized a licensee by a method neither recognized by the Constitution or by statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the Department's petition for a writ of mandamus.

 

1488 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Bernstein v. Board of Medical Examiners


Civ. No. 93


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


204 Cal. App. 2d 378; 22 Cal. Rptr. 419; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2255



June 4, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 29, 1962. Conley, P. J., Deeming Himself Disqualified, did not Participate. Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 1, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Edward L. Kellas, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Board of Medical Examiners to annul its decision and order revoking plaintiff's license to practice medicine.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which denied the doctor's petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondent Board of Medical Examiners of the State of California to annul its decision and order revoking the doctor's license to practice medicine. The board revoked his license, pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 2360, 2361, 2383, after his conviction for statutory rape of a patient.


OVERVIEW: The hearing officer had made a recommendation to the Board members, who then voted based on that recommendation without a personal review of the entire record. On appeal, the court held that the decision to revoke the license was supported by substantial evidence. Although the language of Cal. Penal Code § 261.1 criminalizing statutory rape was necessarily broad in scope, and statutory rape did not, per se, involve moral turpitude, the court found that the circumstances of the doctor's offense did indicate moral turpitude and that the Board's accusation had been specific enough to give the doctor notice of the charge. The court held that the Board members were permitted, under Cal. Gov. Code § 11517(b), to vote based on the hearing officer's recommendation and that this procedure did not deny the doctor due process. The court stated that it would presume that the hearing officer had reviewed all the evidence, including the transcript of the doctor's trial, in the absence of substantial grounds indicating otherwise. The court noted that the accusation's mistaken listing of the patient's age as 15 rather than 16 was not critical, since 16 was still well below the statutory age of 18.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment, which had affirmed the Board's decision and order revoking the doctor's license to practice medicine.

Abstract Inv. Co. v. Hutchinson


Civ. No. 26220


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


204 Cal. App. 2d 242; 22 Cal. Rptr. 309; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2239



May 29, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court for the Santa Anita Judicial District. John A. H. Sturgeon, Judge.

Proceeding in unlawful detainer.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenant appealed from a judgment of the Municipal Court for the Santa Anita Judicial District (California), which found in favor of plaintiff landlord in its action for unlawful detainer. The trial court refused to consider the tenant's affirmative defenses of racial discrimination under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Cal. Const. art. I, § 13, or the Unruh Act, Cal. Civ. Code §§ 51, 52.


OVERVIEW: A landlord proceeded to evict a tenant, who claimed that the only motivation for the action was the tenant's race. The court on appeal found that the tenant raised no counterclaims or questions of title, which would have been properly barred, but raised a fundamental equitable concern under the Fourteenth Amendment and its California counterpart. The court noted that, although the alleged discriminatory action was private, any enforcement by the courts of such an eviction would constitute state action and, as such, would be prohibited by the Fourteenth Amendment. The court further noted that the landlord was operating a "business" under the Unruh Act, Cal. Civ. Code §§ 51, 52, but was not clearly operating a "business establishment" such that the act's prohibitions against private discrimination would apply. Consequently, the court found that a new trial would be necessary where those issues could be considered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the landlord and remanded the case for a new trial.

People v. Lamb


Crim. No. 6864


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


204 Cal. App. 2d 255; 22 Cal. Rptr. 284; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2240



May 29, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for Rehearings were Denied June 13, 14, and 18, 1962, and Petitions of Appellants Lamb, Dembowski, Gangwer and Rucker for Hearings by the Supreme Court were Denied July 25, 1962. Dooling, J., * Participated in Place of Traynor, J.


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying a new trial. Mark Brandler, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to violate Corp. Code, § 3020, subd. (b), to commit grand theft, cheat and defraud by criminal means and obtain money by false pretenses, and for grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from their convictions, after trial by jury in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), for conspiracy to violate Cal. Corp. Code, § 3020(b), to commit grand theft, cheat and defraud by criminal means, obtain money by false pretenses, and for grand theft. They argued that the evidence was insufficient to sustain their convictions and that they were improperly convicted on uncorroborated accomplice testimony.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that defendants were executive officers and contractors for a company engaged in wholesale distribution of drugs, liquor, and chemicals. Defendants falsely represented that work and materials had been furnished to the company. They falsified entries in the company's books, by indicating therein that improvements were made in various drugstores which in fact were not done. Defendants charged the company for services, improvements and materials from which only defendants benefited. On appeal, the court ruled that the evidence showed that the jury was warranted in finding that a conspiracy existed among defendants to cheat and defraud the company. The court ruled that the crime of conspiracy was properly proved by circumstantial evidence. The court rejected defendants' assertion that they were convicted based on the uncorroborated testimony of accomplices. The court noted that the accomplices' testimony was corroborated by company records and information from suppliers who had furnished the various improvements and materials. The court also held that the indictments were sufficient to inform defendants of the substance of the facts constituting the crime charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

People v. Coit Ranch, Inc.


Civ. No. 27


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


204 Cal. App. 2d 52; 21 Cal. Rptr. 875; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2219



May 23, 1962

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Milo Popovich, Judge.

Action to collect unpaid balances due under an assessment levied pursuant to a marketing order for cantaloupes, for civil penalties, costs and injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state and defendant farm sought review of judgments of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which entered judgments for the state, on the ground of nonexhaustion, in actions to collect unpaid portions of assessments made on the farm as a cantaloupe grower under the California Marketing Act of 1937 (Act), Cal. Agric. Code §§ 1300-10 to 1300-30, civil penalties, and court and collection costs, and for injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The farm claimed, and the trial court found, that sales promotional materials under the marketing order contained false advertising. The farm argued on appeal that the nonexhaustion doctrine was not applicable, and that the findings did not support the judgment. The state contended that the trial court erred in failing to issue a prohibitory injunction and in refusing to allow collection costs. The court determined that the farm was required to exhaust its administrative remedy before seeking judicial relief. The court did not think the findings contradictory, and determined that the finding on advertising was surplusage. The court concluded that the collection costs in dispute were not a proper item of recovery in an action brought by the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court.

Taliaferro v. Taliaferro

Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three

Action for divorce.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), which held that plaintiff wife was entitled to a sum certain upon the sale of the husband's business based upon the parties' property settlement. Additionally, the husband appealed the decision of the lower court judge not to recuse himself.


OVERVIEW: The division of property that accompanied the parties' divorce was unclear as to whether the wife was to get a sum certain when the husband merely sold his auto wrecking business or whether the wife was entitled to be paid when the husband sold both the business and the land upon which the business was operated. The husband sold essentially all of the stock of his business, but he did not sell the land.
