1493 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Northrup


Crim. No. 1702


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


203 Cal. App. 2d 470; 21 Cal. Rptr. 448; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2383



May 10, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 4, 1962, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 3, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County and from an order denying a new trial. Archie D. Mitchell, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to prepare obscene photographs.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of conviction of the crime of conspiracy by the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California) and from an order denying a new trial. He was found guilty after a jury trial. Defendant admitted to the prior convictions listed in the information.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to defendant's conviction, he argued that evidence was illegally seized and he was illegally arrested. However, the record failed to show that there was no warrant for either defendant's arrest or the search and seizure of the pornographic photographs taken from defendant's car. Where there was no evidence that the police did not have a warrant, the search and seizure and the arrest were presumed valid. The record also did not indicated that defendant objected to the admissibility of this evidence upon the grounds that it was obtained as the result of an illegal search. Defendant also contended that there was no evidence that he and his brother agreed to prepare lewd and obscene photographs, which led to the charge of conspiracy. The court noted that a conspiracy was usually proven only be circumstantial evidence and it was not necessary to prove an actual agreement to work together to perform the unlawful acts charged. The only proof available could have resulted from actions of the parties, which manifested an intent to carry out a common purpose to violate the law. Furthermore, it was sufficient that only one of the conspirators accomplished the overt act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant.

 

1494 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Alta Bldg. Material Co. v. Cameron


Civ. No. 20465


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


202 Cal. App. 2d 299; 20 Cal. Rptr. 713; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2478



April 11, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Municipal Court for the Oakland-Piedmont Judicial District. Lyle E. Cook, Judge.

Action to foreclose a claim of lien for materials furnished to a plastering contractor and used by him on defendants' real property.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owners appealed a decision from the Municipal Court for the Oakland-Piedmont Judicial District (California), entering judgment in favor of plaintiff supplier in its action to foreclose a claim of lien. The trial court also held that the pre-lien notice requirement found in Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1193 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owners hired the plastering contractor. The supplier provided the plastering contractor with materials. The supplier initiated an action against the owners to foreclose its lien. The owners alleged that the claim was invalid because the supplier did not give notice as required under § 1193. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the supplier. In reversing the decision, the court held that the notice requirement was constitutional. The section did not violate the constitutional prohibition against the impairing of liens because the requirement notice was a procedural matter. Such a requirement affected only the manner in which the right was to be enforced. The legislature did not act arbitrarily and unreasonably in making the classification in the statute between: (1) those who were either under direct contract with the owner or performing actual labor for wages; and (2) all others. Pre-lien notice was not required by those who were under direct contract with the owners because the owners would be apprised of potential claims by way of lien. All others were required to give pre-lien notice because the owners would not have knowledge of their potential claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision with directions to the trial court to enter judgment in favor of the owners. The court also held that the notice requirement contained in § 1193 was constitutional.

 

1495 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Dunham v. Westminster


Civ. No. 6685


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


202 Cal. App. 2d 245; 20 Cal. Rptr. 772; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2469



April 6, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 1, 1962, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 29, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Raymond Thompson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the issuance of a building permit and for declaratory relief.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment granting writ, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which granted the issuance of a peremptory writ of mandate to compel the issuance of a building permit sought by respondent landowner. The town contended that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to hear the matter relating to the constitutionality of a zoning ordinance because the landowner had not exhausted his administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's property was in an area zoned for general business purposes. The town repeatedly turned down his request for a building permit because he refused to dedicate the front of his lot to the town for street purposes, pursuant to Westminster City Code § 8200.20(C).26. Rather than seeking a variance provided by that law, the landowner filed an action for writ of mandate and for declaratory relief, contending that the ordinance was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's award of a peremptory writ because the landowner was precluded from seeking judicial relief until he had exhausted his administrative remedies. The court held that rule in California was that the trial court had no jurisdiction to entertain an action for judicial relief until completion of the available administrative procedure. The rule applied even when the administrative rule was challenged on constitutional grounds and even if the action was for declaratory relief. Once the landowner had exhausted his administrative remedies by seeking a variance and following that process through the administrative remedies provided, he could challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision to grant a peremptory writ of mandate compelling the town to issue the building permit sought by the landowner.

 

1496 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Fleischer v. Adult Authority


Civ. No. 10368


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


202 Cal. App. 2d 44; 20 Cal. Rptr. 603; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2442



March 30, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Albert H. Mundt, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition seeking a court hearing to review actions taken by the Adult Authority.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of prohibition, seeking a court hearing to review the actions taken by respondent Adult Authority in fixing his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner brought the proceeding in prohibition, seeking a court hearing to review the actions taken by the Authority in fixing his sentence. The appeal was from an order of the superior court denying the prisoner's petition for a writ of prohibition. The court found that the prisoner's contention, that he was entitled to notice and hearing before the Authority could redetermine his sentence, was devoid of merit. The absence of a requirement for notice and a hearing did not violate due process because such was given in the proceedings, which resulted in the prisoner's original trial. The prisoner's petition failed to allege any facts disclosing that the Authority abused its discretion in its actions. Because the Authority did not exercise a judicial function, a writ of prohibition could not issue against it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order denying the prisoner's writ of prohibition to review the Authority's actions in fixing his sentence.

 

1497 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Mosk v. National Research Co.


Civ. No. 10191


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


201 Cal. App. 2d 765; 20 Cal. Rptr. 516; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2657; 133 U.S.P.Q. (BNA) 413



March 26, 1962  
March 26, 1962


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Stanley W. Reckers, Judge.

Action to restrain defendants from continuing certain business practices alleged to be unfair, deceptive and fraudulent.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County, which granted a permanent injunction in respondent attorney general's suit to restrain appellants from continuing certain business practices alleged to be unfair, deceptive and fraudulent under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 3369.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sent forms to consumers in attempt to collect information on delinquent debtors. Respondent attorney general alleged that these business practices were unfair, deceptive, and fraudulent under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 3369. Respondent sued to obtain a permanent injunction to restrain appellants from continuing the practice. After the trial court granted the injunction, appellants sought review. On appeal, the court said that equitable relief under the statute was not circumscribed by any prerequisite showing that the conduct was limited to business competition. The terms of the statute showed a legislative intent to be inclusive rather than restrictive in practices to be enjoined. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the trial court neither abused nor exceeded its discretion in determining the type of relief necessary under the facts as found to exist. The court said that the record, including numerous exhibits, convinced the court that the trial court's findings were amply supported.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the trial court neither abused nor exceeded its discretion in determining the type of relief necessary under the facts as found to exist.

 

1498 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Harmon v. Pacific Tel. & Tel. Co.


Civ. No. 25333


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


201 Cal. App. 2d 453; 20 Cal. Rptr. 118; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2613



March 16, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County denying motion to tax costs. Philbrick McCoy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff customer appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denying the motion to tax costs, in which the customer sought to eliminate the cost of printing defendant telephone company's appellate brief.


OVERVIEW: The customer brought the action for declaratory relief involving the telephone company's policy of charging for "message units" without identifying the calls. The case was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction because and that judgment was affirmed upon appeal. The telephone company was awarded costs under Cal. R. Ct. 26, and requested reimbursement for the cost of printing its appellate brief. The customer appealed from the superior court's denial of the motion to eliminate that cost. The court held that the telephone company, the prevailing party, was entitled to the reasonable cost of printing or reproduction of briefs under Rule 26. The fact that the document could have been printed less expensively was not controlling; the rule required only that the telephone company incur the cost and that the cost be deemed reasonable. The court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to support the superior court determination regarding the reasonableness of the cost of printing the appellate brief. The court also ruled that the telephone company was the prevailing party within the meaning of Rule 26 and that costs properly were awarded. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying the customer's motion to tax costs in order to disallow the telephone company's cost of printing its appellate brief.

 

1499 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Henry v. Los Angeles


Civ. Nos. 25188, 25189, 25190, 25191, 25192


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


201 Cal. App. 2d 299; 20 Cal. Rptr. 440; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2595



March 14, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions by Plaintiffs and Appellants for a Rehearing in Civ. No. 25189, Civ. No. 25190, Civ. No. 25191, and Civ. No. 25192 were Denied March 28, 1962, and Petitions by Plaintiffs and Appellants for a Hearing by the Supreme Court in Civ. No. 25189, Civ. No. 25190, Civ. No. 25191 and Civ. No. 25192 were Denied May 16, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Clyde C. Triplett, Judge.

Actions by retired fire and police department pensioners and widows of pensioners against a city and its board of pension commissioners to determine pension rights and benefits and constitutionality of charter amendments affecting them.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments determining pension rights and recovery of unpaid benefits and declaring charter amendments unconstitutional, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the City of Los Angeles, and the city board of pension commissioners (collectively, the City), appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which determined that certain charter amendments were unconstitutional as applied to retired fire and police department pensioners and widows of pensioners. Certain pensioners also appealed portions of the underlying judgments.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court heard the five consolidated cases brought by fire and police department pensioners and widows of pensioners in regard to the constitutionality of certain charter amendments to the terms of the pension programs. The City appealed the decision that two amendments were unconstitutional in that they curtailed the ability of the pensioners to receive a "fluctuating" rather than a "fixed" pension. A number of pensioners also filed appeals of the trial court's decision in their cases. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the charter amendments were unconstitutional and the trial court's decision regarding determination of pension rights and recovery of unpaid benefits. However, the appellate court did find that the City was not equitably estopped from limiting recovery of unpaid benefits to a period of six-months prior to pensioners' filing of their complaints. The appellate court further found that charter amendments that altered the benefits of pensioners to their detriment without any corresponding benefit were unconstitutional, including provisions aimed at altering the eligibility of widows of pensioners to receive benefits.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The appellate court also awarded costs to the pensioners on their appeals.

 

1500 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Eaton v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 25332


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


201 Cal. App. 2d 326; 20 Cal. Rptr. 456; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2596



March 14, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 28, 1962, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 16, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Emmett E. Doherty, Judge.

Action by retired police and fire department pensioners against a city and its board of pension commissioners to determine pension rights and benefits and to have city charter amendments affecting them declared unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions. Judgment determining pension rights and past benefits recoverable and declaring amendments to be constitutional, affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and board of pension commissioners, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered judgment against the commissioners in an action brought by plaintiffs, retired police and fire department employees, for a declaratory judgment to determine plaintiffs' pension rights and benefits and to recover past due pension benefits.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were former employees of the city. Plaintiffs claimed that they were entitled to receive a fluctuating pension in lieu of the fixed pension. Plaintiffs brought a declaratory judgment action to determine their past and future pension rights. The trial court entered a judgment against the commissioners. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that pensions were not a trust and that the city pension fund, unlike an ordinary trust, could never be permanently exhausted and thus terminated. The court held that amendments to the city charter did not create fluctuating pensions to which all plaintiffs were entitled. The court affirmed the trial court's formula for computing fixed pensions. The court held that if by application of the formula a benefit resulted to a plaintiff then such benefit should be accorded to the plaintiff, but if it results in a detriment then the formula may not be applied to such plaintiff. The court held that the trial court erred in entering judgment solely against the commissioners because the obligation to pay pensions was an obligation imposed by law upon the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's formula for computing fixed pensions. The court reversed the judgment against the commissioners and entered judgment against the city. The court remanded for further proceedings.

 

1501 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Atwell v. Los Angeles


Civ. Nos. 25400, 25401, 25402


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


201 Cal. App. 2d 336; 20 Cal. Rptr. 462; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2597



March 14, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions by Plaintiffs for a Rehearing in Civ. No. 25401 and Civ. No. 25402 were Denied March 28, 1962 and Petitions by Plaintiffs for a Hearing by the Supreme Court in Civ. No. 25401 and Civ. No. 25402 were Denied May 16, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Joseph W. Vickers, Judge.

Actions by retired fire and police department pensioners and widows of pensioners against a city and its board of pension commissioners to determine pension rights and benefits and to have city charter amendments affecting them declared unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions. Judgments determining rights and recovery of unpaid benefits and declaring charter amendments unconstitutional, except as to one plaintiff, affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, retired fire and police department pensioners and widows of the pensioners, brought an action against defendants, a city and its board of pension commissioners, to determine pension rights. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) held that a 1925 amendment was unconstitutional, that each widow was entitled to receive a fluctuating pension, and that defendants were estopped to urge defense of the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue involved in all three cases was whether a July 1, 1925, amendment to the city charter relating to eligibility for widows' pensions, which provided that in order to be eligible for a pension a widow had to have been married to her deceased pensioner husband at least one year prior to the date of his retirement instead of for one year prior to the date of his death as had been provided in the charter prior to 1925. Defendants contended that the 1925 modification of the eligibility provisions of the city charter was not unreasonable as to any member or widow. The court held that the widows who had not successfully established status as pensioners within three years from the date their causes of action accrued (the dates of death of their husbands) were barred from asserting such claims by the statute of limitations. In one case, a widow and her deceased husband were not in a position to challenge the constitutionality of the 1925 charter amendments because the husband had suffered a break in his period of service with the city and his pension rights were therefore governed by the charter provisions as they existed at the time of his reemployment by the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments determining the rights and recovery of unpaid benefits and declaring the charter amendments unconstitutional, except as to one widow.

Monterey County Flood Control & Water Conservation Dist. v. Hughes


Civ. No. 24640


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


201 Cal. App. 2d 197; 20 Cal. Rptr. 252; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2581



March 12, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 9, 1962.

* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action in eminent domain to condemn property for a dam and reservoir.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Interlocutory and final judgments of condemnation and fixing monetary damages, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a flood control and water conservation district, brought an action in eminent domain against defendants to condemn property for a dam and reservoir. Defendants sought review from a decision of the Superior Court of San Luis Obispo County (California), which entered interlocutory and final judgments in favor of plaintiff and fixed the monetary damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a flood control and water conservation district, brought an action in eminent domain against defendant to condemn property for a dam and reservoir. The trial court entered interlocutory and final judgments in favor of plaintiff and fixed the monetary damages. On appeal, the court concluded that beneficial and useful purposes of flood and water conservation included recreational uses. Further, the court concluded that the Monterey County Flood Control and Water Conservation District Act (Act), 1947 Cal. Stat. 699, as it stood when the action was commenced, authorized and empowered plaintiff to condemn property for such recreational uses, particularly as incidental to a project for flood control and water conservation. The court held that the findings, conclusion, and judgment of the trial court, asserting that plaintiff had the authority to condemn defendants' property for recreational uses, were fully supported by the evidence and were correct in law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court.

 

1503 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Velarde


Crim. No. 1597


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


201 Cal. App. 2d 231; 19 Cal. Rptr. 832; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2584



March 12, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Raymond Thompson, Judge.

Prosecution for kidnapping for purpose of robbery and for armed robbery.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed in part and reversed in part. Judgment of conviction modified and affirmed as to kidnapping counts and reversed as to robbery counts.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which following a jury verdict convicted defendant of two counts of kidnapping for purpose of robbery and two counts of first degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction on several grounds. The court dismissed with little discussion defendant's claim that Cal. Penal Code § 209 was unconstitutional but agreed with defendant that the counts of the indictment charging kidnapping for the purpose of robbery were not separate crimes from the robbery counts. The court held that defendant's acts of kidnapping, in which he moved two store employees from one room to another where he tied them up, were incidental to the underlying robbery. Consequently, the court held that imposing a sentence for the kidnappings in addition to the robbery was a double punishment in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 654. Therefore, defendant could be charged and sentenced on the more serious offenses of kidnapping for the purpose of robbery, but not on the robbery counts. The court also agreed with defendant that because defendant was given straight life imprisonment on the kidnapping charges, all other sentences for other crimes, either from before or after, had to be concurrent as required by Cal. Penal Code § 669.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction on the two robbery counts of the indictment and modified the sentences on the kidnapping counts of the indictment so that they were served concurrently with the sentences on other offenses. As modified, the court affirmed the judgments on the kidnapping counts.

House of Seagram, Inc. v. M.C.F., Inc.


Civ. No. 19863


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


200 Cal. App. 2d 774; 19 Cal. Rptr. 646; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2771

Action to enjoin a retail liquor store from selling plaintiff's brands of distilled spirits at below the fair trade prices set by plaintiff.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to complaint was sustained without leave to amend, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an alcoholic beverage producer, appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which denied its action to enjoin defendant retailer from selling the producer's brands of distilled spirits at below fair trade prices set by the producer.


OVERVIEW: When the retailer allegedly sold the producer's brands of alcoholic beverages at below fair trade prices, the producer sought an injunction. The trial court sustained the retailer's demurrer on the ground that the complaint stated a purported cause of action that was unconstitutional under the California Constitution and under the United States Constitution. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the cause. The court held that the fair trade prices were properly set pursuant to the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 24755-24757, which had previously been upheld as constitutional by the Supreme Court of California. Therefore, the producer's action clearly stated a cause of action under California law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

1505 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


San Diego v. Otay Municipal Water Dist.


Civ. No. 6704


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


200 Cal. App. 2d 672; 19 Cal. Rptr. 595; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2760



February 23, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Petition of Defendants and Appellants for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 18, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County and from an order denying a new trial. C. M. Monroe, Judge.

Action by a city to enjoin a municipal water district from operating a water system in and furnishing water to inhabitants of the city.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified and affirmed; appeal from order dismissed. Judgment for plaintiff modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of San Diego brought an action to enjoin defendant water district from operating a water system in and furnishing water to city inhabitants. Intervenor landowners sought a declaration that proceedings taken by the water district were invalid. The Superior Court of San Diego County (California) granted the city's requested relief and did not rule on the issue raised by the intervenors. The water district and intervenors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The water district issued bonds for construction of a system to furnish water within an improvement district, which included 4,000 acres that were annexed to the city. The city brought an action to prevent the water district from furnishing water to the inhabitants of the annexed area and from constructing a water distribution system within that area for that purpose. The trial court enjoined the water district's operation of any water works within the city's territory without its consent and enjoined the issuance of bonds for such purpose. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part, finding the water district's authority over territory annexed by the city was limited by the city's charter, which required the city's consent before a corporation could operate works for supplying water to the city's inhabitants. However, the charter provision did not control the authority of the water district to issue bonds for the construction of water facilities. Further, the validity of the bond issue could only be attacked by an elector or taxpayer of the district. The contentions of the intervenors exceeded the scope of the remedy sought by the city and could not be considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as modified, striking only the portion of the judgment that enjoined the water district from issuing bonds for the construction of the water works without the city's consent. The court dismissed the intervenors' appeal.

Whitson v. Long Beach


Civ. No. 25008


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


200 Cal. App. 2d 486; 19 Cal. Rptr. 668; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2737



February 20, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. John F. McCarthy, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief as to the validity of dispositions of moneys derived by a city from the sale of oil and gas produced from certain lands and as to rights under, and validity of, a municipal contract, and for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal, entered after demurrers of certain defendants to second amended complaint were sustained, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California). Plaintiff appealed from a judgment of dismissal entered after demurrers of defendants State of California, City of Long Beach, company, and other officials. The several complaints filed by plaintiff were concerned to a large extent with the respective rights of the parties in the oil and gas revenue from tidelands and submerged lands.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sustained the demurrer of defendants City of Long Beach and its auditor to the first cause of action with leave to amend; it was sustained as to all other causes of action without leave to amend because of multiple misjoinders of causes of action. The demurrer of defendant company was sustained as to all causes of action without leave to amend. The demurrer of defendant State of California was sustained as to the first cause of action with leave to amend and as to the remaining causes of action without leave to amend. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court because the misjoinders of causes of action was a sufficient ground upon which to predicate a refusal of leave to amend. The court found that the decision to deny plaintiff leave to amend was almost entirely within the discretion of the trial court and found that there was not a manifest abuse of discretion in giving final judgment on demurrer without leave to amend. In the present case, the final pleading of plaintiff was the third amended complaint. It was, therefore, the fourth attempt to state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal after the demurrers of defendants were sustained without leave to amend.

Wanamaker v. City Council of El Monte


Civ. No. 25329


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


200 Cal. App. 2d 453; 19 Cal. Rptr. 554; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2732



February 19, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Gordon L. Files, Judge.

Action to have a zoning ordinance declared invalid.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to first amended complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed his action against respondent city officials after a demurrer to the owners' first amended complaint in a zoning dispute, as amended, was sustained without leave to amend.


OVERVIEW: The officials enacted a resolution that proposed to repeal El Monte, Cal., Ordinance No. 252, which was a comprehensive zoning ordinance, after notice in accordance with applicable law. The officials subsequently enacted a new zoning ordinance, which placed a portion of the owners' property in a zone that prohibited its use for the purposes for which it had been acquired. The owners challenged the zoning change on the ground that it was an unconstitutional taking. They contended that Cal. Gov't Code § 65805 required notice by mail rather than by publication. The trial court sustained the officials' demurrer to the owners' first amended complaint and dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed because the owners received notice by publication as prescribed Cal. Gov't Code § 65803, which was applicable to the adoption of a new zoning ordinance. That notice was sufficient to meet the requirements of due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

 

1508 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. Transit Authority of Sacramento


Civ. No. 10121


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


199 Cal. App. 2d 716; 19 Cal. Rptr. 59; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2887; 50 L.R.R.M. 2025



January 31, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Fred R. Pierce, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief as to inclusion of an arbitration clause in a collective bargaining agreement.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying relief, after demurrer to complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, union and union officials, filed a declaratory action against defendant city transit authority for a determination of whether an arbitration clause could be included in a collective bargaining agreement. The Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) sustained the city transit authority's general demurrer and denied the union and union officials' motion for leave to amend the complaint. The union and union officials appealed.


OVERVIEW: The union and union officials alleged the existence of a justiciable controversy within the purview of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1060. The court disagreed with the claims of the union and union officials. The court analyzed the trial court's decision under the alternative theories that the trial court refused to exercise its power of declaratory relief pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1061, or that the complaint failed to show an actual controversy involving a justiciable question. The court held that it was not reversible error per se to refuse declaratory relief by an order sustaining a general demurrer without leave to amend. Further, the court concluded that the union and union officials' complaint failed to state a justiciable controversy. No allegation was made that at the time of the filing of the action there was any unsettled grievance or other controversy pending under the existing contract. On the contrary, the alleged difficulty concerned a provision not in the contract, and about the legality of which there was a difference of opinion among counsel for the parties. The court ruled that the union and union officials sought an advisory opinion on a question of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Gelini v. San Francisco


Civ. No. 19295


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


199 Cal. App. 2d 340; 18 Cal. Rptr. 853; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2837



January 22, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Ben R. Ragain, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for damages for personal injuries arising out of a collision of a cable car and a taxicab.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxi driver appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) entered in favor of defendant cable car operator in a personal injury action arising from a collision between the cable car and the taxi, contending that, as a matter of law, the operator was negligent, and the driver was not contributorily negligent when a pedestrian was injured.


OVERVIEW: The taxi and the cable car were both proceeding south when, in response to a red traffic light, the driver stopped his taxi north of the north crosswalk for pedestrians. When the traffic light changed from red to green, the driver remained stopped while pedestrians were crossing. The cable car struck the rear end of the taxi and knocked it ahead into a pedestrian. At the jury trial, the court entered a verdict for the operator. On appeal, the court held that it was a question of fact as to whether the driver should have proceeded when the traffic light changed to green. It was undoubtedly a judgment call, but the court found that there was substantial evidence upon which to base a finding of contributory negligence by the driver. Therefore, the court affirmed that the question was one of fact that was properly left to the jury to determine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the operator, sustaining the jury's finding that the driver was contributorily negligent.

 

1510 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Burbank v. Nordahl


Civ. No. 6604


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


199 Cal. App. 2d 311; 18 Cal. Rptr. 710; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 2835



January 19, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County and from orders striking plaintiff's cost bill, taxing defendants' costs and directing payment of funds on deposit. Raymond Thompson, Judge.

Proceeding in eminent domain.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions; orders striking cost bill and taxing costs, affirmed; other order reversed. Judgment of condemnation affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which determined that the value of the property taken from defendant property owners in an eminent domain action was $ 260,000. The city also challenged an order that denied its motion to be relieved of a stipulation that it would pay taxes and penalties levied against the property.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an eminent domain action to acquire property. The trial court initially entered a judgment decreeing condemnation and awarded the property owners $ 237,779. The city subsequently deposited the amount awarded with the trial court. The property owners filed a motion for new trial alleging that the amount of the judgment was insufficient. The trial court then vacated the judgment and awarded the property owners $ 260,000. Upon review, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part. The court determined that the property owners were improperly awarded interest above the amount allowable under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1254 where they were only entitled to receive compensation from the date that possession of the property was given to the city until the date of the judgment. The court found that the property owners could not obtain both the use of money deposited by the city and interest on the compensation and damages awarded. The court concluded the city was bound by a stipulation that it would pay a tax and a penalty where the stipulation was not unlawful under Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 2921.5 and the property owners had relied upon the stipulation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that determined the value of the property taken from the property owners in an eminent domain action was $ 260,000. The court affirmed part of a judgment that denied the city's motion to be relieved of a stipulation that it would pay taxes and penalties levied against the property.

 

1511 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Buzard v. Justice Court for Atwater Judicial Dist.


Civ. No. 51


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


198 Cal. App. 2d 814; 18 Cal. Rptr. 348; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1472



January 8, 1962 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Merced County denying a writ of prohibition. R. R. Sischo, Judge.

Proceeding in prohibition to restrain the Justice Court for the Atwater Judicial District from proceeding with a trial.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Order denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner military serviceman appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Merced County (California), which denied his request for a writ of prohibition to restrain respondent Justice Court for the Atwater Judicial District from proceeding with a trial on charges that he failed to register a car as required by Cal. Veh. Code § 4000.


OVERVIEW: The serviceman alleged that § 4000 was unconstitutional in that it required him to pay a license fee to register his car. He argued that Cal. Veh. Code § 6700 et seq. exempted certain military personnel from registration, but not those in his classification, rendering Cal Veh. Code § 4000 unconstitutional as to him. The statute barred anyone from driving on a highway unless the vehicle was registered and the appropriate fees had been paid. The court found that the registration of motor vehicles operated for the purpose of protecting innocent purchasers against fraud, to provide identification in case of an accident, and as a deterrent to theft. The serviceman had not attempted to register his vehicle and thus, was not asked to pay the disputed fee. The court would not prejudge the action of the trial court. It held that if the lower court decided that the serviceman was required to pay a fee pursuant to Cal Rev. & Tax. Code § 10751 and Cal. Veh. Code §§ 6700, 6701 and 6705, he had an adequate remedy to challenge the statute by way of appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision denying a writ of prohibition.

 

1512 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


U. S. Industries, Inc. v. State Board of Equalization


Civ. No. 25175


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


198 Cal. App. 2d 775; 18 Cal. Rptr. 171; 1962 Cal. App. LEXIS 1468



January 8, 1962 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 5, 1962, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 7, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Burnett Wolfson, Judge.

Action for refund of sales tax payment.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, buyer corporation and three selling corporations, appealed an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a judgment for defendant State Board of Equalization in plaintiffs' action for a refund of sales taxes paid on the sales of the entire manufacturing businesses of the selling corporations to the buyer corporation. The trial court held that the sales were not occasional sales exempted from tax.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff buyer corporation acquired the entire manufacturing businesses of plaintiff selling corporations. Each selling corporation held a seller's permit as a retailer selling manufactured goods. Buyer corporation paid sales taxes on its purchase of all of the machinery, furniture, and other items owned by the selling corporations, who then held small minority interests in the buyer corporation. Plaintiffs filed an action for refund of sales taxes under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 6933, claiming that the liquidation sales were occasional and irregular sales not in the regular course of business. Defendant State Board of Equalization (Board) denied the claim for refunds. The trial court determined that the Board properly assessed and collected taxes upon each of the retail sales in question. On appeal, the court affirmed. The sales of the entire businesses were not occasional sales pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 6006.5 because there was no affiliation between the corporations prior to the sales and the ownership of the property changed after the sales. The court rejected plaintiffs' arguments that the sales taxes were unconstitutional violations of their due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that defendant State Board of Equalization properly denied plaintiffs' request for a refund of sales tax payments paid in the acquisition of the entire manufacturing businesses of three selling corporations.

 

1513 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Skyline Materials, Inc. v. Belmont


Civ. No. 19243


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Three


198 Cal. App. 2d 449; 18 Cal. Rptr. 95; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2561



December 26, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 23, 1962, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 21, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Arthur L. Mundo, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to enjoin a city and its officials from enforcing an ordinance establishing a maximum gross weight for vehicles using a city street.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment for plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) that enjoined it from enforcing an ordinance that established a maximum gross weight of eight tons for vehicles using a certain part of a certain road. The ordinance had been amended to provide for an exemption for hauling earthen materials.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that limited to 13 tons the gross weight of any vehicle using a certain avenue; it was amended, inter alia, to reduce the weight limit to 8 tons. The corporation, which leased and operated a quarry, brought the matter into the trial court, and it enjoined the city from enforcing the ordinance. The city appealed, and the court reversed the judgment and directed entry of judgment for the city. The ordinance could not be set aside unless it had no reasonable relation to the public welfare or unless the physical facts showed that there had been an unreasonable, oppressive, or unwarranted interference with property rights by using police power. The court found that there was testimony that the use of the avenue by trucks of a certain weight would cause early breakdown of it and that heavy trucks created a hazard for the many schools located nearby. The evidence proving the justification of the ordinance was fairly debatable. Thus, the trial court's findings that there would be no unreasonable damage or unreasonable traffic hazard could not be upheld. Its conclusion that the alternate route for the corporation was not adequate could also not be sustained.


OUTCOME: Ruling against the corporation, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and directed it to enter a judgment in favor of the city. However, the court declared that the amendment of the ordinance to exempt movement of earthen material was unconstitutional.

 

1514 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Atherton v. Templeton


Civ. No. 19830


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


198 Cal. App. 2d 146; 17 Cal. Rptr. 680; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2519



December 19, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 18, 1962, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 14, 1962. Schauer, J., and Peters, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Wayne R. Millington, Judge.

Action to enjoin use of a tennis court constructed in defendants' front yard and to require removal of such structure.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which granted plaintiff town's motion to enjoin the owners from using or maintaining the sides and backstops of a tennis court located in their front yard and further ordered them to remove the structure.


OVERVIEW: The owners filed an application with the town for a variance from Atherton, Cal., Zoning Regs. § 11-3 so that they could erect a tennis court in their front yard, and upon the denial of the application, the owners constructed the tennis court. After the owners were ordered to remove the tennis court backdrops and sides, the owners claimed that the ordinance was unconstitutional and that the court fence did not constitute a structure. The court affirmed the order of injunction and held that (1) because § 11-3 was intended be interpreted to allow for the broadest possible construction, it was clear that the tennis court fencing constituted a structure; (2) the regulation was not unconstitutional because it could have been argued that the elimination of accessory structures from front yards would add to the attractiveness and comfort of a residential district and aid in traffic safety by affording a better view of street corners; and (3) the owners were not entitled to a variance simply because they did not have room to build a tennis court in their backyard because the evidence showed that the owners sold most of their backyard property; thus, they created the limit themselves.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1515 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


Crim. No. 7622


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


198 Cal. App. 2d 232; 17 Cal. Rptr. 789; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2532



December 19, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. J. Howard Ziemann, Judge.

Prosecution for petty theft following a prior conviction of a felony.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed their convictions from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for petty theft in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 667, with a prior conviction of a felony. Defendants contended that the superior court had lost jurisdiction to sentence them because the statute of limitations barred prosecution of the offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendants pled guilty to the offense of petty theft, with a prior felony conviction. The superior court denied probation and defendants were sentenced to a term in State prison not exceeding five years. The court affirmed defendants' convictions and concluded that the informations were timely filed within three years after the commission of the crime as required by Cal. Penal Code § 800. As such, the superior court did not lose jurisdiction to sentence defendants since the statute of limitations did not bar the prosecution of the offenses. The court ruled that defendants were fully advised of their constitutional rights by the trial judge and their owner counsel and freely and voluntarily entered pleas of guilty and admitted the prior convictions as alleged in the consolidated information. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 667 was not unconstitutional on the theory that it provided for cruel, unusual, or excessive punishment since the statute did not result in punishing defendants twice for the same offense. The additional penalty was considered punishment for the previous offense, and the statute did not subject defendants to involuntary servitude on account of their status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgments of conviction and sentences imposed against defendants for petty theft with a prior conviction of a felony.

 

1516 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Muir v. Steinberg


Civ. No. 31


Court of Appeal of California, Fifth Appellate District


197 Cal. App. 2d 264; 17 Cal. Rptr. 431; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1342



November 22, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied December 21, 1961, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 17, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Robert B. Lambert, Judge.

Election contest.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment of dismissal reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contestant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which, after a recount, dismissed the proceeding brought by the contestant challenging an election. The superior court found that Cal. Water Code § 21706 (1961) afforded the only remedy to correct any mistake in vote counting. The contestant brought the action against defendant contestee pursuant to Cal. Elec. Code § 8511(e).


OVERVIEW: The parties ran against each other for an elected office and the contestee was declared elected. Pursuant to Cal. Elec. Code § 8511(e), which was part of Cal. Elec. Code div. 10, ch. 2, the contestant challenged the election and a recount was held. The recount resulted in the contestant receiving more votes than the contestee. The superior court dismissed the contestant's action for lack of jurisdiction. On appeal, the court reversed the dismissal and directed the superior court to annul the declared election of the contestee and determine that the contestant was elected to the office. The court held that Cal. Water Code §§ 21735 and 21706 afforded alternative remedies for an election challenge and were not interdependent. The court held that Cal. Water Code § 21735 was constitutional. The phrase in § 21735 that an election could be contested "as nearly as practicable" in the manner provided in Cal. Elec. Code. div. 10, ch. 2, was not unreasonably indefinite or uncertain. The trial court had properly eliminated certain votes for the contestee and allowed certain votes for the contestant in the recount.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of dismissal. The court ordered the superior court to enter a judgment annulling and setting aside the declared election of the contestee and determining that the contestant was elected to the office.

 

1517 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. McGaughran


Crim. No. 3907


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


197 Cal. App. 2d 6; 17 Cal. Rptr. 121; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1304



November 15, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 9, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco and from an order denying a new trial. Francis McCarty, Judge.

Prosecution for attempted statutory rape.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which convicted him of attempted rape of a female under 18 years of age.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted rape of a female under 18 years of age. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that defendant was properly sentenced to state prison by the trial court under Cal. Penal Code § 664 for attempted rape. Cal. Penal Code § 264 did not require the place of punishment be fixed by the jury. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant. Although the victim's testimony was conflicting, a portion of her testimony showed that defendant attempted to have intercourse with her. The defendant's niece testified that defendant was with the victim, and there was a positive showing of the vaginal smear for sperm. The court ruled that defendant's intent was proven by the victim's testimony that defendant put his private parts next to hers and that her panties were wet after defendant was finished, and by the finding of sperm. The court ruled that the trial court's failure to instruct of its own motion that the oral admissions of a party should be viewed with caution would not have changed the verdict. There was no miscarriage of justice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's judgment of conviction of attempted rape of a female under 18 years of age.

 

1518 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Church of the Brethren v. Pasadena


Civ. Nos. 25120, 25121


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Four


196 Cal. App. 2d 814; 17 Cal. Rptr. 30; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1650



November 14, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 9, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Kenneth C. Newell, Judge.

Actions for declaratory relief entitling churches to a refund or cancellation of city taxes on real property.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) held that Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 262 was constitutional and that plaintiff churches were entitled to a refund of real property taxes and the return of their property that was confiscated for failure to pay taxes. Defendant city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The two churches each failed to file an affidavit of exemption from taxation and were assessed real property taxes. One church paid the taxes and filed an application for a refund pursuant to Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 262. The other church did not pay the levied taxes. After their property was sold for delinquent taxes, the church requested an exemption. The city alleged that § 262 was unconstitutional because it was retroactive and that return of the levied taxes and the confiscated property constituted an unlawful gift of public funds to religious organizations. The court affirmed the trial court and held that the legislature was authorized to retroactively reverse its prior legislation. Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 1 1/2 granted an exemption from taxation for church property. The withdrawal of the affidavit requirement was carrying out the constitutional mandate. The practical effect of Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 262 was to regard the levy or collection procedures as erroneous. The refund of taxes or property was not an appropriation or payment of "public" funds to a religious organization but merely a return of church property to the rightful owners.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that held that the legislature properly exercised its authority to cancel the waiver provisions for exempt church property and that the churches were entitled to a refund of real property taxes and return of their property.

People v. Vaughn


Crim. No. 7528


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


196 Cal. App. 2d 622; 16 Cal. Rptr. 711; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1620



November 1, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 21, 1961, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 9, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. Julian Beck, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to falsely personate another person and for having falsely personated such person.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to falsely personate another person and of having falsely personated that person. He appealed that judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) and its order denying a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant represented a woman who was arrested on a charge of possessing marijuana. At trial, he directed the woman to sit in the courtroom while her twin sister posed as the woman at the counsel table. After the hearing an officer arrested the twin sister for a traffic warrant under the mistaken belief that she was the woman. Defendant advised the twin sister to continue pose as her sister and that he would have her released from jail within minutes. Defendant alleged that the evidence did not establish a violation of Cal. Penal Code 529 or a conspiracy to commit the impersonation offense because the sister who was impersonated did not suffer a material pecuniary harm or liability and neither was there a pecuniary gain or tangible advantage to the impersonating sister or another. The court held that the statute was explicit and that it covered any benefit that may have accrued to the sister who was impersonated. The deception could have resulted in her escaping a prison term for the alleged offense of possessing marijuana. There was sufficient evidence of an agreement between the twin sister and defendant to sustain a conspiracy conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the order denying a new trial.

In re Schillaci


Crim. No. 7930


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


196 Cal. App. 2d 591; 16 Cal. Rptr. 757; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1617



October 31, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus upon the grounds that he was unlawfully restrained after his conviction for conspiracy to violate Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 600.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered a plea of guilty to a charge of conspiracy to violate Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 600. That statute prohibited the exhibition and distribution, except through designated state agencies, of all printed matter relating to venereal disease and related subjects. Petitioner's one-year jail sentence was suspended, and he was placed on probation for three years. Subsequently, petitioner was held in contempt for violating the conditions of his probation, and he was sentenced to serve 21 days in jail. He then filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking release from custody on the grounds that § 600 was unconstitutional. In granting the writ, the court held that § 600 was unconstitutional because it infringed upon constitutional guarantees of freedom of speech and press. The court also ruled that the statute constituted a delegation of power to an administrative agency that was not restricted by adequate standards. Thus, because Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 600 was unconstitutional, petitioner's conviction was void, and he was ordered discharged from custody.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ.

 

1521 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Lynch Meats of Oakland v. Oakland


Civ. No. 19417


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


196 Cal. App. 2d 104; 16 Cal. Rptr. 302; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1551



October 4, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 29, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Joseph A. Murphy, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief to determine the constitutionality of a municipal ordinance regulating the hours of sale of uncured and uncooked meats.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiffs declaring ordinance unconstitutional, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city and intervenor uncured meat seller appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which ruled in favor of plaintiff meat markets and intervenor meat market operator and declared a city ordinance that regulated the sale of uncured meat unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The meat markets filed a declaratory relief action challenging the constitutionality of a city ordinance that required the closing of places selling uncured and uncooked meats during certain hours. The trial court declared the ordinance unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. The court concluded that the record did not disclose any reason to hold the ordinance unconstitutional. The manifest object of the ordinance was to prevent the sale of unfit or tainted meat at a time when those employed to safeguard the public were not on duty. Despite advances in refrigeration technology, the necessity of ensuring the safety of meats remained. The ordinance could not be set aside by a showing of change of conditions no greater than the advance in refrigeration technology. The court also ruled that the ordinance could not be set aside because other municipalities lacked a similar ordinance. The court ruled that the admission of a health officer's conversations with 43 other health officers was error. The testimony concerning the opinion of the other officers was hearsay and therefore incompetent.


OUTCOME: The court ruled against the meat markets and meat market operator and reversed the judgment that declared the ordinance unconstitutional.

 

1522 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hidalgo


Crim. No. 7258


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


195 Cal. App. 2d 843; 16 Cal. Rptr. 312; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1532



October 2, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. H. Burton Noble, Judge.

Prosecution for burglary.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction of second degree burglary, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of second degree burglary following a jury trial, and which denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary and pled not guilty. When called for trial, defendant's case was consolidated with two other defendants who were charged respectively with burglary and receiving stolen property. Defendant was convicted and appealed. He argued the consolidation was improper and evidence of other crimes and of a certain telephone conversation was inadmissible. The court found consolidation under Cal. Penal Code § 1098 did not prejudice defendant or violate his constitutional rights. Since any possible error was procedural and not jurisdictional, consolidation under the statute was not reversible error. Also, evidence that he stole a driver's license, while evidence of another crime, was admissible because it was pertinent to the crime charged. It showed defendant aided the commission of the burglary because he supplied a co-defendant with the stolen license. Next, the telephone conversation, which was an extrajudicial admission, was admissible because it connected defendant to the crime and there was prima facie proof of the corpus delicti of the crime by evidence other than the admission. Defendant was properly convicted of burglary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of burglary.

Smith v. Nettleship


Civ. No. 6433


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


195 Cal. App. 2d 393; 15 Cal. Rptr. 836; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1467



September 6, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied October 3, 1961, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied November 1, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Dean Sherry, Judge.

Action by a safety member of a county employees retirement association to have the County Employees Retirement Act of 1937 declared unconstitutional, and for injunctive relief.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for plaintiff reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, retirement board and its members (board), sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which declared unconstitutional the board's requirement that all safety members, including appellee safety member, take periodic physical examinations under Cal. Gov't. Code § 31527(f) and the board's regulations.


OVERVIEW: The safety member for the board was notified to appear for a physical examination soon after he became the safety member. He refused and the board set the matter of his refusal for hearing. The safety member was discharged and brought an action against the board. The trial court declared § 31527(f), under which the board promulgated the regulation requiring a physical examination, unconstitutional. The court reversed and held that safety membership was a special classification of the employees eligible for membership in the association and, considering the duties imposed upon the board, the classification was not unreasonable. Further, the requirement of a periodical physical examination of safety members was not for the benefit of the safety members or any private person or organization, but solely to facilitate the performance by the board of its duties. That this use was for a public use was apparent and the use of public funds for a public purpose did not violate the constitution. Finally, the promulgation of minimum physical standards and the requirement of reexamination of safety members failing to meet those standards were essential regulations to effectuate § 31527(f).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's the judgment and order declaring the requirement of a physical examination unconstitutional.
