Baldwin v. San Diego


Civ. No. 6461


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


195 Cal. App. 2d 236; 15 Cal. Rptr. 576; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1446



August 28, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied September 21, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Clarence Harden, Judge.

Action by retired members of city police and fire departments for declaration of their rights to certain fluctuating pension payments.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part with directions. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed as to all plaintiffs but one, and as to that plaintiff reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which issued a declaration of the rights of plaintiffs, retired police and firefighters, to fluctuating pensions and to the reimbursement of sums that had accrued in unpaid pension installments. The city argued that an amendment to its charter, which altered the limitations period for filing claims, should have applied retroactively to bar the action.


OVERVIEW: When certain police officers and firefighters were hired, their pension benefits provided for a fluctuating pension rate. After the city charter was amended to reflect a fixed pension rate, the pensioners filed a claim to enforce the fluctuating rate. The superior court declared that the pensioners were entitled to the fluctuating rates and awarded specific sums in accrued unpaid benefits. On appeal, the city argued that an amendment to its charter, which barred any claim against the city that was not filed within 90 days of accrual, should bar the pensioners' claims. The court emphasized that the right of a pensioner to payments under a pension was a contractual vested right that could not be destroyed; any statute that purported to do so was unconstitutional. Retroactive application of the procedural change enacted by the city would have just such a result. Instead, the court applied the new rule prospectively and presumed that the legislature had allowed the pensioners a reasonable time within which to file their claims. The court affirmed, except as to one pensioner whose work record did not support an award for excess pay under San Diego, Cal., Ordinance 5623, § 7 (1953).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's decision to construe the amendment to the city's charter prospectively, to allow the pensioners' claims to be filed, and to award fluctuating pension rates in the future and reimbursement for unpaid accrued pension benefits. The court reversed the decision as to one pensioner, whose work record did not support an award for excess pay under the applicable city ordinance.

 

1526 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Wareham v. Wareham


Civ. No. 25093


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


195 Cal. App. 2d 64; 15 Cal. Rptr. 465; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1427



August 21, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County modifying an interlocutory divorce judgment to declare that plaintiff was the father of a child born to his wife subsequent to such judgment. John P. Oliver, Court Commissioner, Judge pro tem.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband and defendant wife were parties to a divorce proceeding. Based upon a motion filed by the wife, the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) modified an interlocutory divorce judgment by declaring that the husband was the father of a child born to his wife subsequent to such judgment, awarded custody thereof to the wife, and ordered the husband to pay certain sums for the child's support. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband contended that the adverse order of the trial court was based on evidence, which was inherently improbable, impossible and contrary to physical law. He contended that although the child of a his wife was presumed legitimate that such presumption was only disputable and was conclusively overcome because the blood test established that he could not have been the father. He also contended that the conclusive presumption of legitimacy declared in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1962(5) was inapplicable because he did not cohabit with his wife during her gestation period. The judgment upholding the conclusive presumption was affirmed. The court concluded that neither the law nor the facts supported the claims of the husband. The trier of fact was the exclusive judge of the credibility of witnesses, and the trial judge was entitled to reconcile inconsistencies in resolving conflicting testimony of the witnesses. The court determined that the blood test was not available as a tool for rebutting the conclusive presumption of paternity created by § 1962(5).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court declaring the husband was the father of the child born to his wife subsequent to the entry of an interlocutory divorce judgment was affirmed.

 

1527 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Pepper v. Bishop


Civ. No. 18875


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


194 Cal. App. 2d 731; 15 Cal. Rptr. 346; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1870



August 15, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied October 11, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Monterey County. Anthony Brazil, Judge.

Action for damages for personal injuries sustained by a motorist when his automobile struck a horse owned by defendant.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Monterey County (California), which rendered a jury verdict in favor of defendant on plaintiff's claim to recover damages for injuries sustained by him when his automobile struck a horse owned by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Four mares had escaped from defendant's field. The bolt and chain indicated that the horses had caused the breaks. The trial court on its own motion read to the jury Cal Agric. Code § 423. Plaintiff asserted that it was error to read to the jury the final sentence of the section, which stated that there was no presumption or inference that a collision between a motor vehicle and a domestic animal was due to negligence on behalf of the owner. Plaintiff argued that the effect of reading the statute was to convey the impression that the jury could draw no inferences at all, but was strictly limited to direct evidence on the issues of negligence and proximate cause. The court did not agree. It held that the statute was designed to bar application of the doctrine of res ipsa loquitur to collisions with livestock. This was constitutionally permissible as the animate self-propulsion of livestock warranted placing it in a class distinct from inanimate objects. Viewing the jury instructions as a whole, the court was satisfied that the jury was not misled. The jury was adequately informed that it should not infer negligence from the mere happening of the accident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision in favor of defendant.

 

1528 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Vogulkin v. State Board of Education


Civ. No. 19638


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


194 Cal. App. 2d 424; 15 Cal. Rptr. 335; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1833



July 31, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 20, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. C. Harold Caulfield, Judge.

Action seeking to enjoin enforcement of certain sections of the Education Code, and for an order directing the State Board of Education to conduct a hearing to determine plaintiff's fitness to teach in the public schools.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants after demurrer to complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which sustained defendant board of education's demurrer to his complaint regarding the board's failure to reinstate his teaching credentials. The applicant attacked the constitutionality of the classification under Cal. Educ. Code § 13130, which required the denial of the application of a sexual psychopath or sex offender.


OVERVIEW: The applicant contended that the provisions of § 13130 should not have been applied to him because there were other offenders, convicted of similar crimes, who were not covered by § 13130's classification. He also alleged that § 13130 was unconstitutional because it denied him an opportunity to show that he had been rehabilitated. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that § 13130's classification was constitutional. The court found that the legislature had the discretion to create a lawful classification and that § 13130 was not to be declared unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Clause merely because there might have been other instances to which the legislation might have applied. The court determined that the classification had a rational basis and that the state had a right and a duty to screen teachers. The court also found that the applicant was not required to exhaust his administrative remedies prior to seeking relief in court because the board was not a lawmaking body and it did not have the power to disregard, amend or repeal the provisions of the Education Code. The statutes were mandatory in form leaving nothing upon which the board could act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that the Education Code contained a lawful, constitutional classification and that it was not unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Clause merely because it did not reach every class of offender to which it might have applied.

 

1529 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sinclair v. State


Civ. No. 6423


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


194 Cal. App. 2d 397; 15 Cal. Rptr. 493; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1830



July 28, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 20, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County and from an order denying motion for reconsideration of ruling on demurrer, for order vacating judgment and for permission to file an amended complaint. C. A. Paulsen * and Bonsall Noon, Judges.


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for declaratory relief and for an injunction as to a proposed freeway route and constitutionality of the California Highway Commission's proceeding thereunder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from an order an a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County(California), which sustained the demurrer filed by defendants, the State, the California Highway Commission, and various officials, and dismissed the owners' action for declaratory relief and for an injunction as to a proposed freeway route. The trial court also denied the owners' motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The owners held property along the proposed freeway. The owners filed a complaint against defendant to enjoin the construction of the proposed freeway. The owners contended that the resolution of the Commission determining the freeway route was void because the statute under which the Commission was granted its authority, Cal. Sts. &High. Code § 90, was unconstitutional. Defendants demurred to the complaint. The trial court sustained the demurrer and entered a judgment of dismissal. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that there was no basis exists for declaring § 90 to be unconstitutional as vague and uncertain. Section 90, which authorized the Commission to select the most direct and practicable location for a highway, was sufficiently definite to guide the Commission in the exercise of the powers conferred upon it by the legislature. Moreover, the language of § 90 was clear and unambiguous. Thus, the Commission had authority to set the route for the proposed highway, and the Commission's resolution was therefore valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order and judgment.

 

1530 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Reid v. State


Civ. No. 10149


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


193 Cal. App. 2d 799; 14 Cal. Rptr. 597; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1772



July 18, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of El Dorado County and from an order refusing to tax costs. Robert E. Roberts, Judge.

Action to enjoin an alleged trespass on property in connection with a local service road being constructed by defendants.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California), which dismissed the owners' action against respondent California Department of Public Works seeking to enjoin the Department from acts of alleged trespass upon the owners' property in connection with the construction of a service road.


OVERVIEW: The owners' complaint sought to enjoin the respondents from acts of alleged trespass in connection with the Department's construction of a service road adjacent to a highway. The trial court entered a judgment dismissing the complaint and allowing the Department to recover its costs, including reasonable attorneys' fees. On appeal, the owners contended that the trial court erred in rendering judgment of dismissal, refusing to grant the preliminary injunction, and in allowing the Department attorneys' fees. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that the judgment of dismissal was proper. The Department had the authority to construct the service road along the side of the highway pursuant to Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 90. The Department was authorized to condemn real property for State highway purposes upon the adoption of a resolution by the California Highway Commission pursuant to Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 102. The resolution of the Commission was conclusive evidence that the proposed public improvement was most compatible with the greatest public good and the least private injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1531 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. State Social Welfare Board


Civ. No. 19029


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


193 Cal. App. 2d 708; 14 Cal. Rptr. 776; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1761



July 17, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Twain Michelsen, Judge.

Proceeding to review a decision of the State Social Welfare Board reducing petitioner's old age security grant.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for petitioner reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant welfare board appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which ruled that the welfare board regulation exceeded legislative authorization in reducing respondent claimant's old age security grant.


OVERVIEW: The welfare board determined that the claimant had to exhaust potential resources in the form of his wife's present right to apply for federal benefits at the age of 62, instead of waiting until she reached the age of 65. The claimant filed an action challenging the welfare board's determination. The trial court ruled that the welfare board's regulation exceeded legislative authorization. On appeal, the court reversed. The court determined that the regulation requiring exhaustion of potential resources did not violate U.S. Const. art. XIV. The federal program, like that of the state, required the utilization by the applicant of all potential resources. The state regulation was requisite for compliance with the federal law. The due process and privileges and immunities clauses were not violated. The claimant did not have a fundamental right in old age assistance. His only right was to make application for old age benefits. It was reasonable for the state to require that, as a qualification for assistance, the claimant exhaust his potential resources. The statutory condition that the state comply with the federal rules reinforced the reasonableness of the requirement.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the welfare board and against the claimant and reversed the judgment declaring that the welfare board regulation exceeded legislative authorization.

 

1532 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Gowens v. Bakersfield


Civ. No. 6559


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


193 Cal. App. 2d 79; 13 Cal. Rptr. 820; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1670



June 13, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied August 9, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Frederick E. Stone * and Robert B. Lambert, Judges.


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to have a city ordinance declared unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal with prejudice after demurrer to amended complaint was sustained, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hotel owner sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which sustained respondent city's demurrer and dismissed the hotel owner's suit over the imposition of a tax on transient use of hotel rooms.


OVERVIEW: After a preceding ordinance was struck down by the court, the city adopted a new ordinance, which imposed a tax on the transient use of hotel rooms in the city. The ordinance defined transient use as the rental of a room for less than 30 days. The trial court upheld the ordinance, and likened it to a sales tax imposed on the privilege of eating a meal at a restaurant. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that a tax on the privilege to stay in certain rooms, under certain conditions, for specified lengths of time, was within the city's taxing power. The court further held that the classification of the ordinance, which treated differently those who rented rooms for less than 30 days, as opposed to those who rented for more than 30 days, was a reasonable classification. The court noted with approval that, within the classification, every person within the class specified was treated equally.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, and held that the city could impose a tax on hotel rooms rented for less than 30 days.

 

1533 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Bacich v. Russell


Civ. No. 19525


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


192 Cal. App. 2d 435; 13 Cal. Rptr. 459; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1958



May 24, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 19, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. C. Harold Caulfield, Judge.

Actions for damages for personal injuries arising out of a collision of automobiles.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgments for plaintiffs reversed as to one defendant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant driver sought review of judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which found in favor of plaintiff injured persons in their actions to recover damages for injuries received in an automobile collision. Another driver was also a defendant in the action; that driver did not appeal the judgments.


OVERVIEW: The injured persons were in a car that was a part of a funeral procession when their car was struck in an intersection. Traffic control signals displaying green, amber, and red lights, located on each of the four corners of the intersection, were in operation at the time. The drivers of two separate cars testified that they entered the intersection on a green light and claimed the right of way under the provisions of Cal. Veh. Code § 476. The injured persons claimed the right of way under a city ordinance that gave cars in a funeral procession the right of way where certain conditions were met. On appeal, the court reversed the judgments of the trial court as to the driver that appealed. The city ordinance was invalid because it conflicted with § 476(f), which only allowed the disobedience of traffic lights under certain conditions that were not applicable to the case. It was reversible error for the trial court to have given a jury instruction based on the invalid ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court as to the driver that appealed. The trial court found in favor of the injured persons in their actions to recover damages for injuries received in an automobile collision.

 

1534 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Sweetland v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 19420


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


192 Cal. App. 2d 316; 13 Cal. Rptr. 432; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 1942



May 22, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 14, 1961, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 19, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Orla St. Clair, Judge.

Action for refund of state income taxes allegedly overpaid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trustee challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which affirmed respondent franchise tax board's decision to disallow a tax refund, in the trustee's action for a refund of state income taxes allegedly overpaid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The trustee represented the estate of the deceased taxpayer and contended that the taxpayer's estate was due a refund for overpaid state income taxes. In the taxable year of 1938, the taxpayer reported a gain on the dissolution of a corporation. In reporting the gain, the taxpayer used as the basis of his stock the cost to him of the stock of an acquired corporation. In 1928, the taxpayer had exchanged his shares in an acquired corporation for the shares that he held until 1938. The trustee contended that there was no state income tax law in 1928 to recognize the gain and that the gain should have been recognized in 1928, the year of the exchange. The court held that, because the transaction was a "reorganization" under I.R.C. § 203(b)(2) (1926), no taxable gain resulted in 1928. Because there was no law applicable in 1928, no increase or decrease was recognized, and therefore the basis of the taxpayer's stock was the same as in the case of the property exchanged. Accordingly, the gain was in fact realized in 1938.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the trustee was not entitled to a refund. The taxpayer's gain was properly taxed in the year that it was realized, which was the year that the corporation was dissolved.

 

1535 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Superior Court of Cal.


No. 19845


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2605; 126 Cal. 2351



May 21, 1961, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance company sought a writ of prohibition to restrain respondent trial court from enforcing an order requiring petitioner to permit the real parties in interest to inspect and copy all documents related to an auto accident involving the company's insured. The request by the real parties was made pursuant to Code of Civil Procedure § 2031 (California).


OVERVIEW: The real parties in interest filed an action against the company alleging that the insured caused an auto accident that injured the real parties. The real parties sought all records, correspondence, documents, photographs, memoranda, notes, statements, and any matters pertaining to the file of the insured and the claim. The court found that the materials were sufficiently described but that their materiality or relevancy was not sufficiently shown. The court granted the motion to prohibit the discovery. The court found that Code of Civil Procedure §§ 2031 and 2016, subdivision (b) (California), when read together, required a demonstration that the request would lead to the discovery of admissible evidence. The real parties, if they sought to limit their request, would have to do so by taking depositions or propounding interrogatories. The overbroad request could not be imposed on the company.


OUTCOME: The court granted the company a peremptory writ of prohibition.

 

1536 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Wirin v. Ostly


Civ. No. 24644


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


191 Cal. App. 2d 710; 13 Cal. Rptr. 31; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2113



May 2, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 21, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Charles A. Loring, Judge.

Action for declaration of plaintiff's right to hold office of notary public without subscribing to certain portions of oath set forth in Const., art. XX, § 3.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidate appealed from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) judgment for defendant county clerk in his action for a declaration of his right to hold the office of notary public without subscribing to certain portions of the oath set forth in Calif. Const. art. XX, § 3. He argued that the oath was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The candidate sought a declaratory judgment that he was entitled to hold the office of notary public without subscribing to certain portions of the oath set forth in the state constitution and that the county clerk was without legal authority to refuse to administer the oath in the modified form in which the candidate was willing to take it, or to refuse to transmit the certificate required by Cal. Gov't Code § 8213. At trial, the candidate testified that he could not subscribe to portions of the oath because of his religious beliefs and the tenets of his church in regard to test oaths. The court affirmed, finding the Pockman decision controlling. The oath was not a test of religious opinion nor political opinion. The oath was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the county clerk was affirmed. The oath was not unconstitutional and was not a religious test.

 

1537 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Green v. Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Appellate Dep't


Civ. No. 25334


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


191 Cal. App. 2d 484; 12 Cal. Rptr. 796; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2077



April 24, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 21, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORDER to show cause why a petition for writs of prohibition, mandate and/or habeas corpus should not issue.



DISPOSITION: Order to show cause discharged, and petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought writs of prohibition, mandate, and habeas corpus. She claimed she was denied due process of law because she was denied counsel at her trial, she was denied a jury trial, she was denied the right to a court reporter's transcript on her appeal, and she was denied a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had been convicted of assault and battery. Upon review, the court found that petitioner personally waived her right to a trial by jury in open court. Petitioner made no showing that she was not advised of her right to counsel or that she requested the court to appoint counsel for her. Further, those matters should have been raised on her direct appeal from the judgment against her. Petitioner claimed that as an indigent person, she was entitled to a court reporter's transcript as a matter of right without having to make a proper showing of need. The only showing of need for the transcript petitioner made was that her counsel did not represent her at trial and was unaware of any errors that might have occurred. However, petitioner's counsel made no attempt to secure a settled statement and resisted all efforts of the trial court to procure a settled statement. The court found that it was petitioner's duty to make a bona fide attempt to procure a settled statement for use upon appeal and only if that failed, could she have shown the need for transcript to be furnished to her at the county's expense. Petitioner's claim she was denied a speedy trial was frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petitioner's request for writs of prohibition, mandate, and habeas corpus.

 

1538 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Western Air Lines, Inc. v. Sobieski


Civ. No. 24018


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


191 Cal. App. 2d 399; 12 Cal. Rptr. 719; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2066



April 20, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 17, 1961, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 14, 1961. Schauer, J., and Peters, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Rex Hardy, Judge.

PROCEEDING in mandamus to review a final order of the Corporations Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment granting writ, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commissioner of Corporations, sought review of an order finding that appellant lacked jurisdiction to demand respondent to acquire a securities permit, pursuant to the Corporate Securities Act, Cal. Corp. Code § 25009.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of an order finding that appellant lacked jurisdiction to demand respondent to acquire a securities permit, pursuant to the Corporate Securities Act, Cal. Corp. Code § 25009. The appeals court reversed the lower court's findings, holding that respondent's corporate reorganization constituted a sale under § 25009. According to the appeals court the terms "sale" or "sell" included any change in the rights, preferences, privileges, or restrictions on outstanding securities. The appeals court further held that when the Act was violated by solicitation of sales of stock in California, the Act applied even though the transfer of title was to take place in a foreign state. Lastly, the appeals court held that the issuance and sale of stock within a state other than that of its organization was properly regulated to protect the residents and citizens of the former state.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the lower court's findings, holding that respondent's corporate reorganization constituted a sale under the Corporate Securities Act.

Agnew v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 24676


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


190 Cal. App. 2d 820; 12 Cal. Rptr. 507; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2374



April 5, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 3, 1961, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 31, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from various intermediate orders. Otto J. Emme and H. Eugene Breitenbach, Judges.

Action to enjoin enforcement of certain municipal ordinances on the ground that they conflicted with general law.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeals from orders, dismissed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to amended second supplemental complaint was sustained with leave to amend and plaintiff declined to amend or consolidate, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant electrical contractor challenged the dismissal of its amended complaint from the California Supreme Court. The complaint challenged certain provisions of a municipal code pertaining to electrical contractors on grounds that it conflicted with state law, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 7000-7145.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an electrical contractor licensed by the state, brought suit to enjoin enforcement of certain ordinances of defendant city on the ground that they conflicted with general law and thus were unconstitutional. The municipal code in question imposed certain requirements on an electrical contractor and required the payment of a fee in order to obtain a license tax registration number. The lower court entered judgment in favor of the city. Appellant challenged the decision and the state supreme court reversed, holding that provisions of the ordinance were invalid to the extent they conflicted with Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 7000-7145. The municipal code was subsequently amended in response to that decision. Appellant then filed an amended complaint, which was dismissed. Appellant challenged the decision. The court found that the municipal code, as amended, did not interfere with state regulations or prescribe qualifications for electrical contractors different from or in addition to those prescribed by the state. The amended municipal code also clarified that the tax on the contractors was an exercise of the taxing power for revenue purposes, and thus was not invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the supreme court's dismissal of appellant electrician's amended complaint, which challenged the constitutionality of certain provisions of a municipal code pertaining to electrical contractors.

 

1540 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Floresta, Inc. v. City Council of San Leandro


Civ. No. 19297


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


190 Cal. App. 2d 599; 12 Cal. Rptr. 182; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2345



March 29, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 24, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Folger Emerson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to review decision of a city council denying a zoning use permit, and an action seeking declaration of unconstitutionality of the zoning ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ and declaring the ordinance to be constitutional, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant zoning applicant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which denied the applicant's petition for mandamus and its request for declaratory relief, finding that the zoning ordinance of appellee city, prohibiting liquor establishments near residential districts, was constitutional and that the actions of the city in the denial of a zoning use permit were neither arbitrary nor discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: The applicant requested zoning approval to place a cocktail lounge in a residential strip shopping center. San Leandro, Cal., Mun. Code of 1957 § 7-3-143.2 prohibited liquor establishments near residential districts, and thus the Board of Zoning Adjustments (board) denied the permit after residents voiced objections. The city council affirmed the board, and the court affirmed the trial court's findings because the ordinance neither unconstitutionally invaded the state regulation of liquor nor did it constitute an attempted exercise of local option. The legislature specifically provided in Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 23790, 23791, that licensing was subject to a valid zoning ordinance, and the court found that the ordinance was valid in that it was a geographic restriction for the place of sale and use of liquor and it did not interfere with the state's general regulation of the consumption of liquor. The court further found that the city's decision was not arbitrary and that it was for the board to determine whether the applicant met the burden of proving that the public was not detrimentally affected by the proposed use. Thus, the city had the right to enforce its zoning ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the applicant's petition for writ of mandamus and declaring that the city zoning ordinance for liquor establishments was constitutional.

 

1541 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Daniel v. Board of Police Comm'rs


Civ. Nos. 24763, 24707


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


190 Cal. App. 2d 566; 12 Cal. Rptr. 226; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2341



March 28, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied April 14, 1961, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied May 24, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Clyde C. Triplett, Judge.

Actions to enjoin a city and its board of police commissioners from using public funds to administer or execute provisions of a certain municipal ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged a judgment entered in favor of defendant board of police commissioners in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) in their action alleging that Los Angeles, Cal., Municipal Code §§ 103.102, 103.29, and 103.31 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Sections 103.102, 103.29, and 103.31 required persons to have permits in order to sell food or beverages in a public place and have live entertainment. The board had the authority to issue the permits. The taxpayers alleged that by §§ 103.102, 103.29, and 103.31 the city council attempted to legislate in a field that was preempted by the state and that the enforcement of §§ 103.102, 103.29, and 103.31 was an unreasonable exercise of police power. The trial court ruled that §§ 103.102, 103.29, and 103.31 were not unconstitutional, and the court affirmed. The court held that the purpose of §§ 103.102, 103.29, and 103.31 was not to regulate the liquor business but was to regulate the kind of live entertainment that was furnished in such public places as restaurants and liquor establishments. The state had not preempted the field or area covered by §§ 103.102, 103.29, and 103.31. The ordinance was a valid exercise of police power. The classification between live entertainment and recorded entertainment was reasonable and was reasonably related to the purpose of the ordinance. The ordinance furnished many guides for the board in considering matters with respect to a permit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the board in the taxpayers' action alleging that the ordinance was unconstitutional.

 

1542 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Savage v. Los Angeles Trust Deed & Mortg. Exchange


Civ. No. 24998


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


190 Cal. App. 2d 66; 12 Cal. Rptr. 144; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2268



March 14, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County granting a preliminary injunction. Ellsworth Meyer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Real Estate Commissioner of California (Commissioner) filed an action against defendant real estate salesmen (salesmen) seeking to prohibit them from acting as real estate brokers until licensed by the commissioner. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) granted the preliminary injunction. The salesmen challenged the trial court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The salesmen argued that it was an error for the trial court to permit into evidence a certification by a supervising deputy in the office of the commissioner and a declaration by a deputy attorney general both under penalty of perjury to be filed. According to the salesmen, there was a doubt as to whether the certification or the declarations were additions to the complaint, which would have been required to plead. On appeal, the court held that the documents were filed in lieu of affidavits, which would support the issuance of a preliminary injunction. Next, the salesmen argued that the preliminary injunction was premature. The court determined that the injunction order was not premature because an injunction may have been granted at any time before judgment upon a verified compliant, or upon affidavits. The salesmen then argued that the salesmen were not required by law to be licensed as real estate brokers at the time of the filing of the complaint. The salesmen were performing acts defined as duties of real estate salesmen pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 10132.1. Moreover, the preliminary injunction was not inconsistent with the record. Thus, the court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to grant the preliminary injunction.

 

1543 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Bleamaster v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 24888


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


189 Cal. App. 2d 274; 11 Cal. Rptr. 214; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2173



February 20, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied March 15, 1961, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 19, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. F. Ray Bennett, Judge.

Action against a county and a city seeking removal of a "curb return" constructed on plaintiffs' property and for damages based on asserted inverse condemnation.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal as to county after its demurrer to amended complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner appealed the judgment by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), in favor of defendant county in the landowner's action against the county and defendant city for removal of a curb return from her property and for damages for inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: The county constructed a concrete curb return on the landowner's property without a condemnation. The county refused to remove the curb return. The city then annexed the area, and it refused to remove the curb return or reimburse the landowner. The landowner filed an action against the county and the city for removal of the curb return and reimbursement for the property damage. The trial court dismissed the action against the county. The landowner appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that because the property had been annexed by the city, the county had no authority to remove the curb return; therefore, the landowner had failed to state a cause of action against the county. The court held that Cal. Gov. Code § 29704, which required that a claim be filed with the county prior to filing suit, and § 29702, which provided a one year statute of limitations on claims against the county, applied. The court held that §§ 29702, 29704 were not unconstitutional because they gave a claimant an adequate opportunity to seek compensation for annexed property. The court held that the landowner failed to file a claim with the county on a timely basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed the landowner's action against the county for removal of a curb return and for damages to property.

 

1544 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kimbley


Crim. No. 7160


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


189 Cal. App. 2d 300; 11 Cal. Rptr. 519; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2176



February 20, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 19, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. John F. Aiso, Judge.

Prosecution for driving a vehicle upon a public highway while "addicted to the use" of narcotic drugs.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant for driving a vehicle upon a public highway while addicted to the use of narcotic drugs in violation Cal. Veh. Code § 23105 and of a prior felony conviction of possession of narcotics.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of driving a vehicle upon a public highway while addicted to the use of narcotic drugs in violation of § 23105 and appealed from the judgment.Defendant asserted that the standard fixed by § 23105, any person who is addicted to the use of narcotic drugs, violated due process. Defendant argued that it could not be determined whether the word "addicted" referred to habitually taking or otherwise using narcotics to the extent of having lost the power of self-control or whether it referred to merely using narcotics without reference to whether the power of self-control was lost. The court examined the ordinary, dictionary definition of the word "addicted" and held that it was unlawful for any person "addicted to the use" of narcotic drugs to drive a vehicle upon any highway. Defendant stated there was no evidence that he lost the power of self-control. Since the court has held that "addicted to the use" in § 23105 does not necessarily mean that a person has lost the power of self-control, the point was without merit. There was ample evidence that defendant was addicted to the use of narcotic drugs and therefore the judgment of conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

1545 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Santa Barbara v. Modern Neon Sign Co.


Civ. No. 24850


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


189 Cal. App. 2d 188; 11 Cal. Rptr. 57; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2162



February 16, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County. John P. McMurray, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action to compel compliance with a municipal ordinance forbidding use of certain types of advertising signs.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which denied relief to the city with respect to its action against respondents, owners and lessees, to compel compliance with Santa Barbara, Cal., Sign Ordinance no. 2598, which prohibited moving signs.


OVERVIEW: The moving signs of the owners and lessees were built pursuant to permits issued by the city. The city then adopted an ordinance that prohibited moving signs. The city brought an action against the owners and lessees to compel compliance with the ordinance. The trial court held that the ordinance as applied to the owners and lessees was unconstitutional. The trial court denied relief to the city and entered a judgment in favor of the owners and lessees. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found that there was no natural, intrinsic, or constitutional distinction which furnished a reason for or justified the classification of moving and flashing signs in the manner found in the ordinance. The court also found that the ordinance operated to take the property of the owners and lessees without compensation and without due process of law and that it exceeded the legitimate exercise of the police power. The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the ordinance's prohibition of moving signs based solely on aesthetic grounds and considerations was an unconstitutional exercise of the city's police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which had denied relief to the city with respect to its action against the owners and lessees to compel compliance with the municipal ordinance that prohibited moving signs.

 

1546 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Newport Beach Fire & Police Protective League v. City Council of Newport Beach


Civ. No. 6395


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


189 Cal. App. 2d 17; 10 Cal. Rptr. 919; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2142



February 7, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Ronald M. Crookshank, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a city council to declare invalid the adoption of an initiative ordinance relating to the city's civil service system.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal, after demurrer to petition was sustained with leave to amend and petitioners elected not to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, police association and individuals, sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Orange County (California) that dismissed the appellants' petition for writ of mandate to have respondent city council declare invalid the adoption of an initiative ordinance relating to the city's civil service system.


OVERVIEW: The public servants' association and members claimed that the repeal of Newport Beach, Cal, Ordinance No. 511 amounted to a withdrawal of all of the civil service employees from the city's civil service system and under the city's charter the initiative measure could be adopted only by a two-thirds vote of the electorate. Respondent city officials claimed that there was no withdrawal of any civil service employee from the system, the charter provisions did not apply, and the charter provision in question contravened the California Constitution, which reserved to the electorate through the initiative and referendum the right to legislate by majority action. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that dismissed the association and members' petition based on the city official's demurrer and held that the California Constitution provided that referendum initiative were to be by a majority vote and that the city's charter that attempted to require a two-thirds vote was unconstitutional. The court further held that Ord. No. 511 caused no withdrawal of any employee from the system and that the ordinance scheme specifically left the civil service members in the system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that granted the city officials' demurrer and dismissed the petition of the association and members to have the city ordinance declared invalid.

Stratton v. Long Beach


Civ. No. 23986


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


188 Cal. App. 2d 761; 11 Cal. Rptr. 8; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2484



February 1, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. A. Curtis Smith, Judge.

Proceeding by two attorneys to collect their fees and costs of suit arising out of services rendered in a taxpayer's action against a city.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying petition, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys filed an action against respondent city to collect their attorneys' fees and the expenses they incurred in representing a taxpayer in his lawsuit against the city. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) entered a judgment in favor of the city. The attorneys appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city was using revenue from tide land gas and oil development for public projects. The underlying lawsuit challenged the city's use of the funds for purposes other than waterfront related projects. As a result of the litigation, it was adjudged that the city was entitled to only a portion of the funds it previously had collected, and that the remainder was to be held by the city in trust for the state. The attorneys contended that they were entitled to be paid from the trust funds or the city directly because they benefited those funds by preventing their misappropriation by the city for use on municipal improvements and they saved the city taxpayers from owing a debt to the state. The court affirmed the dismissal of the petition. The court held that: (1) the attorneys were not entitled to compensation from the fund because their services were antagonistic to and not for the benefit of the state or the resulting trust; and (2) they were not entitled to compensation from the city because they did not represent the city in the litigation and because they did not have an express or implied fee agreement with the city.


OUTCOME: In the attorneys' petition for fees and expenses they incurred in representing a taxpayer's lawsuit that involved municipal spending, the judgment that denied their petition for fees and expenses was affirmed.

Rio Vista Gas Asso. v. State


Civ. No. 9947


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


188 Cal. App. 2d 555; 10 Cal. Rptr. 559; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2457; 14 Oil & Gas Rep. 27



January 26, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County and from orders refusing to rescind cost bonds on file and taxing costs after time for filing a cost bill had expired. Vernon Stoll, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action in inverse condemnation against the state for exercising an alleged illegal and unwarranted dominion over mineral rights in certain lands.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal after demurrer to first amended complaint was sustained without leave to amend, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gas association filed an inverse condemnation action against defendant, the State of California, for ownership of mineral rights located beneath state-owned land. The Superior Court of Sacramento County, California, entered judgment in the state's favor and sustained a demurrer to the gas association's first amended complaint without leave to amend. The gas association appealed.


OVERVIEW: The gas association claimed that it retained ownership of mineral rights located under land purchased by the state in fee simple as a dumping ground. On appeal, the association also asked for review of the trial court's refusal to rescind cost bonds. The court affirmed the trial court in all respects. The court held that reclamation board and the drainage districts were authorized to acquire property under 1913 Cal. Stat. 170 and that the state legislature gave the board power to hold title in fee simple and lease gas rights in land so held. Further, the court held that the trial court properly requested the association to post bond in excess of the statutory minimum under Cal. After the court affirmed the award of costs and attorney fees at the trial level, the court ordered the association to pay an additional attorney fee to cover the state's legal expenses of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the state. The court affirmed the order that awarded the state an attorney fee and costs. Further, the court awarded the state an additional attorney fee to cover professional services rendered on the appeal.

 

1549 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Rees v. Palm Springs


Civ. No. 6359


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


188 Cal. App. 2d 339; 10 Cal. Rptr. 386; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2432; 42 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P50,150



January 20, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County. Hilton H. McCabe, Judge.

Action to enjoin enforcement of an ordinance purporting to regulate picketing.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which granted plaintiff picketers' injunction and enjoined the enforcement of an ordinance purporting to regulate picketing.


OVERVIEW: The picketers sought and obtained a judgment enjoining enforcement of certain sections of a city ordinance that purported to regulate picketing. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court concluded that the challenged sections of the ordinance were invalid. They imposed restrictions on picketing that unreasonably discriminated between citizens in their exercise of normal constitutional rights. Specifically, forbidding pickets to be closer than 30 feet apart in a prescribed area did not have any reasonable basis for discrimination between members of the public desiring to speak of labor problems and those desiring to communicate on different problems; forbidding picketing of a place adjacent to a business with whom the picketer did not have a labor dispute did not have any relationship to the announced purpose of protecting traffic and was repugnant to the rights of free speech; and forbidding a picketer to walk in a circular, oval, or rectangular manner gave no appearance of accomplishing traffic safety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the picketers and against the city in the action to enjoin the enforcement of an ordinance purporting to regulate picketing.

Batson v. State Personnel Board


Civ. No. 9881


Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District


188 Cal. App. 2d 320; 10 Cal. Rptr. 452; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2429



January 19, 1961 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Jay L. Henry, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to review a decision of the State Personnel Board discharging a civil service employee.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandate seeking to review a decision of respondent State Personnel Board (California) discharging him from his civil service position with the Department of Mental Hygiene.


OVERVIEW: The employee was discharged from his civil service position because of various incidents of misconduct with patients. The employee requested a hearing before the Board. The Board sustained the decision discharging the employee from his civil service position. The employee sought review of the Board's decision. The trial court denied the employee's writ and, on appeal, the court affirmed . The court found that the evidence clearly supported the factual findings. Each action violated Dep't Mental Hygiene R. 84 and was a cause for disciplinary action under Cal. Gov't Code § 19572. Each action supported a finding of incompetency and discourteous treatment of the public within the meaning of § 19572(b) and (n). In addition, the acts of the employee involving his discourteous treatment of co-employees violated § 19572(n). The court held that the findings of the Board were amply supported by substantial evidence. The court could not say that the Board abused its discretion in determining that the employee should be discharged from his position.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the writ.

Shivell v. Municipal Court for Santa Ana-Orange Judicial Dist.

Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District

OVERVIEW: A criminal complaint was filed that charged appellant with three counts of violating the California Vehicle Code. Count 1 charged him with speeding, a violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 22408, reading: Whenever a passenger vehicle regardless of weight or commercial motor vehicle weighing less than 4,000 pounds is drawing any vehicle the maximum speed shall not at any time exceed 45 miles per hour subject to other and more restrictive limits set forth in this code. The court also held that the legislative power to regulate travel was extensive and that appellant's right to operate his vehicle was not an unfettered one. The statute was constitutional in light of public safety concerns.

1552 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Doctors General Hospital v. County of Santa Clara


Civ. No. 19302


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


188 Cal. App. 2d 280; 10 Cal. Rptr. 423; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2423



January 18, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 10, 1961, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 15, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Edwin J. Owens, Judge.

Action to recover property taxes paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment for defendants reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonprofit hospital appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which held that Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 263 violated Cal. Const. art. IV., § 31 and that defendants, county and officials (county), were not required to exempt the hospital from the payment of property taxes.


OVERVIEW: The hospital failed to timely file an affidavit setting forth the facts that would exempt it from property taxes under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 214, and the hospital paid the property tax. The legislature enacted Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 263, which provided that any property tax paid by a nonprofit hospital in the year in which the hospital failed to file its affidavit was to be refunded to the nonprofit hospital that paid the tax. The trial court held that § 263 was a gift of public money and violated Cal. Const. art. IV, § 31. The court reversed, holding that the hospital was entitled to a refund, that the exemption for nonprofit hospitals was a well-recognized public purpose, and that the legislature could retroactively dispense with the requirement of an affidavit. Because the retroactive cancellation of the hospital's liability for property taxes was enacted for a public purpose, the cancellation was not a gift of public money. Because there was a reasonable basis for cancelling the hospital's liability, the court refused to disturb the legislative determination that a public purpose was served by cancelling the tax liability.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that cancelling the hospital's liability for property taxes was an unconstitutional gift to the hospital and held that the hospital was entitled to a refund of taxes that it paid.

 

1553 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Farina v. Emeryville


Civ. No. 19400


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


188 Cal. App. 2d 100; 10 Cal. Rptr. 288; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2396



January 10, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 9, 1961, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 8, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County. Charles Wade Snook, Judge.

Action by a retired police officer to establish his right to an increased pension.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) in favor of plaintiff retired police chief in his action to establish his right to an increased pension. The superior court declared that his retirement allowance was half of the active police chief's salary, and he was awarded the difference between that amount and the lesser amount that he had received since his retirement.


OVERVIEW: During the police chief's active tenure, the city adopted Emeryville, Cal., Ordinance 224 (1929), which provided him with a pension benefit of one-half of the salary of the acting police chief. Before he retired, the city repealed that ordinance, and he received less than one-half of the active chief's salary for his first three years of retirement. The retired chief brought an action against the city to establish his entitlement to one-half of the active chief's salary and to recover the shortage for the period since his retirement, and the superior court entered a judgment in his favor. The court affirmed the superior court's judgment and found that the chief had a vested right to the benefit pegged to the position's existing salary. In its ruling, the court found that the chief acquired a vested right in the retirement system that was in effect during his rendition of service and that the city's plan could not be changed thereafter to the chief's disadvantage unless the city compensated him for the change. The court ruled that the city's establishment of its substitute pension plan was an advantage to the city, not to the chief, even if it was sound on an actuarial basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Preston v. Municipal Court of San Francisco


Civ. No. 18864


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


188 Cal. App. 2d 76; 10 Cal. Rptr. 301; 1961 Cal. App. LEXIS 2394



January 9, 1961 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 8, 1961, and Respondents' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 9, 1961. Schauer, J., McComb, J., and White, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco and from an order sustaining a demurrer without leave to amend. Orla St. Clair, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Municipal Court of the City and County of San Francisco, and Charles S. Peery, Judge thereof, to furnish a reporter's transcript of a criminal trial.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment denying writ, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which sustained the demurrer of respondent municipal court, in defendant's proceeding in mandamus to compel the municipal court to furnish a transcript of defendant's criminal trial without cost for use in the appeal from her conviction for petty theft. The superior court denied the writ.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for petty theft was a misdemeanor, and she filed an affidavit of defendant in forma pauperis with her notice to the municipal court to prepare a transcript of her trial at the expense of the city and county under Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 274c, Cal. Gov't Code § 69952. The municipal court denied defendant's motion for preparation of the transcript. The superior court rejected defendant's claim that she was entitled to a transcript of the trial proceedings without cost even if the transcript was necessary to defendant's appeal from her conviction. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the superior court to sustain the municipal's court's demurrer and its denial of defendant's application for a writ of mandamus. Defendant's writ application recited allegations to establish the insufficiency of a settled statement as an alternative to a transcript for the purposes of appeal. The proceedings in the municipal court were too complex and a transcript of those proceedings was necessary to defendant's appeal. Defendant's right to a transcript, without cost, was not limited by the classification of her crime as a misdemeanor as opposed to a felony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's decision to deny defendant's application for a writ of mandamus, reversed the superior court's order to sustain the municipal court's demurrer, and ruled that the municipal court should have been permitted to answer defendant's complaint.

People v. Douglas


Crim. No. 7040


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


187 Cal. App. 2d 802; 10 Cal. Rptr. 188; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 1460



December 29, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied January 26, 1961, and the Petition of Appellant Bennie Will Meyes for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 21, 1961. Traynor, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying new trials. Bayard Rhone, Judge.

Prosecution for robbery, assault with intent to commit murder, and assault with a deadly weapon.



DISPOSITION: One judgment modified and affirmed and other judgment affirmed; orders affirmed. Judgment of conviction as to defendant Meyes, modified and affirmed; judgment of conviction as to defendant Douglas, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged their convictions by a jury and sentencing in the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for robbery, assault with intent to commit murder, and two counts of assault with a deadly weapon. The jury found that the second defendant had been convicted of burglary and robbery in the past and was a habitual offender. Defendants' motions for a new trial were denied by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendants dismissed their public defender, and the trial court denied their motion for a continuance for time to obtain private counsel. Defendants defended themselves without the assistance of counsel. Defendants were convicted for 12 felonies, and witnesses for the State described each offense and identified defendants as the perpetrators. On appeal, the court affirmed defendants' convictions and modified the sentence of the second defendant pursuant to Cal. Penal Code §§ 644, 669. Due process of law did not require the State to obtain an indictment against defendants, and prosecution by information was a proper alternative remedy. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in its denial of defendants' motion for a continuance because their rejection of the services of their public defender was an attempt to postpone the trial. Defendants failed to exercise their opportunity to present an alibi defense. Modification of the second defendant's sentence was required under Cal. Penal Code §§ 644, 669, which mandated the merger of that defendant's other sentences with the life term properly imposed upon him as a habitual offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for robbery, assault with intent to commit murder, and assault with a deadly weapon, affirmed the trial court's denial of defendants' motions for a new trial, and modified the sentence of the second defendant to declare that his sentences were merged and were to run concurrently with the life term imposed on the second defendant as a habitual offender.
