Takata v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 24256


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


184 Cal. App. 2d 154; 7 Cal. Rptr. 516; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 1859



August 26, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Walter H. Odemar, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to review an order of a city board to vacate and demolish a building, and to enjoin enforcement of the order.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ and refusing injunctive relief, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which affirmed the findings of the Board of Building and Safety Commissioners (board) after a review of the administrative record and ordered that the owners' building be vacated, demolished, and removed. The owners appealed the denial of their petition for declaratory relief and an injunction against the demolition of the building.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent of the board had determined that the owners' building was a dangerous and substandard residential building and a nuisance. After a hearing, the board accepted the superintendent's determination. The owners appealed the board's findings. The trial court affirmed and held that the owners failed to show any evidence of unequal, arbitrary, or discriminatory enforcement of laws by the board. On appeal, the owners contended that there was insufficient evidence to support the findings of the trial court. The court affirmed and held that the factual findings of the trial court and the board clearly supported demolition of the owners' property in order to provide for the health and safety of neighboring persons and property. The court rejected the owners' contention that the board's actions were preempted by the Community Redevelopment Act (Act), Cal. Health & Safety Code § 33000 et seq. The state had not designated the building's area as a "slum" in need of redevelopment, and nothing in the Act provided for the preemption of a local government's police powers to protect its citizens. The legislature's delegation of demolition and inspection powers to the board was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that affirmed the board's order of vacation and demolition of the owners' building. The court refused to declare invalid or issue an injunction against the enforcement of board's order.

 

1573 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Estate of Krey


Civ. No. 6414


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


183 Cal. App. 2d 312; 6 Cal. Rptr. 804; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 1752



July 28, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied August 19, 1960, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied September 20, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County determining interests in an estate. C. A. Paulsen, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband's heirs sought review of a decree by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) in which the husband's heirs were granted a one half interest in decedent's estate and appellees, heirs of decedent's predeceased wife, were granted a one half interest in the estate.


OVERVIEW: Decedent husband died intestate having been predeceased by his wife and neither having left children or parents. The couple had moved to California for retirement and the property they held had been acquired in common law property states. The trial court decreed that the estate be evenly split between the heirs of the wife and the heirs of the husband. The heirs of the husband contended that this was in error. The court found that in the determination of the character of property for the purpose of Cal. Prob. Code §§ 228 and 229, the critical question was that of the source of the acquisition of the property rather than the nature of its ownership just before death. The court held that property acquired through the efforts of a married couple during the course of their marriage were properly converted to community property by virtue of the laws of domicile once the parties became domiciled in the sate. The court affirmed the prior decree having determined that the heirs of the predeceased wife took not through direct succession from her, but as statutory heirs of the husband.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the prior decree having determined that the decedents were residents of the state and that their property was properly reclassified under the law of domicile.

 

1574 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Clemons


Crim. No. 7000


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


182 Cal. App. 2d 808; 6 Cal. Rptr. 727; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2183



July 19, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from an order denying a new trial. Herbert V. Walker, Judge.

Prosecution for conspiracy to commit an abortion, and for committing an abortion.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which after a trial without a jury, convicted her of conspiracy to commit an abortion and committing an abortion. Defendant also appealed from an order of the same court, which denied her motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy to commit an abortion and committing an abortion. The abortee went to the hospital with an infection caused by an abortion. She led the police to defendant. When requested to refund the money allegedly paid for the abortion, defendant responded that she did not have the money. Other incriminating statements were made regarding the instruments used in the abortion. The abortee testified against defendant. Upon her conviction, defendant made a motion for a new trial, which was denied. She appealed and argued, inter alia, that there was insufficient evidence to sustain her conviction because Cal. Penal Code § 1108 required that the testimony of the abortee be corroborated by other evidence. The court agreed, but it found that under the applicable caselaw, the incriminating admissions of defendant provided the necessary corroboration. Further, the court found that defendant's double jeopardy rights were not violated because it was well settled that the conspiracy was a distinct offense from the actual offense forming the object of the conspiracy and that she could legally be convicted of both offenses. Accordingly, the convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of conspiracy to commit an abortion and committing an abortion, was affirmed. The order of the same court, which denied her motion for a new trial, was also affirmed.

 

1575 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. Vic Tanny Compton, Inc.


Civ. No. 24111


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


182 Cal. App. 2d 506; 6 Cal. Rptr. 490; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2138; 87 A.L.R.2d 113



July 7, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Jerold E. Weil, Judge.

Action for damages arising from failure to furnish a course in physical education to plaintiff in defendant's gymnasium in alleged violation of Civ. Code, §§ 51, 52.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment adverse to plaintiff, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minority applicant appealed an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that entered judgment in favor of defendant gymnasium owner in an action for damages that allegedly arose from the gymnasium owner's refusal to furnish a physical education course to the minority applicant in violation of Cal. Civ. Code §§ 51, 52 (1956).


OVERVIEW: The gymnasium owner declined to allow the minority applicant to take a course in physical education at the gymnasium solely on account of his race and color. The minority applicant sued the gymnasium owner for damages based on violations of Cal. Civ. Code §§ 51, 52 (1956). The trial court found that the gymnasium was open to engagement by some and not all members of the general public, that the gymnasium owner did not furnish courses of education to all members of the general public, and § 51 and § 52 were not applicable because the gymnasium was not a place of public amusement or public accommodation at the time the minority applicant was denied admission. Judgment was entered in favor of the gymnasium owner, and the minority applicant appealed. In affirming the trial court's judgement, the court held that § 51 and § 52 were applicable to places of public accommodation and amusement and the gymnasium did not fall into these categories. Comparing the gymnasium to a private school, the court found that it was not open to the public in general, and that the gymnasium owner could limit its membership by excluding those persons management saw proper to exclude.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that was entered in favor of the gymnasium owner in a discrimination action brought by the minority applicant.

 

1576 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


MacLeod v. Los Altos


Civ. No. 18661


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


182 Cal. App. 2d 364; 6 Cal. Rptr. 326; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2117



July 1, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Edwin J. Owens, Judge.

Action to enjoin a city and certain of its officials from applying or enforcing an ordinance against plaintiffs.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city and its officials (city) sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which entered judgment in favor of appellee voluntary association officers (officers) and enjoined the city from applying or enforcing, or attempting to apply or enforce, a soliciting ordinance against the officers.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance allowed the distribution of literature or the visiting of homes for the purposes of political persuasion but did not allow any solicitation of funds. The officers worked for a voluntary organization affiliated with the Democratic Party. The trial court held that the ordinance did not apply to the officers and that if it did apply, it was unconstitutional. The court agreed that the ordinance did not apply to the officers and affirmed the verdict. The purpose of the ordinance was to have regulated the practice of door-to-door solicitation of business for the purpose of soliciting orders for the sale of goods, ware, and merchandise and of disposing of or peddling or hawking the same. Therefore, the ordinance was not applicable to the activity to have been engaged in by the officers. Because the ordinance did not apply to the officers then the officers were not required to have sought any administrative remedy and the injunction was properly issued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that enjoined the city from enforcing the ordinance against the officers.

 

1577 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Biber Electric Co. v. San Carlos


Civ. No. 19011


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


181 Cal. App. 2d 342; 5 Cal. Rptr. 261; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2004



May 26, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 24, 1960, and the Petition of Appellant City of San Carlos for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 20, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Arthur L. Mundo, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for declaratory relief and to enjoin enforcement of a city ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment declaring ordinance invalid, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Sam Mateo County (California), which in plaintiff electrical contractor's action for declaratory relief and to enjoin enforcement of a city ordnance entered judgment that invalidated San Carlos, California, Ordinance § 4038 on the basis that § 4038 attempted to impose additional requirements in fields that were preempted by the State.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted San Carlos, California, Ordinance § 4038 that required any party subject to business licensing within the city to display a certain emblem on their commercial vehicles. The electrical contractor brought an action for a declaratory relief and to enjoin the city from enforcing § 4038. The trial court entered judgment that declaring that the ordinance was unconstitutional on the basis that it attempted to impose additional requirements in fields that were preempted by the State. The city sought review of the trial court's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's ruling, holding that the § 4038 did not purport to impose a business license fee as claimed by the city but envisioned the use of city streets by commercial vehicles and regarded licensure of vehicles, a matter that was within the purview of Cal. Veh. Code §§ 9250, et seq. (1959). The court also found that the Legislature's enactment of Cal. Veh. Code § 21 (1959) clearly indicated the intent that the State retain exclusive authority over matters in the California Vehicle Code unless express power was otherwise granted to municipalities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that had declared the city ordinance to be invalid.

 

1578 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Farrant


Crim. No. 3781


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


181 Cal. App. 2d 231; 5 Cal. Rptr. 171; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 1988



May 24, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in habeas corpus to secure release from custody.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a habeas corpus action to secure his release from custody, petitioner alleged that respondent county sheriff (California) unlawfully restrained him by a criminal complaint issued by the Municipal Court of the Concord Judicial District (California) charging him with violating Contra Costa, Cal., Ordinance 142, alleging that petitioner unlawfully played and carried on a game played with dice for money within the county.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the ordinance unconstitutionally conflicted in jurisdiction with Cal. Penal Code § 330. Cal. Const. art. XI, § 11 provided that a county could make and enforce any ordinance that did not conflict with general laws. The preemption test was whether the concrete provisions of the state law occupied a particular field, or only part of it, and left the local regulations an implied freedom to supplement. Local government was commonly accepted to operate in the field of gambling. In denying the writ, the court relied heavily on a state gambling case in which a city ordinance that closely paralleled the Contra Costa County ordinance conflicted with the state penal code. That petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied because that petitioner failed to show that the game he was charged with playing was the proscribed percentage game of the state statute. The court likewise rejected petitioner's argument that the games with dice appeared in both state and local enactment and held that he did not establish that his dice game was a preempted percentage game. The county's ordinance excluded the state-prohibited gambling and was not vague and uncertain.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request for a writ.

 

1579 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Duke Molner Wholesale Liquor Co. v. Martin


Civ. No. 23768


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


180 Cal. App. 2d 873; 4 Cal. Rptr. 904; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2413



May 16, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied June 1, 1960, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 12, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Ellsworth Meyer, Judge.

Action by wholesale liquor licensees to have a rule of the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control declared unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment upholding validity of rule, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wholesale liquor licensees challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which, in appellants' action against respondent California Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, held that rule 28 of the California Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control, codified at Cal. Code Regs. tit. 4, §§ 1 - 145 (1957), was proper and constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The licensees were four persons engaged in and licensed to engage in the wholesale liquor business in California. They generally obtained their bourbon whiskey from distillers in Kentucky, their gin and vodka from Boston, and some items of distilled spirits from California. The shipments from the east required two weeks or more before delivery in California. After the Department adopted rule 28, the licensees instituted their action, claiming that rule 28, which set forth requirements as to the licensees' warehouse space and stock, was unconstitutional. The court held that rule 28 was valid, noting that Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 23778 provided that the licensees were not entitled to licenses unless they kept a reasonable stock of distilled spirits as determined by the Department. The court further held that the Department, under rule 28, codified at Cal. Code Regs. tit. 4, §§ 1-145 (1957), set forth the requirements to prescribe the maintenance of a reasonable stock on hand as a prerequisite to holding such a license. The court held that the Department was well within its rights to require a high standard of economic stability for those who were to hold wholesaler's licenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1580 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


McMurtry v. State Board of Medical Examiners


Civ. No. 6042


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


180 Cal. App. 2d 760; 4 Cal. Rptr. 910; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2396



May 9, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 27, 1960, and Respondent's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied July 6, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Strother P. Walton, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel reversal of an order revoking a certificate to practice medicine.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions. Judgment denying writ, reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which denied the physician's request for a writ of mandamus to compel reversal of respondent board of medical examiners' (board) order revoking the physician's certificate to practice medicine.


OVERVIEW: The board revoked the physician's certificate after determining that the physician failed to report certain named habitual users of narcotics as required by Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11425 and failing to keep records of the dispensation of narcotics as required by § 11255. The court reversed the judgment and directed the trial court to enter a judgment commanding the board to set aside its order and to reconsider the case in light of the court's opinion. The court concluded that the findings of the board did not support the charge of unprofessional conduct based on a violation of § 11425. The board determined that the physician was guilty of unprofessional conduct in failing to make the report required by § 11425 respecting his patients who, the board found, were habitual users of narcotics but not addicts. The court held that the term "habitual users" lacked the certainty of standard required of a regulatory statute and gave the physician no reasonable standard for compliance. Because the board based its decision on an alleged violation of the unconstitutional phrase of § 11425, the decision was not supported by the findings and, thus, constituted an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied the writ of mandamus. The court directed the trial court to enter a judgment commanding the board to set aside its order of revocation and directing the board to reconsider the case and thereafter make such order as it deemed proper in the light of the court's opinion and judgment.

 

1581 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Banville v. County of Los Angeles


Civ. No. 24294


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


180 Cal. App. 2d 563; 4 Cal. Rptr. 458; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2371



May 2, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 24, 1960, and Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 29, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Evelle J. Younger, Judge.

Action for declaration of rights and duties of parties with respect to usage of property under a county zoning ordinance.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment adverse to plaintiffs after demurrer to fourth amended complaint was sustained with leave to amend, and plaintiffs failed to amend complaint, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff landowners' action against defendants county and officials challenging a zoning ordinance, the landowners appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), sustaining the county's demurrer to the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The landowners alleged that they had been deprived of the highest and best usage of their property, and that the county's actions constituted the taking of property without due process of law. The court considered the question of whether the right to apply for an exception under the zoning ordinance was an administrative remedy which had to be exhausted prior to an attack upon the constitutionality of the ordinance as applied to it. The court held that the landowners had not exhausted their administrative remedies. The landowners requested an amendment to the zoning ordinance to change the zone of their particular property, but a change of zone was a legislative, not an administrative remedy. The court held that the landowners would not have a cause of action until they made an application for an exception and unreasonable restrictions or conditions were imposed. The court further held that the fact that the landowners experienced some hardship or that it may have been more profitable to make other use of the property was not controlling in determining whether the regulations were arbitrary or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the county's demurrer to the landowners' challenge to the rezoning.

 

1582 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hunter v. Adams


Civ. No. 18827


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


180 Cal. App. 2d 511; 4 Cal. Rptr. 776; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2365



April 29, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 22, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Monterey County. Stanley Lawson, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel a city council and others to invalidate a resolution freezing building permits in a proposed redevelopment project area.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owner and purchaser, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Monterey County (California), which was in favor of respondents, city council and related parties. The judgment discharged an alternative writ of mandamus and denied a petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus in the action challenging a resolution forbidding the issuance of building permits in an area of community redevelopment.


OVERVIEW: The property owner and purchaser filed an action against the city council challenging a resolution that forbade the issuance of building permits for one year in an area of community redevelopment. The trial court denied the request for a writ of mandamus, and the court affirmed the decision. The court held that the city council's resolution that froze building permits was a proper exercise of police power. The court held that the resolution was not in conflict with Cal. Health & Safety Code § 33749 or with Cal. Health & Safety Code § 33574, which had been repealed. The court found that the only duty imposed upon the local community by both of those sections was that the applicant for a permit "be advised." The court held that the mere fact that the state, in the exercise of its police power, had made certain regulations, did not prohibit the municipality from exacting additional requirements, so long as there was no conflict between the two and such requirements were not unreasonable. The court found it difficult to conceive how an intelligent integrated redevelopment plan could be formulated if, during planning, the area was in a constant state of flux with new construction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the city council. The judgment discharged an alternative writ of mandamus and denied a petition for a peremptory writ of mandamus in the action brought by the property owner and purchaser challenging a resolution forbidding the issuance of building permits in an area of redevelopment.

 

1583 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Beamon v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 23968


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


180 Cal. App. 2d 200; 4 Cal. Rptr. 396; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2330



April 21, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Ellsworth Meyer, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the Department of Motor Vehicles to set aside and expunge from its records its order revoking petitioner's motor vehicle operator's license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner licensee challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied his petition for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent Department of Motor Vehicles (DMV) to set aside and expunge from its records its order revoking the licensee's motor vehicle operator's license.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing, the DMV determined that the licensee was a negligent operator and revoked his motor vehicle operator's license. The licensee sought mandamus in the trial court to set aside and expunge the revocation. The trial court denied the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed. The legislature, by empowering officers of the DMV to determine whether an operator's license should be revoked, did not confer judicial power upon executive officers. The authority was a lawful delegation of legislative power. The legislation was not a delegation of absolute legislative discretion, but provided DMV a complete and comprehensive guide for its action. The licensee was not denied due process. At the conclusion of its investigation, the DMV gave notice to the licensee that it was considering revoking his operator's license and of his right to a hearing. He failed to request a formal hearing, but appeared and testified at an informal hearing. Due process was satisfied. The fact that the licensee might suffer inconvenience or economic loss because he was denied a license as a result of his driving record did not make the remedial action of the DMV the imposition of punishment for past offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the licensee's petition for a writ of mandamus to set aside and expunge the revocation of his motor vehicle operator's license.

 

1584 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Terry


Crim. No. 6815


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


180 Cal. App. 2d 48; 4 Cal. Rptr. 597; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2312



April 19, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied May 9, 1960, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 14, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County and from orders denying a new trial and probation. Mark Brandler, Judge.

Prosecution for lewd conduct with children and the crime against nature.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeals from orders dismissed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) convicting him of lewd conduct with children and the crime against nature, and from an order denying his motion for a new trial and for probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with lewd conduct with children and with committing crimes against nature. Defendant requested probation, but the request was denied. Defendant was convicted on all charges, and filed a motion for a new trial that was denied. Defendant challenged the decisions of the trial court first contending that he was unconstitutionally deprived of the right to confront his accusers face to face and cross-examine them, and that due process of law was thereby denied him. The court noted that the deposition testimony was taken before a magistrate with defendant's presence, which offered an opportunity for cross-examination. Thus the court concluded that it did not appear that defendant's constitutional rights were infringed. Defendant then argued that prejudicial error was committed by taking foundation evidence in the presence of the jury. The court noted that defendant was unable to point out the particular evidentiary matters that resulted in prejudice to his case. Therefore, his failure to comply with this requirement rendered his argument meritless. Defendant's remaining contentions were equally without merit, and his conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1585 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Muller v. Muller


Civ. No. 19074


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


179 Cal. App. 2d 815; 4 Cal. Rptr. 419; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2301



April 18, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County. Wayne R. Millington, Judge.

Action for cancellation of a forged deed and for other equitable relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of dismissal affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for cancellation of a forged deed and for other equitable relief, appellant land claimant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which granted the motion to dismiss filed by appellees, the holder of the deed and another person.


OVERVIEW: The claimant brought an action alleging that the deed was forged. Appellees contended that the holder was the legal and equitable owner and that a prior judgment had quieted title in the holder. After the cause was set for trial, appellees moved to abate the action until after the decision on the pending appeal from the prior judgment. The motion was granted. When the claimant next filed a memorandum to set the cause for trial, appellees filed a motion to dismiss based on Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 583, which required that the cause be brought to trial within five years. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the period of the stay was excluded in computing the five-year period. However, at most the stay would have continued until the denial of the claimant's petition for a hearing on the prior judgment quieting title. Even excluding that period, the claimant's rights had expired under the five-year rule. Also, the period was not extended for holidays.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the case.

 

1586 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Crocker-Anglo Nat'l Bank v. Franchise Tax Board


Civ. No. 18363


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


179 Cal. App. 2d 591; 3 Cal. Rptr. 906; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2270



April 11, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. William T. Sweigert, Judge.

Action to obtain a refund of personal income taxes paid under protest.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for defendant affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied a refund of personal income taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, California residents, owned stock in a Canadian corporation that did no business in California. The corporation withheld Canadian taxes from dividend payments. For several years, the taxpayers, in filing their California tax returns, reported the gross amount of the dividends and claimed the Canadian taxes as deductions from gross income. Thereafter, the taxpayers sought to obtain California tax refunds on the ground that they were entitled to the credit provided by Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 18001(a) for foreign net income tax payments. The court affirmed the denial of the refunds, finding that the Canadian taxes, which were imposed on the gross income from the dividends, did not constitute net income taxes. Consequently, the Canadian taxes did not qualify as allowable credits under § 18001. The court further held that the legislative policy of permitting credit only for taxes similar to the California tax did not deprive the taxpayers of the equal protection of the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of personal income tax refunds.

 

1587 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Department of Public Works v. Los Angeles


Civ. No. 24314


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


179 Cal. App. 2d 558; 4 Cal. Rptr. 531; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2267



April 8, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied June 2, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Kurtz Kauffman, Judge.

Proceeding to condemn realty for highway purposes.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiff affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant heir sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a judgment in a condemnation action in favor of plaintiff California Department of Public Works (department) and denied the heir compensation.


OVERVIEW: The department filed an action against defendants, city, heir, and others, to condemn their interests in certain lands that were known as a park for the construction of a state highway. The trial court granted a judgment in favor of the department and denied the heir compensation. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that the state could acquire property that was already dedicated by a municipality as a park pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 102 and Cal. Sts. & High. Code §§ 102 and 103.5 where the land was condemned by the state for the more necessary public use as a state highway. The court concluded that the State Highway Commission was properly delegated the power to establish and maintain a state highway system because the commission fulfilled a statewide purpose, not a local one, and its authority and functions were not per se an interference with municipal affairs. The court determined that the heir was not entitled to compensation where the heir's reversionary interest terminated upon the condemnation and his interest became remote and speculative because at the moment of the condemnation there was had been no misuse by the city of the land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an judgment that was entered in favor of the department.

 

1588 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


City Council of Santa Barbara v. Superior Court of Santa Barbara County


Civ. No. 24503


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Two


179 Cal. App. 2d 389; 3 Cal. Rptr. 796; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2246



April 1, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County from further action in a mandamus proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city council requested a writ of prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California) from further action in a mandamus action brought by real party in interest, a refuse company, that sought a judgment that commanded the city council to grant higher rates for residential garbage collection service under an existing contract for the collection and disposal of refuse and rubble within the city.


OVERVIEW: The refuse company requested an increase in rates for the collection of residential refuse from the city council, under the terms of the existing contract between them. After meetings and consideration of the request, the city council refused to increase the rates. The refuse company filed a mandamus action in the superior court. The superior court denied the city council's demurrer to the petition and issued an alternative writ of mandate directed to the city and the members of the city council that commanded them to grant an increase in residential rates or to show cause why they had not done so. The city council filed a petition for a writ of prohibition. The court granted the petition because the refusal to increase rates was a decision that required exercise of judgment, and discretion. The court had no authority to exercise jurisdiction over a legislative act and could not constitutionally compel the city council to enact legislation.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city council's petition for a writ of prohibition that prevented the superior court from taking injunctive action that compelled legislative action by the city council.

 

1589 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Blake


Crim. No. 3627


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


179 Cal. App. 2d 246; 3 Cal. Rptr. 749; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2225



March 28, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. John B. Molinari, Judge.

Prosecution for illegally offering to sell marijuana.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which found him guilty of two counts of violating Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11500, unlawfully offering to sell marijuana.


OVERVIEW: An undercover police officer was introduced to defendant, who asked him if he had the man with $ 5,000 with him. Defendant attempted to work with the police officer on a transaction involving the sale of marijuana. The parties discussed the profit and price per pound. Over one month later, the police officer and another policeman went to defendant's apartment to arrest him. There, they found a scale in defendant's kitchen but no marijuana other than one seed in defendant's car truck. Defendant was indicted with two counts of violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11500 of the Health and Safety Code: (1) unlawfully offering to sell marijuana; (2) the unlawful possession of marijuana. A jury found defendant guilty only of the first count. Defendant appealed and the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court's instruction to the jury was proper and did not violate Cal. Penal Code § 20, which provided that in every crime there must have existed a union of act and intent. The court found that the trial court had carefully delineated the difference between the requisite intent, the act required, and a mere attempt or incomplete offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court.

 

1590 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Gowens v. Bakersfield


Civ. No. 6054


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


179 Cal. App. 2d 282; 3 Cal. Rptr. 746; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2230



March 28, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. John P. McMurray, Judge. *


* Assigned by Chairman of Judicial Council.

Action for a judgment declaring a municipal ordinance unconstitutional and for injunctive relief against its enforcement.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Judgment of dismissal entered after defendants' demurrer to complaint was sustained, reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hotel owner appealed a judgment of dismissal from the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which sustained defendant city's demurrer to the hotel owner's action for a judgment declaring a tax ordinance unconstitutional and for injunctive relief against its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The challenged ordinance required hotel owners to collect from transients a tax upon the compensation paid for lodging rentals. All persons obtaining lodging in establishments containing less than five accommodations were completely exempt from the tax. The court held that the hotel owner had standing to maintain the action because of the inconvenience of collecting the tax and because of the probable loss of business to nearby communities that imposed no similar tax. The court further concluded that there was no reasonable distinction for tax purposes, from the viewpoint of a lodger, between a large establishment capable of accommodating many people and a small one accommodating a lesser number. Accordingly, the ordinance violated the constitutional requirement of uniformity of intended application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of dismissal.

 

1591 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Munro


Civ. No. 18479


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


178 Cal. App. 2d 67; 2 Cal. Rptr. 737; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2561



February 17, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from judgments of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Raymond J. Arata, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief and for an injunction.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgments for defendants affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs retail liquor dealers (dealers) sought review of the summary judgments by the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California) in favor of defendant, the Department of Alcoholic Beverage Control (department), in the dealers' action for declaratory relief and injunction after the dealers were charged with violating the fair trade provisions of the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 24750 et seq.


OVERVIEW: In granting the department's motion for summary judgment, the court held that the dealers were engaged in administrative action before the department in which the constitutionality of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §§ 24750 to 24757 and department rules were raised and that it was more expeditious and proper that the department rule on the questions before the trial court ruled on the issues. The court affirmed, finding that the dealers failed to exhaust their administrative remedies first as the trial court's jurisdiction for judicial relief was conditioned upon a completion of the administrative procedure. The court further found that the constitutionality of §§ 24750 to 24757 may have been determined in the first instance in the pending administrative proceedings and that it was clear that the trial court did not abuse its discretion granted by Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1061. The court found that since the initiating of the proceedings the constitutionality of the provisions in question were determined to have been constitutional and the issues were moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the department in the dealer's action for declaratory and injunctive relief.

 

1592 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Los Angeles City School Dist. v. Landier Inv. Co.


Civ. No. 24037


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division One


177 Cal. App. 2d 744; 2 Cal. Rptr. 662; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2541



February 9, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants' Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied April 6, 1960. Schauer, J., Spence, J., and Peters, J., were of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Clyde C. Triplett, Judge.

Action for declaratory relief.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment for plaintiffs affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district entered into a settlement agreement with defendant management company under which the management company would repay a sum already paid out by the school district on a contract with the company that was void ab initio. The Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) denied the company's motion for relief from a stipulation in the settlement. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The school district entered into a settlement agreement with the management company under which the management company would repay a sum already paid out by the school district on a contract with the company that was void ab initio. The trial court denied the company's motion for relief from a stipulation in the settlement that in the event of default, judgment would be entered for twice the balance due. The court held (1) the denial of the motion was proper, (2) ordinarily, a party could be relieved from a stipulation only upon timely application to the court wherein it was made, notice thereof first being given to the opposing party, (3) from the standpoint of laches, whether a party acted with promptness was a question of fact and depended on the circumstances of the case, (4) as in other situations where a party sought relief from the consequences of his own act, the discretion of the trial court was broad and unless abused would not warrant appellate interference.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the company's motion for relief from the stipulation in the settlement with the school district.

 

1593 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ragsdale


Crim. No. 3630


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division Two


177 Cal. App. 2d 676; 2 Cal. Rptr. 640; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2532



February 8, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County. Jordan L. Martinelli, Judge.

Prosecution for sex perversion.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which, following a guilty verdict by 11 jurors, convicted defendant and his codefendant of oral sexual copulation, a violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288a.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his codefendant were inmates in a state prison when they were observed engaging in oral sexual copulation. They were placed in solitary confinement as discipline for the offense under the prison's regulations. Following their indictment, they were tried before a jury. After the close of evidence but before the verdict, one juror was excused due to illness. The parties stipulated to permit the case to be decided by the remaining 11 jurors, who returned a guilty verdict. The trial court convicted defendant and his codefendant. Defendant appealed. Because no objection was made at trial, defendant had failed to preserve his speedy trial challenge. However, under Cal. Const. art. I, § 13, defendant was not an accused party until he was indicted. The solitary confinement was not an arrest under Cal. Penal Code § 834. Defendant's speedy trial rights were governed by Cal. Penal Code § 1381. Binding precedent allowed defendant to consent to trial by less than 12 jurors. Defendant's attack on Cal. Penal Code § 288a as applied to prisoners presumed without authority an intent to encourage procreation. The criminality of unnatural sexual relations was embedded in common law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1594 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Department of Motor Vehicles


Civ. No. 6287


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


177 Cal. App. 2d 440; 2 Cal. Rptr. 235; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2492



January 26, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 23, 1960. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. John Shea, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to review action of Department of Motor Vehicles in suspending an operator's license.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which denied a writ of mandate after respondent California Department of Motor Vehicles (department) suspended the citizen's driver's license.


OVERVIEW: At a hearing, the department determined that the citizen was a negligent operator of a motor vehicle. The department required the citizen to surrender his driver's license. The trial court denied the citizen's writ of mandate. On appeal, the citizen contended that he should not be penalized by reason of a traffic offense where he had not admitted his guilt or been found guilty. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that: (1) the trial court found that there was a full, complete, and fair hearing and that the action of the department was supported by substantial evidence; (2) the findings of the trial court were amply supported by the record; (3) the posting of bail on a traffic ticket and the forfeiture of such bail could properly be considered an admission of guilt; (4) the legislature had properly placed within the department the discretion of determining which persons were qualified to receive driver's licenses and of determining which licenses should be revoked.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the citizen's writ of mandate after the department suspended his driver's license.

 

1595 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


In re Covina Argus-Citizen


Civ. No. 23825


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


177 Cal. App. 2d 315; 2 Cal. Rptr. 184; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2472



January 22, 1960 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. A. Curtis Smith, Judge.

Proceedings to have the standing of a newspaper as a newspaper of general circulation ascertained and established.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment modifying prior judgment with respect to status of such newspaper, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper publisher sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a judgment for respondent competitor and modified a prior judgment that had adjudicated the publisher's newspaper to be a newspaper of general circulation within a city and determined that it was presently a newspaper of general circulation within a county.


OVERVIEW: In 1952, the publisher's newspaper was adjudged to be a newspaper of general circulation for the city, county, and State of California. Thereafter, the competitor filed a motion to have the adjudication vacated, pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 6024, on the grounds that the publisher's newspaper was no longer printed and published in the city. The publisher conceded that its printing was not done in city, but asserted that the substantial business affairs of its newspaper were conducted there. The trial court modified the 1952 decree and found that the publisher's newspaper was a newspaper of general circulation for the county and state. The court held that the use of the word "may" in § 6024 did not give a superior court the discretion to determine whether a subsequent substantial departure from Cal. Gov't Code § 6000 should be disregarded. Further, in order to qualify as a "newspaper of general circulation," the newspaper had to be printed and published in the same city. Finally, Cal. Gov't Code § 6024 was constitutional as applied to the publisher because it was not unreasonable to expect that local citizens would rely on such newspapers for matters of local public importance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1596 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


People v. Zucker


Crim. No. 6350


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


177 Cal. App. 2d 172; 2 Cal. Rptr. 112; 1960 Cal. App. LEXIS 2443



January 14, 1960 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied February 8, 1960, and Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied March 14, 1960. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, from an order denying a new trial, from the verdict, and from denial of petitions for dismissal, for court orders and for a writ of mandate. Clement D. Nye, Judge.

Prosecution for grand theft.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order denying new trial affirmed; other appeals dismissed. Judgment of conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of grand theft, denied his motion for a new trial, denied his petitions for dismissal, denied his petitions for court orders, and denied his petition for a writ of mandate. Defendant argued that Cal. Penal Code § 952 (1929) was unconstitutional and that he was denied his constitutional right to counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was engaged in the mortgage and finance business using different names. Defendant induced the landowners, a husband and wife with limited education, to buy a truck and 10 acres of unimproved property in exchange for the landowners' two rental houses. In reliance on defendant, the landowners signed papers and made payments. When the truck was repossessed and the landowners discovered that the documents did not memorialize the oral agreement, defendant was charged with crimes and was convicted of grand theft. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. Section 952 was not unconstitutional, and the information sufficiently alleged that defendant unlawfully took the labor or property of another. Defendant's activities were part of a single scheme to appropriate the property of the landowners. The evidence warranted a conviction for theft based upon any one of three distinct acts of embezzlement committed by defendant. At most, the information merely contained an erroneous description of the stolen property, and the variance was harmless. Defendant was not deprived of his right to counsel, and his motion for a new trial lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and the order denying a new trial, and it dismissed defendant's other appeals.

 

1597 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Garden Grove Congregation of Jehovah's Witnesses v. Garden Grove


Civ. No. 5981


Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District


176 Cal. App. 2d 136; 1 Cal. Rptr. 65; 1959 Cal. App. LEXIS 1457



December 11, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied February 3, 1960. Peters, J., was of the Opinion that the Petition Should be Granted.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Ronald M. Crookshank, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the issuance of a conditional use permit.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which denied its application for a writ of mandate to compel respondent city to issue a conditional use permit so that it could build a church in a residentially zoned neighborhood.


OVERVIEW: After the planning commission denied the corporation's application for a conditional use permit, the corporation appealed to the city council which also denied the application. The corporation applied for a writ of mandate but the trial court denied it. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the city had exercised its discretion, so had exclusive jurisdiction to determine the application for a conditional use permit and therefore could not be controlled by a writ of mandate. The court reviewed the caselaw and found that it was proper for cities to regulate the use of property, including church uses, by zoning ordinances. The court found that the corporation could not both apply for relief under the ordinance and challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance in a mandamus proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the corporation's application for a writ of mandate to compel the city to issue a conditional use permit.

 

1598 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Hersch v. Boston Ins. Co.


Civ. No. 18336


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


175 Cal. App. 2d 751; 346 P.2d 796; 1959 Cal. App. LEXIS 1407



December 3, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Petition for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied January 27, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco granting a judgment creditor lien upon the judgment debtor's cause of action against an insurance company. Milton D. Sapiro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment debtor sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which granted respondent judgment creditor a lien pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 688.1 upon the judgment debtor's cause of action against defendant insurance company.


OVERVIEW: The judgment creditor obtained a judgment against the judgment debtor. While that judgment remained unsatisfied, the judgment debtor instituted an unrelated action against the insurance company. The judgment creditor filed a motion pursuant to § 688.1 to have a lien placed upon the judgment debtor's cause of action against the insurance company. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the judgment creditor argued that the trial court's decision to grant the motion was not appealable, and the judgment debtor argued that § 688.1 violated his freedom to contract because it required that the judgment debtor obtain the approval of the judgment creditor before entering into a settlement. The court affirmed the trial court's decision and found that the order granting the lien was a final decision on a collateral matter and was therefore appealable. The court also found that § 688.1 was not unconstitutional because the restrictions imposed were a reasonable safeguard to a fraudulent or collusive settlement of the action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to grant the judgment creditor a lien on the judgment debtor's cause of action against the insurance company.

 

1599 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Superior Court of Marin County


Civ. No. 18759


Court of Appeal of California, First Appellate District, Division One


175 Cal. App. 2d 8; 345 P.2d 513; 1959 Cal. App. LEXIS 1289



October 30, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] A Petition for a Rehearing was Denied November 25, 1959, and the Petition of the Real Party in Interest for a Hearing by the Supreme Court was Denied December 23, 1959.


PRIOR HISTORY: PROCEEDING in prohibition to restrain the Superior Court of Marin County from proceeding further upon an indictment.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney sought a writ of prohibition to restrain respondent Superior Court of Marin County (California) from proceeding on an indictment returned against the attorney for conspiracy to pervert and obstruct justice and the due administration of the law and to cheat real party in interest State of California of property by violating Cal. Penal Code § 4570 in taking a manuscript out a prison without the warden's permission.


OVERVIEW: A prison warden prohibited an inmate from writing manuscripts for publication. The inmate violated the order and wrote a book. The attorney, who represented the inmate, received the manuscript in the mail. The book was eventually published. The attorney was indicted, along with the book's publisher and the inmate's literary agent, for conspiracy under Cal. Penal Code § 182 for violating Cal. Penal Code § 4570, which delegated authority to the warden to refuse communication with a prisoner. The attorney filed a motion to dismiss the indictment. The superior court denied the motion. The attorney filed a petition for a writ of prohibition, requesting that the superior court be restrained from proceeding on the indictment. The court issued the writ and found that the indictment, which was based on the theory that the state acquired an automatic ownership in an inmate's creativity, was not supported in the law. Although the court held that the indictment supported the limited conspiratorial purpose of taking a manuscript from the prison without permission, the attorney's possession of the manuscript did not in itself supply evidence that he took the manuscript from the prison.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of prohibition in the action against the attorney for conspiracy.

 

1600 of 2002 DOCUMENTS


Brodsky v. California State Board of Pharmacy


Civ. No. 23634


Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three


173 Cal. App. 2d 680; 344 P.2d 68; 1959 Cal. App. LEXIS 1642



September 15, 1959 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Bayard Rhone, Judge.

Proceeding in mandamus to compel the State Board of Pharmacy to annul its order suspending petitioner's license to practice as a licentiate in pharmacy for 30 days.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Judgment denying writ, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pharmacist sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that denied the pharmacist's petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondent California State Board of Pharmacy (board) to annul its order suspending the pharmacist's license to practice for 30 days and placing him on probation for one year.


OVERVIEW: A board investigator was able to fill a prescription at the pharmacy in the absence of the pharmacist. The pharmacist was then charged with permitting a person who was not a registered pharmacist to compound and sell a prescription in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 4385, and neglecting to place a registered pharmacist in charge of the pharmacy during his absence in violation of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 4386. The board suspended the pharmacist's license with a stay and probation. On appeal from the denial of his petition for a writ of mandate to compel the board to annul its decision, the pharmacist argued that the board's findings could not support its conclusion that he had permitted the selling of drugs by an unregistered pharmacist when he had specifically instructed his employee not to make such sales. The court affirmed the denial of the pharmacist's petition for a writ of mandate, and held that the board's findings were supported by substantial evidence. The court found that the legislature differentiated between knowingly permitting an act and merely permitting it, and that when the legislature intended that an act must be knowingly permitted, it had so stated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the pharmacist's petition for a writ of mandate.
